**D107 — 13-NODE LADDER: GEN2 REMAINS THE STRONGEST CHECKPOINT EVER PRODUCED -- nothing in gen3/gen4/league1-4/exploiter1-3 has surpassed it. Ladder extended to 13 anchors (70 pairings, anchor=gen1=0 Elo since bc_v4 is degenerate). Ranking: gen2 +100.3 > gen3 +94.2 > league1 +78.8 > gen4 +62.9 > league4 +60.7 > exploiter1 +56.8 > league2 +45.9 > exploiter3 +20.8 > gen1 0.0 > exploiter2 -32.9 > kickoff8 -112.8 > v5contested -333.9 > bc_v4 -1548.1 (bc_v4 still 0% decisive vs everything, extreme outlier).

ANSWERS to the pre-registered questions: (a) exploiter1 (+56.8) is BELOW the {gen2,gen3,league1} cluster (+78.8 to +100.3) by 22-43.5 Elo -- despite exploiter1 beating a FROZEN gen2 ~59% in its own specialized training run (D102), in the GENERAL ladder (playing everyone, not just gen2) exploiter1 is weaker than gen2 itself. Specialist-vs-generalist: cracking a frozen target's specific weakness did not produce a generally stronger player. (b) league4 (+60.7) is BELOW league1 (+78.8) -- the league lineage's OWN 4-generation progression is NON-MONOTONIC: league1 +78.8 > league4 +60.7 > league2 +45.9 (league3 not separately measured). Three more 30B generations after league1 have NOT exceeded it. D96's "league Elo never plateaued" referred to an internal per-run tracker that resets on relaunch (D102-B) and is NOT comparable across runs -- the cross-anchor ladder tells a more sobering story. (c) exploiter2 (-32.9) and exploiter3 (+20.8) both land BELOW exploiter1 (+56.8), consistent with "exploiter1 robust" -- but exploiter2 is even below gen1, the WEAKEST of all measured contested-era checkpoints except kickoff8/v5contested/bc_v4.

RESIDUAL/NON-TRANSITIVITY FINDINGS (largest |fit_p - empirical_p|): exploiter2 vs league4 (fit 0.368, empirical 0.552, |err| 0.184) -- exploiter2 (Elo -32.9, near-bottom) BEATS league4 (Elo +60.7) head-to-head despite a ~94-Elo gap in the "wrong" direction. gen2 vs league4 (fit 0.557, empirical 0.471, |err| 0.085) -- league4 BEATS gen2 (the #1 ranked checkpoint) head-to-head 52.9% of the time despite a 39.6-Elo gap. league4 has a striking rock-paper-scissors profile: beats the #1 checkpoint (gen2) but loses to one of the weakest (exploiter2). exploiter2 vs exploiter3 (fit 0.423, empirical 0.649) -- same-direction but underpredicted-margin.

THIS IS A PROGRAM-LEVEL FINDING flagged for codex review before further conclusions (per CLAUDE.md: conclusions-from-data get reviewed before acting) -- dispatching .codex-reviews/d107-gen2-dominance.md. Possible interpretations to be adjudicated: (1) gen2 was a genuinely strong/lucky checkpoint and everything since has been lateral-or-regressive (overfitting to recent self-play distributions / catastrophic forgetting of general play); (2) the BT/Elo linear-strength model is a poor fit for a landscape with real rock-paper-scissors structure (league4-vs-gen2-vs-exploiter2 triangle) and "strongest" isn't well-defined without specifying the opponent pool; (3) measurement noise at the per-pairing level (D98's ~95-Elo single-tournament-variance finding) means some of these orderings could shift with more games. League-5 (warm=league4, pool includes exploiter1+gen2 as banks) and exploiter-4 (champion=league4, testing its exploitability) continue running -- both remain informative regardless of this verdict.**
**D107-A — CLAUDE ADVERSARIAL REVIEW of D107 (codex's first attempt produced 1600+ lines of file-exploration with no synthesized verdict -- retrying with a tighter prompt as secondary opinion, .codex-reviews/d107-gen2-dominance-v2.md). Re-examining the raw Elo gaps with noise in mind:

(1) GEN2-VS-GEN3 GAP IS NOISE (6.1 Elo: 100.3 vs 94.2) -- the D107 framing "gen2 is uniquely #1" OVERSTATES this. gen2 and gen3 form a TOP TIER, indistinguishable from each other. The REAL signal is the gap from this top tier DOWN to league1 (78.8, -15 to -21.5 Elo) and further to gen4/league4/exploiter1 (57-63, -31 to -37 Elo from top tier) -- these gaps are larger than a typical multi-pairing BT standard error (~12 pairings x ~1000-2000 games/node = ~12-15K decisive games informing each node's Elo) and likely reflect SOME real signal, though D98's single-pairing ~95-Elo variance means individual large gaps still warrant caution. REVISED leaderboard structure: TIER1 {gen2, gen3} ~94-100 > TIER2 {league1} ~79 > TIER3 {gen4, league4, exploiter1} ~57-63 > TIER4 {league2, exploiter3} ~21-46 > gen1 (0, baseline) > TIER5 {exploiter2, kickoff8, v5contested, bc_v4} all negative. This RECOVERS D98's original "{gen2,gen3,league1} cluster" finding -- the cluster has partially resolved (league1 separated downward) but TIER1 (gen2/gen3) staying flat across a full additional ratchet generation (gen2->gen3, the SAME 30B-vs-frozen-self recipe that produced gen3 from gen2) is consistent with D97/D97-A's "slope flattening" finding, now corroborated at the absolute-ladder level: the FIRST ratchet jump (gen1->gen2/gen3, +94-100 Elo from baseline) was real and large; nothing since has added to it.

(2) NON-TRANSITIVITY IS REAL, NOT NOISE. league4-vs-gen2: empirical gen2-win=47.1% vs BT-fit-predicted 55.7% (8.6pp gap on n=1133, ~3 SDs). exploiter2-vs-league4: empirical exploiter2-win=55.2% vs fit-predicted 36.8% (18.4pp gap on n=909, ~5.6 SDs) -- this one is STRONGLY non-transitive, not explainable by sampling noise. RIGHT FRAMING: BT/Elo is a useful AVERAGE-RANKING diagnostic (and the ladder tooling stays valuable for spotting tier structure and flagging non-transitive pairs), but "is training progress happening" should ALSO be read against the ABSOLUTE human-baseline eval suite (tools/eval_game_stats.sh from-kickoff vs docs/human-baseline.json, D61) -- a scale the BT ladder doesn't capture and that ISN'T relative to a possibly-drifting opponent pool.

(3) THE PATTERN IS REAL AND HAS A MECHANISM: warm-starting from a checkpoint and continuing self-play (ratchet-vs-frozen-self OR league-pool) tends to PLATEAU-OR-REGRESS on the cross-anchor ladder even when IN-RUN internal trackers (tds, possession, per-run hist_score/elo) look flat-to-improving. Ratchet: gen2->gen3 flat (94.2 vs 100.3, noise-band), gen3->gen4 REAL decline (-31.3 Elo). League: league1(78.8)->league2(45.9) sharp decline ->league4(60.7) partial recovery, still -18 below league1. MECHANISM (distributional drift / self-play overfitting): each arm's opponent population (frozen self, or a pool seeded mostly from the SAME lineage's recent generations) is a NARROW slice of the full strategy space. The learner specializes against THAT slice -- in-run trackers (which measure performance against exactly that slice) improve or look fine -- while drifting away from effectiveness against the WIDER population the ladder samples (gen1, kickoff8, v5contested, and now also each OTHER lineage's checkpoints). D96's "league Elo never plateaued (84.9->224.3)" was this exact illusion: a per-run internal tracker measuring fit-to-its-own-training-population, NOT cross-population strength -- D102-B's note that this tracker "resets on relaunch, not persistent" actually UNDERSTATED the problem; it isn't just non-persistent, it was NEVER a strength measure in the first place.

(4) LEAGUE-5 DECISION: DO NOT ABANDON (it is ~10min in, cheap to let ride) -- AND its design is ALREADY PARTIALLY RESPONSIVE to this finding: league-5's 8-bank pool (D106-A) includes BOTH gen2 AND gen3 (the TIER1 checkpoints) alongside gen4/league2/exploiter1/etc. If gen2/gen3 are genuinely strong pool opponents, league-5's learner now trains under pressure FROM the strongest known checkpoints -- a direct (if late) fix to the narrow-pool mechanism in (3). ACTION: at league-5's next ladder-worthy checkpoint, the critical NEW measurements are league5-vs-gen2 and league5-vs-gen3 specifically (does training WITH tier1 opponents in the pool let the learner approach/exceed tier1?). Separately, queue a CHEAP DIAGNOSTIC for ballhawk after exploiter-4: a short (10-15B) "gen2-continuation" arm (warm=gen2, teacher=gen2, the EXACT ratchet recipe that produced gen3) -- if a SECOND independent gen2->gen3-equivalent run ALSO lands flat/below gen2, that's strong evidence the gen2->gen3 transition is at a genuine local-optimum/plateau for this recipe, not a one-off; if it instead EXCEEDS gen2 this time, gen3's specific underperformance may have been a bad-draw artifact.

(5) DOCTRINE INCONSISTENCY FLAGGED: D102-B framed "more total training from a strong checkpoint (relaunching league3 for another 30B after the disk-crash) is a net positive from the crash" -- D107 suggests this assumption needs revisiting: MORE continued self-play from an already-decent checkpoint is NOT unconditionally good and can regress ladder-measured strength. This doesn't make D102-B's RECOVERY ACTION wrong (the alternative was losing the run entirely) but the "net positive" framing should be read as "recovered the run" not "more training = more strength."

PRACTICAL UPSHOT for the next several cycles: (a) keep league-5 + exploiter-4 running (both already informative, both cheap relative to total runway); (b) the LADDER, not internal trackers, is the persistent scoreboard -- re-extend it at every new cap, anchor=gen1 (non-degenerate); (c) the стандарт "warm-start from the most recent cap" heuristic is now SUSPECT -- future warm-start choices should be the LADDER-TOP checkpoint among recent caps, which as of D107 would be gen2 or gen3 (not league4/league3) -- this may mean some future arm warm-starts from gen2/gen3 directly rather than continuing the league/exploiter chains, once league-5/exploiter-4 report back.**
**D108 — EXPLOITER-4 CAPPED NEGATIVE/MARGINAL (hist_score_bank_0=0.367 final vs champion=league4, never approached 0.5; tds=1.083). 14-node ladder placement (anchor=gen1=0): exploiter4 = +13.3 Elo -- ABOVE its own warm-start gen1 (0.0) by 13.3, but FAR below league1/gen2/gen3 (78-103) and even below league2 (47.1)/exploiter3 (22.0). Notably exploiter4 ALSO beats gen2 (59.0% decisive) and gen3 (57.5% decisive) head-to-head despite gen2/gen3 being ~85-90 Elo ABOVE exploiter4 in the overall ranking -- ANOTHER non-transitivity instance (exploiter4's specific style counters gen2/gen3 specifically, similar to exploiter2-vs-league4 in D107). LIVE (pid 920, teacher pinned confirmed at 40s). This is the cleanest test of D107-A's central question: is gen2->gen3-equivalent training PLATEAUED (a second independent run also lands ~flat, ~94-103) or was gen3's near-tie with gen2 a draw-specific artifact (this run exceeds gen2 clearly)? Given the accumulating non-transitivity findings (D107, D108), a THIRD possible outcome is now plausible too: gen2-cont1 could land in the SAME ~95-105 Elo neighborhood as gen2/gen3 (i.e. genuinely flat/plateaued) -- all three would then form a real "tier 1 cluster" rather than a single point estimate, consistent with D98's original cluster framing one level up the lineage.**
**D109 — LEAGUE-5 IS THE NEW ALL-TIME LEADER BY A HUGE MARGIN: +178.7 Elo, 77.5 Elo above the previous tier1 (gen2 +101.2). This is the LARGEST single-generation jump in the program's history (league4 +61.9 -> league5 +178.7, a +116.8 Elo gain in ONE 30B generation), exceeding even the original gen1->gen2 ratchet jump (~+100 Elo). 15-node ladder (anchor=gen1=0, 8829 decisive games for league5 alone): league5 +178.7 >> gen2 +101.2 ~ gen3 +98.3 > league1 +77.5 > gen4 +64.0 ~ league4 +61.9 ~ exploiter1 +58.0 > league2 +47.1 > gen2cont1 +43.9 > exploiter3 +22.0 > exploiter4 +13.2 > gen1 0.0 > exploiter2 -31.7 > kickoff8 -111.5 > v5contested -330.3 > bc_v4 (degenerate). Direct head-to-heads confirm dominance: league5 beats league1 64.8% decisive, beats gen2cont1 77.9% decisive.

CAUSAL HYPOTHESIS (per D107-A's claim C, now strongly supported): league5's 8-bank pool (D106-A) was the FIRST league generation to include gen2 AND gen3 (the tier1 checkpoints) as training opponents -- exactly the "fix" D107-A proposed for narrow-pool drift. league1-4's pools never included tier1 checkpoints as opponents (league1-4 trained against progressively-drifted descendants of THEMSELVES + weaker anchors). league5, forced to play against genuinely strong, stylistically-stable opponents (gen2/gen3, which D107 showed are themselves STABLE -- gen2~gen3 within noise across a full generation), broke the narrow-pool-drift cycle decisively. This is NOT yet proven causal (one data point) but is the leading hypothesis and directly actionable.

**D110 — GEN2-CONTINUATION (gen2cont1) REGRESSED -57.3 Elo from gen2 (+43.9 vs +101.2), landing BELOW even league2 (+47.1) and well below tier1. SECOND independent confirmation that the gen2->frozen-self-30B ratchet recipe does not produce gains and CAN actively regress (gen3's result from the same recipe was roughly flat, -3 Elo; gen2cont1's is a much larger -57 Elo drop -- high variance, but BOTH independent attempts at "continue training from gen2 against a frozen copy of itself" failed to improve and one regressed substantially). Final mirror-tds 1.453 (below gen2cont1's own mid-run peak 1.575) illustrates AGAIN that in-run tds is not a reliable strength proxy (D107-A). gen2cont1 itself remains a useful POOL DIVERSITY asset (different region of strategy space than gen2/gen3, per the same logic as exploiter caps) but is NOT a viable warm-start or champion candidate going forward.

SYNTHESIS: D109+D110 together tell a clear story. The "ratchet vs frozen self" recipe (gen1->2->3->4, and now gen2cont1) is DONE -- two independent gen2-continuations both failed to improve. The "league diverse pool" recipe was ALSO failing (league1->2->3->4 non-monotonic, league4 below league1) UNTIL league5 added tier1 checkpoints (gen2/gen3) to the pool -- which produced the single best result ever. THE RECIPE GOING FORWARD: diverse pools that include the CURRENT ladder-top checkpoints as training opponents, refreshed every generation as the ladder-top changes.**

**D109-A/D110-A — LAUNCHES based on D109/D110. Both boxes get the SAME 8-bank pool design (gen2, gen3, league5, gen4, league2, gen1, exploiter1, kickoff8 -- drops v5contested, the weakest non-bc_v4 anchor, and bc_v4 itself which was already dropped at league-5) but DIFFERENT warm-starts, to test whether D109's causal hypothesis (tier1-in-pool drives gains) GENERALIZES across starting points: (1) LEAGUE-6 on japan: warm=league5_cap (the new #1 -- continue the winning lineage). (2) LEAGUE-6B on ballhawk: warm=gen3_cap (the OTHER tier1 member, Elo 98.3, a DIFFERENT lineage than league5's league4-ancestry) -- if league6b ALSO jumps dramatically with the same pool composition, the recipe generalizes broadly (strong evidence for the causal hypothesis); if it stays flat/near gen3's level, league5's jump may have been more specific to league4's particular state. Both 30B, snapshot_interval bumped 500M->2B (per the disk-pruning lesson from league3-5), kickoff-pure v4 economy (rush_cost 0.015, demo knobs 0), frozen_bank_pct 0.06/8 banks. Both caps (league5_cap, gen2cont1_cap) backed up to B2.**
**D111 — DOCTRINE: "HARD OPPONENTS" POOL-COMPOSITION PROTOCOL (codifying D109's lesson as a standing rule, not a one-off). The root cause of league1-4's non-monotonic drift was that NO league pool ever included the genuinely-strongest checkpoints as training opponents -- each generation trained against weaker/drifted descendants of itself. League5 (first pool to include gen2+gen3, the ladder-top at the time) produced the largest jump in program history (+116.8 Elo). GOING FORWARD, every new league/pool build follows this protocol:

POOL COMPOSITION (8 banks, the selfplay.py hard cap, frozen_bank_pct ~0.06):
- 2-3 TIER1 slots: the current ladder-top checkpoint(s) by fitted Elo (anchor=gen1, the stable non-degenerate anchor) -- the "hard opponents."
- 2-3 TIER2 slots: the next tier down -- a difficulty gradient so not every game is a wall (D97-A's H6 rationale: some learnable losses/wins consolidate gains).
- 1-2 DIVERSITY slots: stylistically distinct lineages even if lower-ranked (exploiters, retired-macro v5 lineage, old kickoff-era) -- prevents pool homogenization, the same logic that made exploiter1/v5contested useful pool members despite sub-tier1 Elo.
- 1 FLOOR slot: gen1 (Elo 0, the stable reference point) -- NOT bc_v4/v5-style degenerate anchors (D98: bc_v4 is 0% vs everything, zero training signal).

REFRESH CADENCE: at EVERY new cap (every ~30B generation, both lineages), extend the anchored ladder (EXTRA_ANCHORS --resume) and refit BEFORE deciding the next launch. If the new cap enters TIER1 (top-3), it joins the next pool's TIER1 slots (possibly evicting a bank that has fallen toward TIER2/3). WARM-START = current ladder-top checkpoint (D107-A's rule, already adopted) -- not necessarily "the cap that just finished," though those often coincide when the lead generation IS the new ladder-top.

DURABILITY: the ladder CSV (currently /tmp/anchored_ladder.csv on the rig, ephemeral) gets committed to the repo as tools/anchored_ladder.csv after every extension, so the ladder survives rig reboots/session loss and any future agent can read it. A checkpoint REGISTRY (docs/checkpoint_registry.json, mapping ladder-names like "gen2"/"league5" to B2 keys + local filenames + one-line provenance) is also added -- the durable lookup table that lets pool-building be mechanical rather than requiring an agent to remember "gen2 = v4_contested2_cap.bin."

AUTOMATION: tools/build_pool_from_ladder.py reads the committed ladder CSV + registry, applies the slot-allocation rule above (with override flags for diversity/floor picks), and emits the build_league.py seed-list + recommended warm-start -- turning "pick 8 checkpoints" from a manual judgment call into a mechanical step. Dispatching to codex now (.codex-impl/brief-pool-automation.md).

CURRENT STATE (as of D109's 15-node ladder, anchor=gen1): TIER1={league5 +178.7}, the next tier ={gen2 +101.2, gen3 +98.3} (note: league6/league6b are CURRENTLY TESTING whether gen2/gen3 belong in TIER1-with-league5 or get superseded). TIER2={league1 +77.5, gen4 +64.0, league4 +61.9, exploiter1 +58.0}. DIVERSITY candidates={league2 +47.1, gen2cont1 +43.9, exploiter3 +22.0, exploiter4 +13.2, exploiter2 -31.7, kickoff8 -111.5}. FLOOR={gen1 0.0}. DEGENERATE/RETIRED={v5contested -330.3, bc_v4 -1571.4}. The league6/league6b pools (D109-A) already approximate this protocol (gen2,gen3,league5 as the "hard" core + gen4/league2/exploiter1 as tier2/diversity + gen1 floor + kickoff8 diversity) -- this entry formalizes it as the STANDING rule for league7+ regardless of league6/6b's outcome.**
**D112 — LEAGUE5 FROM-KICKOFF MIRROR EVAL: tds=0.667 (30% of human 2.217), a NEW LOW -- below even the now-retired v5-kickoff's 1.625 (73%, D87). possession_rate=0.245, the HIGHEST mirror possession ever recorded (prior bests ~0.22-0.23). Sample is SMALL (8M steps, ~6-10 games, D87-equivalent caveat applies -- wide CIs). Other deltas: blocks_thrown 7.0 vs human 88.8 (-92%, lowest ever), pickup_attempts 1.917 (-74%), pass_attempts 0.000.

THE LADDER-VS-MIRROR DECOUPLING: league5 is the all-time #1 on the anchored ladder (+178.7 Elo, D109, beating gen2/gen3/league1/etc. by 20-80+ Elo each) yet posts the WORST from-kickoff mirror-tds ever measured. HYPOTHESIS (not yet verified): a policy this optimized for possession/ball-security, played against an EXACT COPY OF ITSELF, may produce a low-variance defensive standoff -- neither side takes the dodge/GFI risk needed to score, even though against a DIFFERENT policy (the ladder's diverse opponent pool: gen1-4/league1-4/exploiter1/kickoff8) it dominates. If true, the mirror-from-kickoff eval -- our historical "vs human" proxy since D61 -- may have become MISLEADING specifically for pool-trained checkpoints, and the ladder (diverse real opponents, far more human-like in variety than a self-clone) may now be the better proxy for "vs human" strength. NOT YET VERIFIED -- needs (a) a larger-sample mirror rerun to rule out the n~8 variance explanation, and (b) a league5-vs-OLDER-WEAKER-checkpoint from-kickoff eval (e.g. league5 vs kickoff8/v4_kickoff9_cap via puffer match with demo_reset_pct 0) to test whether league5 scores normally against a non-self, non-pool-trained opponent.

CONTEXT for the live timeline discussion with Alex (re: Opus's forecast): this finding ADDS uncertainty rather than resolving it in either direction. It does NOT confirm "we're closer to human than the relative jump implied" (the raw mirror number got WORSE, not better) -- but it also doesn't cleanly mean "further from human," because the METRIC ITSELF may be broken for this checkpoint. Launching a larger-sample (32M-step) rerun + a league5-vs-kickoff8 cross-checkpoint from-kickoff eval on the idle 2070 now to disambiguate.**
**D112-A — DISAMBIGUATION: gen1's mirror eval (tds=1.111, 50% of human; possession=0.176) supports the POSSESSION-SPECIALIST hypothesis over the "general contested-era degeneracy" hypothesis. Side-by-side (all from-kickoff mirror, small samples n~9-13):
  v5kick (D87, dead-teacher era):       tds 1.625 (73%), possession 0.184
  gen1   (D112-A, ladder floor, Elo 0): tds 1.111 (50%), possession 0.176
  league5 (D112, ladder #1, Elo +178.7): tds 0.667 (30%), possession 0.245

This is MONOTONIC and DIRECTIONAL, not flat: as possession_rate climbs (0.176->0.245), mirror-tds falls (1.111->0.667). gen1 is NOT in league5's depressed range -- it sits in a "normal," moderately-below-v5kick band, consistent with gen1 being an ordinary contested-era checkpoint. league5 is the OUTLIER, and it is ALSO the most possession-optimized checkpoint ever measured (highest possession_rate ever recorded). The mechanism from D112 (two highly possession-focused copies of the same policy produce a low-variance defensive standoff -- neither risks the dodge/GFI needed to score) is SUPPORTED, though still n=2 (gen1, league5) at small per-arm samples.

IMPLICATION FOR THE LIVE TIMELINE DISCUSSION (Alex's "Opus's quarters/year estimate doesn't scan given our ~2M SPS / 4h-per-30B-generation throughput"): the mirror-from-kickoff metric -- the ONLY "vs human" proxy this program has ever had -- appears to DEGRADE precisely as the policy gets MORE possession-optimized, i.e. precisely as the ladder says it's getting STRONGER. The metric and the (likely-true) underlying strength signal are anti-correlated for the current champion. This means: (1) league5's mirror-tds drop is probably NOT evidence of "further from human" -- it's a measurement artifact; (2) the ladder's +178.7 (biggest jump ever, achieved in ONE ~4-8h generation) is more likely the trustworthy "real progress" signal, supporting Alex's faster-than-quarters intuition; (3) BUT we have NO WORKING absolute "vs human-like-opponent" eval for the current champion -- v5kick's 1.625/73% is retired AND was measured under a different (non-possession-annuity-dominant, dead-teacher-era) regime, so it's not a clean baseline either. THE REAL GAP is now: build a cross-checkpoint from-kickoff eval (league5 vs an old/weak frozen opponent like kickoff8, NOT mirror) -- this avoids the self-clone degeneracy and would give the first genuinely informative absolute-scale read on the current champion. Not yet built; eval_game_stats.sh is mirror-only. Queued as the next disambiguating step once league6/6b cap (the generalization-test verdict takes priority for the next launch decision).**
**D113 — RESEARCH: reward-inference from human replays (Alex's IRL question). Two independent research efforts (a direct opus dispatch covering GAIL/AIRL/ValueDICE/AlphaStar/MimicBot, and a /research-skill agent on classic IRL tractability) converged at high confidence (9/10): full IRL (Ng-Russell LP, MaxEnt/Ziebart) is INTRACTABLE for this setup -- both require an RL-solve-to-convergence per reward-update on what would need to be a stationary MDP; self-play is the opposite of stationary, and the 454-way factored action space / 2782-dim obs is far beyond any scaled IRL precedent (even Google Maps' ICLR-2024 "massively scalable IRL" relies on DAG road-graph structure BB doesn't have).

THE TRACTABLE WINNER (independently arrived at by both research paths): AGGREGATE-STATISTIC / FEATURE-EXPECTATION MATCHING (Abbeel & Ng 2004's apprenticeship-learning framing == AlphaStar's productionized "pseudo-rewards": episode-end reward = -distance(agent's cumulative game stats, human target stats)). This is the literal match to Alex's framing ("look at every step in aggregate, derive what reward would produce this behavior"). Implementation: NO engine/C changes needed (episode-boundary hook exists); compute agent stats via the same machinery as game_stats.py (possession_rate, tds, dodges, pickups, passes, blocks per game), compute distance to docs/human-baseline.json / docs/per-team-baseline.json, add as an episode-end pseudo-reward term. Fully interpretable and auditable-per-statistic against D90's anti-farming doctrine (unlike a discriminator logit).

SECOND PRECEDENTED OPTION: MimicBot (the actual Bot Bowl III winner for THIS GAME, arXiv 2108.09478) used interleaved BC-gradient updates during RL (behavioral anchor toward bc_v4) -- pure trainer-loss term, also no engine changes, the BB-native version of AlphaStar's KL-to-human-policy anchor.

GAIL/AIRL (discriminator-as-learned-reward) was assessed and DEPRIORITIZED: it's the "formal" version of the idea but adds a SECOND opaque reward channel at exactly the moment D112 showed our FIRST (hand-tuned) reward channel produced degenerate possession-obsessed behavior -- either frozen (exploitable/reward-hacking) or co-trained (GAN instability on top of self-play non-stationarity).

SEQUENCING: TD-maniac (queued, zero possession annuity / big reward_td / zero rush_cost) is the CHEAP PROBE -- if a 5-minute hand-retune fixes D112's degeneracy, aggregate-stat-matching may be unnecessary; if it doesn't, aggregate-stat-matching is the principled follow-up (lets HUMAN DATA set the target mix instead of hand-guessing). Relative to D111's pool-composition lever: orthogonal axis, but D109's biggest-ever jump came from POOL not REWARD changes, and D90 already warns against opaque shaping ("defense needed an opponent, not a bounty"). PRIORITY: pool-composition (D111) remains primary; TD-maniac launches when a box frees (league6/6b cap, ~1.5-2h); aggregate-stat-matching is a queued PARALLEL low-priority research track, design pending TD-maniac's result.**
**D113-A — Aggregate-stat-matching refined to an implementable spec (confirms+extends D113). GAIL/AIRL angle: confirmed deprioritized -- no 2023-2026 work solves discriminator instability for >100-way factored action spaces under self-play; the closest success (AMP, frozen discriminator) is continuous/single-agent/fixed-opponent, and the RLHF frozen-reward-model literature documents the EXACT failure mode self-play would trigger (policy diverges from training distribution -> frozen classifier becomes unreliable -> exploited). If tried at all: small auxiliary bonus with a DECAY SCHEDULE, never primary.

Aggregate-matching angle: STRONGLY reinforced with new grounding. (1) Waymo Open Sim Agents Challenge (2023-2025) validates the exact pattern (aggregate behavioral-statistic matching) at industrial scale. (2) "Of Moments and Matching" (Swamy, ICML 2021) gives the formal bound: matching moments of demonstrator behavior bounds the imitation gap regardless of the TRUE unknown reward. (3) "Correlated Proxies" (Laidlaw 2024) is the KEY justification for why JOINT matching avoids D112's single-stat degeneracy: optimizing an ENSEMBLE of correlated proxies jointly is robust because gaming one metric while tanking others requires orthogonal exploitation of ALL simultaneously -- possession_rate is SAFE as one dimension of a joint target even though it was UNSAFE as an isolated annuity (D90/D112).

IMPLEMENTABLE SPEC: episode-end pseudo-reward = -scale * sqrt(sum_i ((agent_stat_i - human_mean_i)/human_std_i)^2) [diagonal-Mahalanobis/Z-score L2, NOT PBRS -- raw episodic term]. Stat vector: {tds, dodgeRoll, pickUpRoll, passRoll, goForItRoll, block_2dred_frac, possession_rate_d90} -- all 7 jointly (possession_rate INCLUDED but only as one of seven, not isolated). scale ~0.2-0.5x typical episode return (start small). MUST zero reward_possession (the 0.03 annuity) -- cannot coexist with possession_rate in the joint target (annuity has denser gradient, would dominate). Activate ONLY at kickoff-start (demo_reset_pct=0) -- curriculum-stage episodes are too short for full-game stat targets to be meaningful. Use docs/human-baseline.json as a FIXED exogenous target (not the live opponent's stats -- in contested self-play the opponent's defense affects your tds/dodges, but the human baseline is fixed and correctly anchors the optimization). Gotchas: untracked-dimension exploits (the 7 stats don't cover everything -- monitor post-hoc), sparse episodic credit (keep coefficient small relative to dense per-step rewards), small-sample eval noise (track running averages over 1000+ episodes during training, not single evals).

This is now a near-ready brief for a codex-implementer dispatch -- queued as the parallel low-priority research track per D113, behind TD-maniac (cheap probe) and D111's pool-composition primary lever.**

**D113-B — MimicBot deep-dive: NOT usable as a tournament contestant (no code/weights exist, BB2016/wrong-edition, 8116-way flat-conv action space vs our 454-way factored), but yields THREE transferable techniques. (1) EV-BASED MASK SHAPING (the most actionable): MimicBot's biggest lever beyond BC was deleting no-brainer-bad actions from the LEGAL ACTION MASK at decision time -- specifically, blocks with >70% turnover probability were masked to -inf pre-softmax (plus forcing ball-carrier-blocks-last). We ALREADY COMPUTE the exact probabilities needed (obs-v4's A1/A2/B planes, tools/blockev_mc.c) -- this could be added as a cheap, ANNEALABLE binding-level mask filter (per D28/D46's gradual-anneal-never-cold-off doctrine), a candidate anti-degeneracy A/B independent of reward changes. (2) INDEPENDENT VALIDATION of our obs-v4 probability-plane design -- MimicBot (SOTA at the time) independently arrived at the same "put roll/block-dice probability planes in the observation" idea; no design change needed, just external corroboration. (3) INTERLEAVED-BC-DURING-RL (alternating whole optimizer steps between RL and BC, hard-cutting BC at a step threshold) is a DISTINCT technique from our current bc_coef aux-loss (cosine-annealed auxiliary loss term) -- a legitimate ablation if BC-anchoring (D113's Option B / MimicBot-recipe) ever shows gradient interference.

THE "MIMICBOT-STYLE BASELINE" recommendation: replicate the RECIPE (BC warm-start + interleaved-BC + EV-mask-shaping) trained on OUR BB2025 corpus (validation/pairs_v4) -- drops into the ladder/registry with ZERO new infra (same obs-v4/454-head/flat-fp32 format). Medium value: likely lands near the bottom (D98 found bc_v4-style pure-imitation is degenerate, 0% decisive vs everything) but serves as (a) a reproducible NAMED baseline node, (b) a testbed for techniques (1) and (3) above. LOW PRIORITY -- queued behind TD-maniac and D111's pool lever.

FOR AN EXTERNAL BB2025 CONTESTANT (the original ask's "at minimum"): NOT MimicBot/botbowl (wrong edition, no bot exists there either). FFB (the BB2025 reference engine) has NO bot/AI player currently -- NUFFLEBOT (the headless FFB-client bridge, docs/nufflebot-feasibility.md) remains the right long-term path, and ~70% of its code overlaps the already-planned Phase-4 replay-differential harness (task #6). No shortcut exists; this is a multi-week project already on the roadmap, not a quick win.**

**D114 — IMPLEMENTED: D113-A's aggregate-statistic-matching pseudo-reward (the principled "let human data set the target mix" follow-up to D112's hand-tuned-reward degeneracy). New env knob `reward_statmatch_scale` (CLI `--env.reward-statmatch-scale`, default 0.0 = OFF = bit-identical to existing arms; binding.c:90, bloodbowl.h struct field). When >0, `bbe_finish_episode` adds an episode-end term `-scale * sqrt(sum_i z_i^2)`, z_i = (agent_stat_i - human_mean_i)/human_std_i over the 7 D113-A stats {tds, dodgeRoll, pickUpRoll, passRoll, goForItRoll, block_2dred_frac, possession_rate} (diagonal-Mahalanobis / Z-score L2 -- a RAW episodic term, NOT PBRS, per spec). New dashboard field `statmatch_term` (the per-episode term, <=0; binding.c dict_set) so it is directly observable.

KEY IMPLEMENTATION CHOICES (reviewable design calls):
(1) MATCH-LEVEL, SYMMETRIC, not per-agent. The 7 stat counters in the env (ep_dodge_attempts, ep_block_tier, ep_turns/ep_turns_with_ball, etc.) are tracked match-level (both teams summed) -- which is EXACTLY how human-baseline.json was measured (dodgeRoll_per_game etc. are both-teams-per-game totals, see tools/game_stats.py METRICS). So I compute ONE term on the match-level vector and apply it SYMMETRICALLY to both self-play agents. The spec said "per-agent from that agent's counters"; I deviated because per-agent half-game stats are NOT what the baseline measures, and self-play means both agents jointly authored the game's statistics. Flagged for review: if a future asymmetric (learner-vs-frozen) statmatch arm is wanted, the term should switch to per-team counters and apply only to the learner -- not done here (statmatch1 is symmetric frozen-self).
(2) GATE: term activates ONLY when reward_statmatch_scale>0 AND demo_started==0 (kickoff-pure episode). Curriculum/demo-reset episodes never receive it regardless of the flag (safe-by-default; full-game stat targets are meaningless on truncated curriculum starts). statmatch1 also forces --env.demo-reset-pct 0 so EVERY episode is a full game.
(3) reward_possession FORCED to 0 in the launch (cannot coexist -- the 0.03 annuity's dense per-turn gradient would dominate the joint possession_rate target; D90/D112 already showed isolated possession shaping is poison, D113-A's Correlated-Proxies result only rehabilitates possession_rate AS ONE OF SEVEN jointly).

human_std DERIVATION (the open methodology question -- DEFENSIBLE-BUT-ARBITRARY, documented per Alex's review rule): NO per-game stats table exists anywhere in the repo (searched validation/ tools/ docs/ for any per-replay JSON/CSV with these 7 stats -- only the AGGREGATE docs/human-baseline.json from D61 exists; the corpus was reduced to means over 12722 games / 453617 team-turns, per-game values not retained). Re-deriving a per-game corpus from raw replays is a much larger task (>>30min) so I used the spec's principled FALLBACK: count stats (tds, dodgeRoll, goForItRoll, pickUpRoll, passRoll) are event-counts-per-game, treated as Poisson => std = sqrt(mean); fraction stats use std = sqrt(p(1-p)/n) with n = the per-game denominator (block_2dred over ~88.83 blocks/game = blockRoll_per_game; possession_rate over ~35.66 team-turns/game = 453617/12722). Computed stds: tds 1.489, dodgeRoll 5.068, pickUpRoll 2.700, passRoll 1.404, goForItRoll 4.169, block_2dred_frac 0.01368, possession_rate 0.0812 (hardcoded HB_STD[7] in bloodbowl.h alongside HB_MEAN[7]). CAVEAT WORTH REVIEW: block_2dred_frac's std (0.0137) is SMALLER than its mean (0.0169), and the agent sits at ~0.12-0.15 (~10x human), so that single dimension's z is ~9-10 and contributes ~84% of the squared norm -- the term is effectively "stop taking 2d-red blocks" with the other 6 stats as minor seasoning. This is DIRECTIONALLY correct (the planes-working doctrine wants 2dred falling toward human) but means statmatch1 is NOT a balanced 7-way pull in practice. If we want a balanced pull, floor the fraction stds (e.g. min 0.03-0.05) or switch counts to a real empirical per-game std -- left as-is for the first probe, monitor whether 2dred collapses while the other 6 stay stuck (= over-domination) vs all 7 converging.

SCALE = 0.01 chosen (the launch default), calibrated EMPIRICALLY not guessed: a scale=1.0 smoke run (warm league5_cap, native, 40M steps, kickoff-pure) measured mean statmatch_term = -13.4 => mean per-episode ||z|| ~ 13, and base episode_return ~0.45-0.65 (statmatch off). 0.01 => mean term ~ -0.11 to -0.13 = ~0.2-0.3x of base return, the LOW end of the spec's 0.2-0.5x band ("start small" -- sparse episodic credit must stay subordinate to the dense per-step rewards). (Note: hand-computing ||z|| from the mean stats gives 10.45, but the per-episode-then-averaged term is -13.4 by Jensen -- episode-to-episode noise inflates E[||z||] above ||E[z]||. Both are sane; implementation verified correct.)

SMOKE-TEST EVIDENCE (rig, RTX 2070, native --float build, warm league5_cap): builds CLEAN with the changes (only the pre-existing benign _XOPEN_SOURCE redefinition warnings; math.h/sqrtf added to bloodbowl.h). scale=1.0 run: statmatch_term -13.4, demo_episodes 0.0 (kickoff gate confirmed -- all episodes full games), no crashes, term finite/sane. REGRESSION CHECK: a scale=0 run (15M steps, otherwise identical) gave statmatch_term EXACTLY 0.0 and episode_return 0.456 = base economy only, proving the default-off path is inert (additive 0.0f is an IEEE no-op; the `>0.0f` gate excludes the default). Code committed atomically (knob+pseudo-reward; launch script separate). POOL-COMPOSITION CHOICE: statmatch1 runs FROZEN-SELF (no D111 league pool) deliberately -- to get a CLEAN single-variable read on the REWARD change without entangling D111's orthogonal pool lever (per the launch guidance). A pool-enabled variant is a later follow-up.**

**D115 — NEXT-STEPS BACKLOG: reward-economy "extreme variant" candidates (Alex's "what would an extreme TD/win reward look like, and what's the downside" discussion, 2026-06-14). These are FOLLOW-UPS, contingent on results from the three currently-active probes (statmatch1 running on the rig per D114-A; TD-maniac and stakes1 staged at /tmp/launch_tdmaniac1.sh and /tmp/launch_stakes1.sh, both warm=league5_cap, both pending a freed Vast box). Not launched -- documented so the reasoning survives even if the next session doesn't have this conversation's context.

TD-REWARD AXIS (current default reward_td=0.4; TD-maniac=1.2):
- Axis-1 (magnitude) extreme: reward_td 3.0-5.0+. At this scale a single TD swing (+/-3 to +/-5, zero-sum per bloodbowl.h:1919-1922) dwarfs every other term (dist_endzone 0.2, k_value/k_ball/k_kd/k_seq 0.25/0.15/0.03/0.01, win 0.6, possession 0.03/turn) -- the game reduces to "TD differential, weighted huge."
- Axis-2 (structure) extreme: zero ALL other shaping (dist_endzone, k_*, ball_gain, possession, win/draw) so reward_td is the ONLY signal -- sparse TD-differential-only RL.
- DOWNSIDE (both axes): (1) TDs are RARE (human ~1.1/team/game over ~100 turns) and arrive after long sequences -- making the rarest, latest event also the LARGEST reward maximizes return variance on exactly the hardest-to-credit signal, especially destabilizing against a non-stationary self-play opponent. (2) The dense shaping terms teach the PREREQUISITE skills (positioning, ball security, dodge selection) that human TDs are built on; swamping them in the value-function loss could paradoxically SLOW TD growth, not accelerate it. (3) Directly amplifies the existing "Hail Mary" pattern (GFI/dodge attempts already 5-10x human at reward_td=0.4) -- pushes FURTHER from human on the exact axes D113-A's statmatch term is pulling TOWARD human. (4) Same Goodhart shape as D112 (possession), mirrored: over-weighting one proxy optimizes that proxy at the expense of what it's a proxy FOR, with no guarantee the result generalizes (echoes D107/D108 non-transitivity). RECOMMENDATION: only pursue axis-1 (3.0-5.0) as a follow-up if TD-maniac (1.2) shows TDs moving in the right direction but too weakly to matter; axis-2 (sparse TD-only) is a last resort, not a first move.

WIN-REWARD AXIS (current default reward_win=0.6 spread 1.2; stakes1=1.4 spread 2.8; reward_draw=0):
- Axis-1 (magnitude) extreme: reward_win 3.0-5.0+ (spread 6-10). bloodbowl.ini:40's "reward_td + reward_win <= 1.0 on the winning-TD step" invariant is already broken by stakes1's 1.4 and would be badly broken here (5.4 on that one step vs 0.01-0.25 elsewhere).
- DOWNSIDE (axis-1): (1) Long-horizon discounting: a ~100-team-turn episode means gamma^(steps-to-go) may shrink an even-bigger terminal reward into near-irrelevance at turn 1 anyway -- cranking the NUMBER doesn't fix a problem that's really about HORIZON LENGTH; what it reliably does is dominate the last few turns disproportionately (normal play for 90% of the game, erratic/extreme in the endgame). (2) Win/loss is NOISY (a late dice roll flips close games) -- huge magnitude on a noisy binary outcome inflates variance on otherwise-similar trajectories, destabilizing PPO's advantage estimates. (3) AMBIGUOUS effect on D112's stalling problem: raising stakes SYMMETRICALLY could make a policy that's AHEAD stall EVEN HARDER (bigger downside to blowing the lead) while a policy BEHIND gets more desperate -- net "liveliness" could be unchanged, just redistributed by game-state rather than reduced.
- Axis-2 (punish draws specifically): leave reward_win alone, make reward_draw meaningfully NEGATIVE (both sides, symmetric) -- e.g. -1 to -2. More SURGICAL than axis-1: D112's finding wasn't "winning isn't valuable enough," it was "drawing/low-scoring-stall is currently a perfectly acceptable outcome (reward_draw=0)." Making any non-decisive result actively costly targets that directly without disturbing the win/loss spread or the reward_td+reward_win<=1.0 invariant.
- Axis-2b (the genuinely-extreme option): zero ALL shaping entirely -- no dist_endzone, no k_*, no possession, no ball_gain, no per-TD reward -- pure +/-W at episode end (AlphaZero-style). Removes essentially ALL Goodhart/proxy-gaming risk (nothing to game except the actual win condition) but reintroduces the cold-start problem dense shaping was ADDED to solve -- EXCEPT we are not training from scratch; league5 is already a competent, win-capable policy. Stripping scaffolding from a strong warm-start and letting pure win/loss take over is the natural endpoint of D28/D46's "anneal scaffolding away" doctrine taken to its limit in one step rather than gradually. The most STRUCTURALLY INTERESTING of the extreme options -- a real "next era" candidate (post-statmatch1/TD-maniac/stakes1, from whichever checkpoint wins that 3-way readout), not a first move.

SEQUENCING: all of the above are gated on the outcomes of the THREE currently-active probes (D114-A statmatch1, staged TD-maniac, staged stakes1). Revisit this entry once those resolve -- the winner/loser pattern among those three should inform WHICH of these follow-ups (if any) is worth a box.**

**D116-A — LAUNCH: TD-MANIAC live on japan (pid 235), warm/teacher=`training/league6_cap.bin` (28.03B -- used in place of the originally-staged league5_cap, since league6 is a strict continuation of league5's winning D111 recipe with an even-more-refined pool; "freshest available, same lineage" beats "one generation stale" under D107-A's ladder-top-warm-start rule even before the formal ladder extension confirms the ordering). **D116-B — LAUNCH: STAKES1 (Alex's "is winning rewarded enough?" probe, D115 axis-1) live on ballhawk (pid 176), warm/teacher=`training/league6b_cap.bin` (28.03B, same "freshest of the lineage" rationale as D116-A). Config: `--env.reward-win 1.4` (spread 0.6->1.4 means win/loss spread goes 1.2->2.8), everything else UNCHANGED from D90 settled v4 economy -- `reward_possession 0.03` deliberately left ON (single-variable test: can raised win/loss stakes override the possession-stalling incentive D112 implicates, without touching possession/TD directly). **D119 — RESEARCH BACKLOG: "skill-aware role assignment" is weakly-or-non represented in the reward economy (Alex's passing digression, 2026-06-15). Three related findings, unified by one theme: Blood Bowl strategy constantly asks "WHICH PLAYER should do this," and our reward function mostly can't see player identity/skills at all -- it sees positions and ball state.

(1) PASSING'S PRECONDITION-OF-A-PRECONDITION: a Pass requires (a) the ball-carrier to have Pass/be a Thrower, AND (b) a Catcher already positioned downfield, in range, unmarked -- BEFORE the pass is even attempted. In human play, "get the ball to the Thrower" (often via kickoff retrieval routing, sometimes a hand-off) is itself a deliberate early-game decision, made turns before any pass. CONFIRMED IN CODE: `reward_ball_gain` (bloodbowl.h:1945) is completely skill-agnostic -- picking up the ball with the Thrower vs. any Lineman gives an IDENTICAL reward. The reward function cannot represent "this pickup matters more because of who made it."

(2) THE FORMATION PROBLEM: pushing a Catcher into open space downfield, BEFORE the ball arrives near them, changes none of {dist_ball, dist_endzone, k_value, k_ball} (all ball/carrier-centric) -- it is reward-NEUTRAL at the moment it happens, with the payoff (enabling a future pass) several turns away and uncertain. Blood Bowl strategy is substantially about TEAM SHAPE (screens, cages, spreading receivers) independent of where the ball currently is -- there may be NO existing reward term with this in its domain at all.

(3) PICKUP RISK SHOULD BE SKILL-CONDITIONAL: 4+AG and/or Sure-Hands players should preferentially contest loose balls -- minimizing failed-pickup turnovers is foundational risk management (a failed pickup roll = immediate turnover, ending the whole remaining turn). PARTIALLY may already be addressed by EXISTING machinery: obs-v4's probability planes encode per-square pickup-success odds (docs/obs-v4-spec.md, "AG/TZ/weather grids -> expected plane-B"), and `k_seq` = `P(turnover of this roll) * pending_safe_activations` (bloodbowl.h:276) is a generic turnover-probability-weighted penalty that SHOULD already discourage low-AG players from contesting risky pickups when better options exist. OPEN RESEARCH QUESTIONS: (a) is the probability plane computed per-ACTING-PLAYER (so the agent can see "if I move THIS specific low-AG player here, my odds are worse than if my Sure-Hands player went instead") or is it a generic/shared plane that doesn't vary by who's being asked to act? (b) is k_seq's gradient strong enough RELATIVE to the other dense terms to actually shape "send the right player" -- given D46's standing finding that GFI/dodge attempts run 5-10x human rates, the EXISTING turnover-probability machinery does not appear to be producing human-like risk aversion in general, so (3) may be a SYMPTOM of that broader unsolved problem rather than a missing feature per se.

SEQUENCING: this is a RESEARCH track (per Alex, "backlog entry to research") -- queued alongside D113-B's MimicBot-style-baseline and D115's reward-economy-extreme-variants as parallel low-priority threads, behind the three currently-running probes (statmatch2, TD-maniac, stakes1). Candidate next steps when picked up: (i) audit whether obs-v4's probability planes are per-acting-player or generic (quick code read); (ii) if generic, that's a real obs-v4 gap worth its own design doc; (iii) if per-player and k_seq's weight is the bottleneck, that's a cheap knob to A/B; (iv) the formation problem (2) likely needs either a new reward term (team-shape/spread metric) or the D115-axis-2b sparse-objective route -- no cheap fix exists yet, needs design work before any launch.**

**D117-A — D117's FIX CONFIRMED: both TD-maniac and stakes1 capped cleanly at 15.0B with ZERO Traceback/KeyError (vs league6/6b's crash), and BOTH saved a final checkpoint at essentially exactly 15.0B (`0000014999879680.bin` -- the new save-location convention is `checkpoints/bloodbowl/<epoch-ms>/`, NOT the pool dir). Both backed up to B2 (`tdmaniac1_cap.bin`, `stakes1_cap.bin`). The fix is validated on its first real-world test.

THE 3-WAY REWARD-SHAPING PROBE RESULTS (all vs the league5-mirror baseline, D112; statmatch1 = D114-A 5B steps warm=league5; TD-maniac/stakes1 = D116-A/B 15B steps warm=league6/league6b respectively -- NOTE different warm-start lineages and step counts, not perfectly apples-to-apples):

|---------------------|-------|----------------|-----------------|------------------|----------------|
| tds                 | 2.217 | 0.667          | 1.325           | 1.016            | 1.042          |
| possession_rate     | 0.378 | 0.245          | 0.248           | 0.178            | 0.222          |
| pass_attempts       | 1.97  | ~0              | 0.006           | 0.001            | 0.035          |
| block_2dred_frac    | 0.0169| ~0.18-0.20      | 0.125           | 0.100            | 0.080          |
| dodge_attempts      | 25.68 | -               | 14.93           | 11.92            | 8.31           |
| gfi_attempts        | 17.38 | -               | 20.18           | 13.16            | 10.78          |
| pickup_attempts     | 7.29  | -               | 4.18            | 1.76             | 1.65           |
| pickup_success_rate | 0.67  | -               | 0.568           | 0.988            | 0.938          |
| episode_return      | -     | -               | ~0.45-0.65 base | 0.876            | 0.319          |
| score_diff vs frozen-self | -| -              | -               | 0.158            | -0.061         |

THREE FINDINGS:

(1) **D46 ("GFI/dodge 5-10x human") NO LONGER HOLDS for any of the three current arms** -- ALL THREE now show gfi_attempts AND dodge_attempts BELOW human levels (statmatch1 closest to human on gfi, stakes1 lowest of all on both). This is a REVERSAL of the standing D46 finding. D46 was measured on an OLDER pre-D109/D111 checkpoint lineage; the league5/6/6b-descended lineage (hard-opponents pool training) appears to have ALREADY substantially fixed the GFI/dodge-spam pathology, independent of any of these three reward tweaks. **THIS MATTERS FOR D120** (the codex/Opus reward-economy pressure test, still pending): Opus ranked "k_seq's block-declarations-only scope -> explains most of D46" as the #1 highest-impact gap. That code-level analysis is still TRUE (k_seq IS scoped to blocks only), but its empirical URGENCY may be stale -- the gfi/dodge-spam it was meant to explain doesn't appear to be happening anymore in the current lineage. D120 should account for this.

(2) **stakes1's pass_attempts=0.035 is the first meaningful movement off zero** -- 6x statmatch1's 0.006, 35x TD-maniac's 0.001 (still tiny vs human's 1.97, but a real signal for the first time across ~6 measured checkpoints). Speculative: raising win/loss stakes may open exploration of previously-never-sampled actions (including Pass) by making the policy more willing to deviate from its current near-deterministic behavior when the stakes of the outcome are higher. Worth watching if stakes1 continues.

(3) **block_2dred_frac ranking is stakes1 (0.080) < TD-maniac (0.100) < statmatch1 (0.125) < league5-baseline (~0.18-0.20)** -- stakes1, which doesn't target this metric in any way, achieved the BEST reduction of the three. tds ranking is statmatch1 (1.325) > stakes1 (1.042) ~ TD-maniac (1.016), all well above the 0.667 baseline -- though statmatch1's comparison is confounded (different warm-start lineage [league5 vs league6/6b] and step count [5B vs 15B]).

STANDING CAVEAT (D107-A): these are single end-of-run TRAINING DASHBOARD reads (self-play distribution against the arm's own frozen-self), not tournament/ladder placements -- in-run tds is not a reliable strength proxy. The real verdict needs the deferred D109-A ladder-extension tournament (now finally possible -- both Vast boxes are free: japan idle since TD-maniac capped, ballhawk just restarted after the idle-guard stopped it). Queued for next cycle: extend the anchored ladder with league6, league6b, tdmaniac1_cap, stakes1_cap, and statmatch1_cap (statmatch2 still running on the rig).**

**D121 — AndyDavo corpus synthesis vs reward-economy pressure test (research, 2026-06-15).** Read all 16 AndyDavo coaching-video packs in `docs/vendor/andydavo/*.md` (344KB; numbered by playlist position) for anything mapping onto a reward term, curriculum/demo-bank design, or BC-anchoring target. The packs each carry a doc-author "RL-mapping" section, but those were treated as SECONDARY — the load-bearing content is the timestamped dialogue/board-states (the actual source). Two prior artifacts frame this: the codex/Opus **pressure test** (pending as D120) and the in-repo **`docs/reward-design-coaching-wisdom.md` memo (R1–R11)**, which I discovered IS itself a prior synthesis of much of this same corpus — a comprehensive but as-yet-UNIMPLEMENTED design (the live header only has `k_kd/k_value/k_ball/k_seq` + `surf_taken/inflicted` [DEFAULT 0=OFF] + `possession` + `dist_*` + `ball_gain/loss` + `rush_cost` + `statmatch`). Reconciliation below is against BOTH the pressure test AND the R-memo, since they overlap.

**CODE-LEVEL GROUND TRUTH (verified in `puffer/bloodbowl/bloodbowl.h` this pass):** (a) `k_seq` is block-declaration-only AND turn<8-gated (line 1812: `act.type == BB_A_BLOCK_TARGET ... && m->turn[bteam] < 8`); dodges/GFI/pickup pay ZERO sequencing charge — pressure-test #1 finding CONFIRMED still true at code level. (b) Crowd-surf terms (`reward_surf_taken/inflicted`) ARE coded (header 255–258, applied 2044–2053) but ship DEFAULT-OFF — not in the settled v4 economy. (c) NO term has off-ball formation/screen/cage/spread in its domain (D119-2 confirmed). (d) NO per-step reroll-management term exists, and the R-memo (line 82) deliberately EXCLUDES "reroll budgeting beyond R9" as a value-network job.

### Part A — the 9 pressure-test principles

1. **Risk-sequencing / action-order ("safe things first").** CORROBORATED, overwhelmingly — the single most-repeated theme in the corpus. "Stand up downed players FIRST (0-risk) before rolling any dice" (#09 12:59, #01 08:00 "flat mistake" blitzing-before-standing-up). "Screen/cover the ball BEFORE throwing LoS blocks" (#01 03:01 "I should have covered and screened the ball first"). "Secure the ball carrier's safety before non-Block blocks" (#22 12:12, #29 12:12, #08 12:12 — the Str-5-no-Block-blocks-first blunder recurs across 3 packs of the SAME Chaos/Skaven game). EXTENDS the pressure test in one concrete way: AndyDavo repeatedly frames the cost as **scaling with unactivated players left** ("two-thirds of my turn's resources for precisely zero," #01 29:27; "spent two-thirds... a mistake") — which is EXACTLY R1's `pending_safe_activations` weighting that `k_seq` already implements for blocks. So the corpus strongly endorses EXTENDING `k_seq`-style pricing to dodge/GFI/pickup declarations (the pressure-test #1 gap), NOT just leaving it block-only. **But see D117-A caveat: the gfi/dodge-spam this was meant to explain no longer appears in the current lineage.**

2. **Caging.** CORROBORATED + EXTENDED with hard mechanics. Anti-leap "elongated X-cage" = put a 5th player DIRECTLY BEHIND the carrier to deny the leap-landing square (#02 11:20). "Never leave a cage CORNER open — agile opponents dodge in / the 2d-uphill out lives there" (#08 19:14, #22 15:53 "loose cage with open corner," #29 15:53). "Sideline three-prong cage" uses the sideline as the 4th wall, freeing one player (#01 33:51). "Loose cage" intentionally trades tightness for carrier escape-mobility when based (#06 08:33). Keep the ball on a Str-4 piece so cage-breaking needs multiple assists (#01 18:00 "keeping the ball on a Str-4 piece is always preferred"). NONE of this is representable today (no formation term). R-memo's **R6 (carrier-exposure, min-dodges-to-reach == 0)** is the formation-agnostic proxy and is its stated answer (memo line 80 explicitly refuses cage-shape templates).

3. **Cage-breaking.** CORROBORATED + EXTENDED with the most quantitative heuristic in the whole corpus: **to strip a caged ball, mark the cage corners in 2 tackle zones FIRST — a bouncing ball that an AG3 corner would catch on 4+ becomes a 6+ in two TZs, so they drop it and it bounces OUT of the cage** (#06 22:26, near-verbatim repeated in the #06 frame catalog). "Crush something IN: chain-push an adjacent player INTO the carrier to dislodge them" as an alternative to pushing a corner out (#32 03:49). "Rolling 8–12 block dice on the carrier in one turn makes a strip mathematically guaranteed even with no rerolls" (#26 39:35, the Frenzy-Werewolf double-blitz stack). Leap-sack into the open landing square behind the carrier (#02 12:45). Not representable; would emerge from R6/R7 + the exposure transfer if the agent ever learned to set it up.

4. **Screening.** CORROBORATED + heavily EXTENDED. The recurring concrete rule: **screeners stand on DIAGONALS / 2-squares-apart (knight's-move) so tackle zones overlap and no straight-line lane exists, WITHOUT giving the opponent a free block** (#10 "S-shape," #07 "column defense," #06 18:33 "2-square horizontal gap," #31 12:40 "Space Invader screen, staggered columns 2 apart"). "Maintain a 1-square gap — do NOT stand base-to-base on the opponent's turn; force them to spend their blitz for any contact" (#06 18:33, #10 takeaway-3). "Wide/flat denies the wings; the Boat/Chevron each have specific counters" (#07 whole pack). Today: no screen term. R-memo's **R7 (conceded-2D contact)** prices "do not stand where the opponent gets a free ≥2d block on you," which is the inverse-side of the same coin. **NEW nuance R7 does NOT capture: the "1-square air-gap" is about denying contact ENTIRELY (zero blocks), not just denying 2-dice — corpus is emphatic that 1-dice free blocks are also to be avoided on defense.**

5. **Screen-penetration.** CORROBORATED. "Stretching the rope": with a player advantage, spread WIDE to thin the opponent's screen, then concentrate locally against one thin section and flood through (#31 11:35 — a genuinely new, named concept). "Offset/split the LoS to open a 7-square gap, then punch through with Guard/Str4/AG5" (#07 04:30, #06 12:47). "Faking the score" — send runners deep to force the defense to spread, opening the center (#16 02:50, #29). Chain-push your OWN blitzer forward through a T/box to gain 1–2 squares of reach and blitz an out-of-range carrier (#09 12:59, the out-of-range-chain-push puzzle). No term; needs path-actions (v5) or formation reward.

6. **Basing / tie-up trades.** CORROBORATED + EXTENDED + one CORRECTION to the pressure test's "partially-and-possibly-mis-signed" worry. The corpus is crystal-clear on the SIGN: **base on a KNOCKDOWN (follow up, pin the prone player); on a PUSH do NOT follow up (step back, keep the air-gap, deny the free return-block)** (#02 28:30 "Basing on Knockdown, Free on Push," #16 38:00 invariant). Base with HIGH-strength / grouped-assist pieces so any block-back is 1-die/uphill; never base with a weak piece that gets blocked back free (#01 25:53, #02). "4-vs-7 trade": tie up 7 opponents with 4 cheap Zombies to win the numbers war elsewhere (#26 30:52). "Pseudo-stun": knocking down a MA3 Mummy costs it 3 MA to stand = effectively removed (#02 18:50). This is a clean, consistent sign and matches R7's "1D-marking-is-fine, concede-no-2D" framing — the pressure test's mis-sign worry looks RESOLVED by the corpus: the doctrine is "marking is good when it's 1-dice-for-them, bad when it's 2-dice-for-them," which is exactly R7's dice-based (not adjacency-based) predicate.

7. **Re-roll management.** CORROBORATED with the SPECIFIC NUMBER the pilot hoped for. Pack **#13 (FiveWaysToImprove) Tip 4, [03:01–04:13], verbatim: "Try to save one or two team rerolls for the final three turns of a drive (the 'business end')."** Corroborated by #02 09:08 ("preserve a reroll for the Turn-8 one-turn-score attempt") and #31 15:10 ("rerolls wasted early on low-impact actions left none for the critical end-game dodges"). Decision heuristic, repeated: **"If this fails, does it screw me? Do I even NEED to do this action?"** (#13, #08 06:40, #26 16:37) and **"Would I take this 3+ dodge if I had ALREADY used my team reroll?" — if no, it's sub-optimal** (#26 18:10). PRESSURE-TEST AGREED this is "not representable as a per-step reward (needs BC/curriculum)" — corpus CONFIRMS: the "save for the last 3 turns" rule is a clock-and-trajectory value judgment, exactly what the R-memo (line 82) says to leave to the value net. R-memo's **R9 ("no greed rerolls" — don't burn a RR on a pool that already has a zero-turnover face)** is the ONLY per-step slice that's cleanly priceable, and the corpus directly supports it (#26 18:10, #29 06:43). **The "reserve 1–2 RRs for the final 3 turns" heuristic is a BC-anchoring / curriculum target, not a reward term.**

8. **Game-management / tempo.** CORROBORATED, ubiquitous (every replay pack). The "Turn-8 stall" / "2-1 grind" is stated in #01, #02, #08, #09, #16, #22, #29, #31 — universal across races, with the execution-timing varying by speed (fast teams wait in the backfield; slow teams like Dwarfs/Orcs must START advancing by turn 2–3, #02 00:00, #31). Defense has exactly two win-conditions: force an EARLY score (you get turns to equalize) OR prevent scoring entirely (#01 24:31, #02 14:00). EXTENDS: **"two-turn planning horizon — never play turn-by-turn; every move must set up where you go next turn AND the turn after"** (#31 09:10, #10 "working backwards from where you want to be on Turn 8"). This is precisely R-memo's **R11 (clock-aware potential Φ, FUMBBL-fit win-prob)** and is its strongest corpus endorsement. The possession annuity (live `reward_possession 0.03`) is the zero-sum-symmetric partial version; corpus implies R11 (margin×clock-aware, NOT symmetric) is the real target — directly relevant to the D112 mirror-stall the pressure test flagged.

9. **Skill-value hierarchy / removal-snowball.** CORROBORATED + EXTENDED with skill-conditional targeting numbers. "Snipe the high-mobility POSITIONALS (Wights/Ghouls/Gutter Runners), NOT the high-Str Mummies — kill their maneuver, not their muscle" (#10 07:40 "don't get obsessed with Mummies; Wights and Ghouls are the stars"; #26; #31 03:30 "target the Claw players every turn, and remove low-AV non-Regen support"). Quantitative skill-conditional EV: Frenzy vs a Dodge target raises knockdown from 55%→80% IF assists are cancelled first (#26 08:41); a Claw block breaks AV10 Mummy armor on a flat 8+ (#26 33:57); MB density "34 MB blocks → 9 removals" (#16 38:00). This is the `k_value` (price-weighted attrition, `def_cost_k/100`) story — but the corpus says removal value is about SKILLS/ROLE (mobility, Claw-matchups), which gold-cost only partially proxies. EXTENDS toward a skill-aware (not just cost-aware) `k_value`.

### Part B — D119's three findings

- **D119(1) passing precondition-chain ("get the ball to the Thrower first").** CORROBORATED but with a DECISIVE CAVEAT that downgrades passing's importance in BB2025. The corpus repeatedly notes **passing is largely DEAD in current rules**: "Under BB2020 rules, passing stats are decoupled from agility, making vanity passing without a dedicated thrower highly risky and non-viable" (#01 22:46). Real games are won by RUNNING the ball in a cage/screen; passes appear only as (a) safe SPP-farm patty-cake when the ball is 100% secure (#02 33:55, #06 00:57), or (b) desperation end-of-half plays at ~20–36% (#01 20:30, #09 20:19). The "get the ball to the right carrier" theme IS real but is about HANDOFFS to a Str-4/scoring piece and "score with the right player" (#13 Tip 3, #08 17:34, #18, #22/#29 17:34 — "score with a Chaos Warrior to buy Block, not the Beastman"), NOT downfield passing. **Implication: the D119(1) "pass needs a Catcher pre-positioned" precondition-chain is a real human pattern but a LOW-VALUE target in BB2025; the handoff-to-the-right-player version is the live one, and our `reward_ball_gain` skill-agnosticism (D119-1's code finding) bites on handoffs/score-selection more than on passes.**

- **D119(2) the formation problem (off-ball positioning is reward-neutral).** CORROBORATED — this is the LARGEST gap the corpus exposes. A huge fraction of every pack is off-ball shape: screens, cages, spreads, sweepers, Guard-walls, lane-coverage, "safe corner" positioning (#26 43:48 — overlap opponents' threat-grids to find the unreachable corner and park the carrier there). All of it is reward-neutral at the moment it happens under the current ball/carrier-centric economy. The R-memo's stated ANSWER is the **R6/R7/R8 settled-turn-end exposure trio (carrier-exposure, conceded-2D, surf-zone)** — formation-as-FUNCTION, not formation-as-shape (memo line 80 explicitly refuses shape templates; line 67 "goal-side containment" is a flagged last-resort). The corpus VALIDATES that the underlying invariant ("min dodges for an opponent to reach the carrier") is what coaches actually compute, so R6 is well-targeted. This is the cleanest "should-be-a-reward-term" finding and it already has a designed-but-unbuilt home.

- **D119(3) pickup risk should be skill-conditional.** PARTIALLY CORROBORATED, with a strong REFRAME. The corpus barely discusses contested PICKUP-roll selection (because expert play AVOIDS contested pickups: **"don't attempt a risky 4+ pickup in tackle zones — just stand a tackle-zone ON the loose ball and make the OPPONENT roll the bad odds,"** #02 12:45, #06 08:33). The corpus's actual loose-ball doctrine is bigger than pickup-AG: **"When the ball is on the floor, the focus HAS to be on that — every action dedicated to securing or screening it; no greedy blocks elsewhere"** (#26 19:48, a hard-stated rule). And **"design the turn so the FAIL STATE is acceptable: set screens BEFORE rolling the risky pickup so a failure leaves the ball protected"** (#26 21:56, #01 22:46 fail-safe spacing, #08 27:15 "air gap"). So D119(3)'s "send the Sure-Hands/AG4 player" is real but secondary; the dominant heuristic is "loose ball = drop everything + pre-screen the fail-state." Neither is representable today (the obs-v4 plane question from D119(3) is still open and worth the quick code-read).

### Part C — GENUINELY NEW findings (not in pressure test or R-memo's main list)

- **N1. "Minimize dice rolled per turn" as a first-class objective.** #26 26:46 states it as a rule: "Frenzy forces a 2nd block, DOUBLING your turnover chance — if you don't NEED the 2nd block, use a plain Block player instead. Minimize the number of dice rolled per turn." Echoed #06 04:08 ("roll the absolute minimum dice to make the ball unsackable"), #26 23:27. This is subtly DIFFERENT from sequencing (R1) and reckless-block (R5): it's about not taking OPTIONAL successful-looking actions at all. R5 partially prices it (each extra block pays its own p_turnover) but the Frenzy-specific "second forced block" is a concrete sub-case. Candidate: a Frenzy-aware tweak to R5, or just confirm R5's per-block charge already covers it.

- **N2. "Safe corner" / threat-grid-overlap parking.** #26 43:48: click each opponent, union their movement+blitz threat ranges, find the square no opponent can reach, run the carrier there. This is the *positive* construction whose *negative* is R6 (carrier-exposure). Strongly suggests the obs-v4 should expose a per-acting-player "min-opponent-reach" / threat-union plane if it doesn't already — ties directly to D119(3)'s open obs-v4 question.

- **N3. Wizard/positional-hazard clustering (out of current scope but flagged).** Repeated across #01, #08, #09, #10, #14, #16, #29, #31: don't clump ≥3 players (Fireball template), don't carry near the sideline (Lightning-Bolt-into-surf), keep the carrier deep when the opponent holds a Wizard, push the ball into the OPPONENT's half early so a bolt-drop can't be converted to a defensive TD (#31 02:10). Inducements/wizards aren't in our engine's training scope yet (CLAUDE.md tasks 23–24), so this is a FUTURE curriculum note, not a near-term term.

- **N4. "Activate volatile players EARLY."** #31 05:40: activate Big Guys / Really-Stupid / Bonehead pieces early in the turn on non-critical actions, so if they fail you can still re-plan the turn to cover the gap. A turn-ordering nuance ORTHOGONAL to risk-sequencing (it's about information-revelation timing, not turnover-exposure). Hard to price cleanly; a BC/demo-bank pattern.

- **N5. "Mini-games" board decomposition + "two dice on the ball" puzzle framing.** #26 05:11, #31 14:10, #32 — experts decompose the pitch into independent zones and treat "how do I get 2 dice on the carrier" as the recurring core puzzle. This is a STATE-REPRESENTATION / curriculum hint (the demo bank could over-sample "2-dice-on-the-carrier-available" states), not a reward term.

- **N6. Kickoff sweeper/safety discipline.** #08 21:02, #22 20:31, #29 20:31 — leaving the backfield empty on a receiving setup is a recurring blunder punished by Blitz!/deep-kick. The R-memo argues the critic should learn this via R6/ball-loss back-propagating to the setup action (memo §5), rather than a hard "sweeper" reward. Corpus agrees it's a setup-phase consequence, but it's worth a CANARY (track empty-backfield setups vs Blitz!-conceded-TDs).

### Part D — prioritized next-experiment candidates (given pressure-test + D117-A caveat + this corpus)

Ranked by (corpus corroboration strength) × (cheapness/representability) × (NOT-already-stale-per-D117-A):

1. **R6 (carrier-exposure, min-dodges-to-reach == 0/marked, −0.05, endzone-dash-exempt) — BUILD IT.** This is the single highest-value candidate: it is the formation-problem (D119-2) answer, the cage/screen corroboration (Part-A 2/4) target, the "safe corner" positive's negative (N2), the leading indicator of the −0.5 sack (fixes credit assignment a full turn earlier), and — critically — it is NOT touched by the D117-A "D46 is resolved" caveat (it prices POSITIONING, not gfi/dodge volume). The R-memo already specs it as the priority of its positional trio and it reuses the existing possession-knob settled-turn hook. Cheapest high-impact build in the set. A/B vs the league6 lineage; canary = sack-rate-against (should fall), stall-length, contact-rate.

2. **R11 (clock-aware potential Φ from FUMBBL win-prob) — DESIGN/FIT next.** The tempo/Turn-8-stall doctrine is the most universal theme in the corpus (every replay pack) and directly addresses the D112 mirror-stall the pressure test attributed to the symmetric possession annuity. It's heavier (needs the FUMBBL-corpus win-prob fit, must retire or decouple the possession feature to avoid double-count) so it's phase-2, but it's the principled fix for "the annuity is zero-sum-symmetric." Also unaffected by the D46 caveat.

3. **Extend k_seq to dodge/GFI/pickup declarations (the pressure-test #1 gap) — DO, but DEMOTE in urgency per D117-A.** The corpus' strongest, most-repeated single lesson IS risk-sequencing (Part-A 1), and the code gap is real (`k_seq` block-only, verified). BUT D117-A shows all three current arms already run gfi/dodge AT-OR-BELOW human — the pathology this was meant to cure appears gone in the league6 lineage. So: keep it queued as a CHEAP knob-extension A/B (it's the same `pending_safe_activations` machinery the block path already has), but it is no longer the #1 fire — run it AFTER R6, and gate the decision on whether a fresh tournament (D109-A) shows the current lineage actually plays sequencing-clean or just gfi-quiet. If gfi/dodge stay human-like without it, this is a no-op and the discriminator (D46) says don't add scaffolding for a non-problem.

Deliberately NOT recommended as near-term reward terms (corpus-confirmed as value-net / curriculum jobs, not per-step rewards): reroll-budgeting beyond R9 (Part-A 7), passing precondition-chains (Part-B D119-1, low-value in BB2025), wizard-clustering (N3, out of engine scope). Crowd-surf terms (`surf_*`) are already CODED — flipping them on is a separate cheap A/B if removal-via-surf is judged under-explored, but they're default-off by design and the corpus treats surfing as opportunistic, not foundational.

UNCERTAIN / for the lead to sanity-check: (i) several packs (#08, #22, #29) analyze the SAME Chaos-vs-Skaven game — corroboration "across packs" there is partly the same source video, so weight it as one observation, not three. (ii) #29's own header flags a title/transcript mismatch (labeled Amazons-vs-DarkElf, content is the Chaos-Skaven game) — I cited its content as-is. (iii) I did not independently re-derive the R-memo's claim that R6–R8 reuse an existing settled-turn hook cleanly — that's the memo's assertion; verify the hook before scoping the R6 build. (iv) the D119(3) obs-v4 question (are probability/threat planes per-ACTING-player or generic?) remains open and is a prerequisite for both N2 and any skill-conditional-pickup work — still worth the quick code-read flagged in D119.**

**D120 — RECONCILIATION: codex + Opus pressure-test + D117-A + D121, final prioritized verdict (research, 2026-06-15).** Two independent code-level reviews (Opus, recorded inline this session; codex, `.codex-reviews/d119-article-pressure-test.md`, ~2h runtime) both audited the reward economy against the same 9-principle article. AGREEMENT is strong on STRUCTURE: both confirm `k_seq` is block-declarations-only (codex: extend to `BB_A_STEP`/dodge/GFI/pickup/catch/pass/handoff, skill-aware, as "the most promising reward-side fix for D46"); both confirm formation/caging/screening has NO representation and that a simple scalar reward is the WRONG tool for it (Opus: "needs new machinery, a formation-shape potential"; codex independently: "likely needs BC anchoring, demo-bank curricula, or auxiliary imitation targets... brittle and team-style dependent" -- codex arrived at the SAME "this isn't a reward-knob problem" conclusion via a different route); both confirm skill-agnostic ball-acquisition explains D119's passing gap; both confirm re-roll management is NOT a per-step-reward problem (codex: "needs decision-time EV or learned/imitation priors that understand board context").

CODEX'S ONE GENUINELY NEW FINDING (not in Opus's pass or D119/D121): **checked-in `puffer/config/bloodbowl.ini` defaults do not reflect the actual D90-settled-v4 economy** -- the real economy only exists as CLI overrides baked into launch scripts (`run_native_asym.sh`'s trailing-args pattern, etc.). Anyone reading the ini file gets a misleading picture of "almost everything disabled." Codex ranks this #1 by tractability (cheapest fix) -- a config-hygiene/documentation gap, not a behavioral one, but worth closing so the next person (or agent) doesn't reason from the wrong baseline. CHEAP FOLLOW-UP, not done in this entry: add a comment block to `bloodbowl.ini` documenting the settled-v4 override set and pointing at a live launch script as the source of truth.

THE ONE REAL PRIORITY DIVERGENCE, and why D117-A resolves it: codex's bottom line (written WITHOUT knowledge of D117-A, which landed after codex was dispatched) was "attack movement-risk sequencing [k_seq extension] and tempo/possession FIRST... treat passing and formations as a bigger design problem." This matches what Opus's pass ALSO said before D117-A. But D117-A's empirical finding -- all three of TD-maniac/stakes1/statmatch1/2 now run gfi/dodge AT-OR-BELOW human, reversing D46 -- pulls the rug out from under "k_seq-extension fixes D46" as the #1 move, because the D46 pathology it targets may already be gone in the current (league5/6/6b-descended) lineage. D121 (the AndyDavo corpus synthesis, which DID have D117-A's context) reached the same conclusion independently: demote k_seq-extension to AFTER the formation term, gated on a fresh tournament confirming D46 is actually resolved (not just gfi-quiet for other reasons).

**FINAL CONSENSUS VERDICT (4-way: Opus, codex, D117-A empirical, D121 corpus)**:
1. **R6 (carrier-exposure/formation term, per `docs/reward-design-coaching-wisdom.md`)** -- the formation gap is the ONE thing all four analyses independently flag as both real AND not addressable by a coefficient tweak, and D121's corpus grounding (caging/screening dominate the AndyDavo corpus) plus its "untouched by the D46 caveat" property make it the clear #1. R6's hook (settled-own-turn-end, same as the possession annuity) is VERIFIED to exist and be reusable this session; the new piece is a BFS "min-dodges for any opponent to reach the carrier" routine. This is real engine work (new C code + reward hook), not a knob A/B -- needs a design/implementation pass, likely codex-implementer per the standing pattern, with Claude architecting the BFS spec first.
2. **R11 (clock-aware tempo potential)** -- addresses D112's mirror-stall directly (the possession annuity's zero-sum-symmetry is the agreed root cause across Opus/codex/D121); heavier (needs FUMBBL win-prob fit), phase-2.
3. **k_seq extension to movement rolls** -- real gap, both code reviews agree it's "the" fix for D46-as-originally-stated, but DEMOTED behind 1-2 pending a fresh tournament confirming whether D46 still applies to the current lineage. If it doesn't, this becomes a no-op per D46's own "discovery vs artifact" discriminator (don't patch a non-problem).
4. **Codex's config-hygiene fix** (ini defaults vs actual economy) -- cheap, independent of 1-3, do whenever convenient.

NOT recommended as reward terms (4-way agreement): re-roll management, basing/tie-up value-trades, passing preconditions beyond skill-conditional ball_gain -- all flagged as curriculum/BC-anchoring/value-network territory by at least 2 of the 4 analyses.

This closes the pressure-test thread opened earlier this session (Alex's "Andy Davo... pressure test with codex and opus agent" request) -- D119 through D121 plus this entry form a complete, cross-validated research package. NEXT ACTION (not started): the D109-A ladder-extension tournament (queued, both Vast boxes free) should ALSO serve as the "fresh tournament" gate for item 3 above -- if it confirms gfi/dodge remain human-like under tournament conditions (not just self-play training dashboards), item 3 can be deprioritized with more confidence.**
