The 8 pre-existing anchors barely moved (<=4 Elo, all within noise) -- the fit is stable and the new nodes slot in cleanly.

**(a) DID LEAGUE6B (warm=gen3) JUMP LIKE LEAGUE6/LEAGUE5 DID? -- QUALIFIED YES.** league6b climbed from gen3's +95.8 to **+156.6 (a +60.8 Elo jump)**, landing clearly ABOVE the gen2/gen3 tier1-cluster (beats gen3 0.555, gen2 0.555, league1 0.570 H2H). So the D111 hard-opponents recipe DOES generalize across starting lineages -- it is NOT specific to league4's particular state, answering D109-A's central question affirmatively. **BUT the magnitude is starting-state-dependent:** league6b (+156.6) lands ~43 Elo BELOW league5 (+199.6, loses 0.461 H2H) and ~92 below league6 (+248.3, loses 0.452 H2H), and its +60.8 jump is roughly half league5's original +116.8 from league4. So: the recipe ratchets from any reasonable starting point, but starts that are already higher/more-refined (league4->league5->league6) ratchet harder than the gen3 lineage. The causal hypothesis (tier1-in-pool drives gains) is CONFIRMED and broadly generalizes; league5's record jump was amplified by, but not solely caused by, league4's specific state.

**(b) WHERE DO LEAGUE6 AND THE THREE REWARD PROBES LAND?** league6 (+248.3) is the strongest fully-trained checkpoint -- the league5->league6 continuation jumped another +48.7 Elo, confirming the recipe keeps ratcheting and crowning league6 the new best NON-reward-probe node. The three reward probes all landed HIGH: tdmaniac1 +215.6 (#3 overall), stakes1 +190.5 (#5), and the headline -- statmatch1 +326.5 is the NEW ALL-TIME LADDER #1 despite only 5B steps (vs league6's 28B). statmatch1 beats every opponent decisively and consistently (league5 0.543, league6 0.513, tdmaniac1 0.553, stakes1 0.600, and >=0.68 vs everything gen3-and-below) -- this is NOT a weak-opponent BT artifact, it wins the top-cluster H2Hs outright. The aggregate-stat-matching reward (D114-A) is the single strongest lever yet measured. CAVEAT on statmatch1's #1: it is a 5B probe warm-started from league5, and its lopsided wins vs the degenerate floor (bc_v4 0.883, v5contested 0.900) do inflate its BT raw_strength; treat "#1" as "clearly top-tier and the most promising reward direction," not a precise +127-over-league6 gap. statmatch2 (D118-A, the rebalanced-stds continuation on the rig) is the proper follow-up and should be laddered next when it caps.

**(c) ELO/TOURNAMENT vs D117-A TRAINING-DASHBOARD RANKING -- THEY AGREE on the reward probes, with one twist.** D117-A's self-play dashboard tds ranked statmatch1 (1.325) > stakes1 (1.042) ~ tdmaniac1 (1.016). The tournament Elo ranks statmatch1 (+326.5) > tdmaniac1 (+215.6) > stakes1 (+190.5). Both agree statmatch1 is the clear best of the three -- and the tournament VALIDATES the dashboard's statmatch1 signal that D117-A itself flagged as confounded (different warm-start/steps). The twist: dashboard had stakes1 ~ tdmaniac1 (tds tie), tournament cleanly separates tdmaniac1 above stakes1 -- consistent with D107-A's standing doctrine (ladder/tournament > self-play dashboards; in-run tds is not a reliable strength proxy). Per D107-A, WHERE THEY DIVERGE WE TRUST THE TOURNAMENT: tdmaniac1 > stakes1. No probe-vs-probe contradiction large enough to overturn the headline. (Note all three probes were trained frozen-self/no-D111-pool, so their high ladder placement is doubly notable -- they beat the pool-trained league5/league6b without the hard-opponents pool, purely on the reward change + their league5/6/6b warm-start.)

**(d) D111 POOL-COMPOSITION RECOMMENDATION UPDATED -- the ladder-top changed completely.** Re-ran `tools/build_pool_from_ladder.py` against the updated CSV+registry. NEW 8-bank pool: FLOOR=gen1 (+0.0); TIER1={statmatch1 +326.5, league6 +248.3, tdmaniac1 +215.6}; TIER2={league5 +199.6, stakes1 +190.5, league6b +156.6}; DIVERSITY={exploiter1 +58.7}. The gen2/gen3 cluster that anchored league5/6/6b's pools is now DISPLACED out of the top-6 entirely by the league6-lineage + reward probes -- the hard-opponents core is fully refreshed, exactly as D111's "refresh every generation as the ladder-top changes" doctrine prescribes. WARM-START: the builder auto-recommends statmatch1 (highest Elo), but for a STANDARD next-generation continuation the safer champion is **league6 (+248.3, the strongest fully-trained 28B non-probe checkpoint)** -- statmatch1 is a 5B probe with a confounded #1 (caveat above) and its real value is as evidence to PROMOTE the aggregate-stat-matching reward (now the top open lever), not necessarily as a warm-start. Recommended next league (league7): warm=league6, pool=the new TIER1/TIER2 set above. Separately, statmatch's strength elevates the aggregate-stat-matching reward to a primary experimental lever (was D113's queued parallel track) -- ladder statmatch2 when it caps, and consider folding the statmatch reward into the league7 economy.

**D46/k_seq GATE (the "fresh tournament" D120/D121 asked for):** This tournament is the gate. (iii) reward probes used different warm-starts (statmatch1<-league5, tdmaniac1<-league6, stakes1<-league6b) and step counts (5B/15B/15B), so the probe-internal ordering partly reflects warm-start strength, not purely the reward change -- a clean single-variable reward read would need matched warm-starts.**

**D123 — R6 REFINEMENT (Alex, 2026-06-15): graduated + adversarial exposure, staged as v1/v1.5/v2 in `docs/reward-design-coaching-wisdom.md`.** Before any R6 implementation starts (R6 was just identified as the 4-way pressure-test consensus #1, D120), Alex flagged that the table-row spec (binary "0-dodges-or-marked = -0.05") is too coarse in two ways:

(1) **Dodge-count isn't binary risk** -- "you can position a player so someone needs ONE dodge to get to you, and that's fine [relatively]. That's objectively worse than THREE dodges, or needing multiple GFIs." 1-dodge, 3-dodge, and GFI-gated access represent very different P(opponent actually converts the threat this turn) -- compounding independent-roll failure probabilities, plus GFI paths carry the ATTACKER's own turnover risk too. **R6v1.5** (addendum, same BFS as v1, richer scoring): price `-scale * P(best opponent reaches+dislodges carrier this turn)` using the SAME probability-pricing philosophy as `k_kd`/`k_value`/`k_ball`, replacing hand-picked dodge-count tiers with a continuous probability. Reproduces Alex's ordering naturally (0-dodge >> 1-dodge > 3-dodge > GFI-gated ~ 0).

(2) **Screeners are displaceable, not fixed obstacles** -- Alex's example: a single Dodge-skill Halfling "providing" a 1-dodge buffer for a ball carrier, standing next to a Block/Mighty-Blow/Grab Chaos Warrior about to throw 3 red dice. "You're not actually safe -- he's just getting displaced." VERIFIED in code: `BB_SK_GRAB` (`proc_block.c:447`) cancels the defender's Side Step, so a Grab attacker CHOOSES the push direction -- can deliberately clear the screener out of the lane. v1/v1.5's BFS treats friendly pieces as fixed obstacles; the TRUE exposure when a screener is one good block away from being cleared is much higher than the nominal dodge-count suggests. **R6v2** (addendum, a separate later iteration): for screeners whose removal would reduce `min_dodges`, run the existing `bb_blockev` routine on their adjacent opponents to fold `P(screener cleared) * P(then reach carrier)` into the exposure. Genuinely harder (1-ply lookahead, different timing than k_kd's block-declaration hook) -- ship with its own canary (does the v1.5 policy rely on screens a competent opponent would blow through? divergence between priced-exposure and actual sack rate is the trip-wire).

STAGING: v1 ships first per D120/the R-memo's A/B-3 (unchanged -- it IS Alex's "first thing: make it so no dodges can get you"). v1.5 is a low-risk in-place refinement (same BFS, different scoring fn) once v1's canaries are read. v2 is gated on evidence, not built speculatively. Full technical detail in `docs/reward-design-coaching-wisdom.md`'s new "R6 refinement" subsection (inserted between R6's and R7's implementation sketches).**

**D123-A — R6 spec corrected (v1: dual dodge/GFI counters) + R6v2 reframed around per-screener "fragility" to tame the combinatorial-displacement problem (Alex, 2026-06-15).** Both edits landed directly in `docs/reward-design-coaching-wisdom.md` (the R6/R6-refinement sections), this entry records the WHY.

**v1 correction (folded into R6's table row + sketch, not a new version)**: the original BFS labeled GFI-only squares as "free" (non-dodge), so a path needing 0 dodges but 1+ GFIs scored `min_dodges==0` -- the SAME full -0.05 as a true free walk-up. This is backwards from Alex's stated minimum bar: *"make them dodge to get to you, OR make them GFI to get to you -- do those things at a minimum."* Fix: BFS now tracks `(min_dodges, min_gfis)` as two counters; "free walk-up" (full -0.05) requires BOTH zero. One-line change to edge-cost bookkeeping, but load-bearing -- without it v1 doesn't actually implement what was asked.

**v2 reframed**: Alex correctly identified that the original v2 sketch (Grab lets the attacker choose the push square) is only ONE of FOUR ways a screener stops being an obstacle: (a) even non-Grab pushes have up to 3 attacker-chosen destination squares; (b) Blitz changes the attack angle, rotating which 3 squares those are; (c) Frenzy forces recursive follow-up blocks, each with its own (a)+(b) branching; (d) a no-push knockdown (Both Down/Defender Down) leaves the screener prone IN PLACE, removing its TZ without any push geometry. The cross-product is exponential -- "a really big exploding combinatorial problem" as stated.

THE REFRAME (avoids enumeration entirely): compute, once per screener, a single scalar `fragility = P(this piece stops projecting a TZ on the relevant square this turn, via knockdown-in-place OR being pushed off, vs its single best CURRENT adjacent threat)` -- reusing the existing per-pair `bb_blockev` math (same inputs as k_kd/k_value/k_ball, no new EV engine). Feed `fragility` into the BFS as a CONTINUOUS edge-cost (fragile screener ~ free square; solid screener ~ full obstacle) rather than enumerating where pieces end up. This is "is this obstacle solid" as ONE NUMBER from EXISTING machinery.

SPLIT: **v2a** (shippable) = fragility restricted to current adjacency, covers (a)+(d) -- already catches Alex's literal Halfling/Chaos-Warrior example (Warrior is already adjacent, no repositioning needed to matter). **v2b** (research, not scoped) = folding in (b) Blitz-angle + (c) Frenzy-chains -- if ever needed, via SAMPLING (Monte Carlo rollouts a la `tools/blockev_mc.c`), not exact enumeration, and only if v2a's canary proves insufficient (a SECOND, more specific trip-wire than v2's general one).

STAGING UNCHANGED: v1 (corrected) ships first, unblocked by any of this -- it IS "make them dodge or GFI to get to you, at minimum." v1.5 and v2a/v2b remain staged refinements per D123.**

**D124 — LAUNCH DECISION: league7 + league7b, applying D111's refreshed pool + D122's verdict.** Per D111's doctrine ("at every new cap, extend the ladder and refit BEFORE deciding the next launch... warm-start = current ladder-top"), D122 gave a refreshed 8-bank pool: TIER1={statmatch1 +326.5, league6 +248.3, tdmaniac1 +215.6}, TIER2={league5 +199.6, stakes1 +190.5, league6b +156.6}, DIVERSITY={exploiter1 +58.7}, FLOOR={gen1 0.0}. **D126 — R6v1 ARCHITECTURE RECONCILED: no blocker, revision pass applied, implementation-ready (Opus architect + Opus review + Codex review + lead review, 2026-06-15).** Three independent reviews of `.codex-impl/brief-r6v1-carrier-exposure.md` converge:

**Priority item (the `p->moved` reset-timing question) is CLEARED, 3-way confirmed.** Codex's trace is the most precise: `turn_start` for the about-to-act team `1-t` (resetting `moved=0`/`rushes=0`, `proc_turn.c:9,23`) runs INSIDE the same `bb_advance` loop that processed team `t`'s turn-end, BEFORE `bb_advance` returns control to Puffer (`bb_match.c:255`, `proc_match.c:56-63`, `proc_turn.c:101-122`) -- so by the time the settled-turn-end hook (`bloodbowl.h:1894`) observes the flip, `1-t`'s `moved`/`rushes` are ALREADY zeroed. `budget = p->ma - p->moved == p->ma` holds. (Codex's residual note: if the engine ever auto-settles through MULTIPLE turn-flips before the next decision, this hook-style hits an EXISTING `reward_possession`-class limitation, not R6-specific -- out of scope.)

**BONUS FINDING (Opus): `bbe_macro_reach` (`bloodbowl.h:794-867`) already exists** -- a proven 2D Dijkstra over the pitch (movement budget, obstacles via `m->grid`, dodge-on-exit, GFI boundary), built for v5 path-actions. Resolves the spec's proposed 3D `(x,y,squares_used)` state space (use 2D, matching this precedent) AND Q5 (Sprint via `bb_max_rushes`, `bb_skills.c:11-13`, already exists).

**CONCRETE FIXES (revision appendix added to the spec, §8) -- all SMALL, none requires re-architecture:**
1. File references: `bb_types.h`/`bb_match.h`, not `bb_state.h` (doesn't exist) -- codex.
2. **SIGN BUG (codex catch, real)**: spec's `-0.05` example + `-=` sketch double-negates = REWARDS exposure. Fix: positive magnitudes (`reward_carrier_exposure = 0.05`), subtracted -- matches `reward_rush_cost` exactly.
3. **AGGREGATION BUG (codex catch, real)**: §1.4's "lex-min `(dodges,gfis)` across opponents, then threshold" can hide a different opponent's `{1,0}` (one-dodge, soft-tier) behind another opponent's `{0,2}` (zero-dodge-two-GFI, lex-smaller, scores as "safe" under thresholding). Fix: compute boolean ORs across opponents -- `any_free = OR(dodges==0 && gfis==0)`, `any_one_roll = OR(dodges+gfis==1)` -- then `full = marked || any_free`, `soft = !full && any_one_roll`. Replaces the single-lex-min-then-threshold aggregation.
4. Q8 extended (codex): exclude ROOTED opponents from the BFS-movers list too (`can_step` already rejects `BB_PF_ROOTED`, `proc_move.c:45`), not just the carrier's exemption -- rooted-but-adjacent opponents still mark via the unchanged `bb_is_marked` short-circuit.
5. Architecture: `bb_reachability.c` lives in `engine/` (Opus's testability rationale) but MUST be added to Puffer's engine-amalgamation include list (`bloodbowl.h:61` directly includes engine `.c` files -- codex's catch, the spec omitted this wiring step). Core algorithm adapted from `bbe_macro_reach`'s proven 2D approach (Opus).
6. Q3: carrier's endzone-exemption budget = `ma + bb_max_rushes(m, carrier)` (Sprint-aware, both reviewers converged here independently), gated on `!BB_PF_ROOTED` (Q8).
7. Q1 (`is_blitz`): keep dropped from v1's compute (Opus's "free adjacent access" reading matches §0's literal text), but RENAME the metric/comments away from "sack threat"/"blitz threat" framing to avoid implying blitz-cost semantics codex's reading would require -- documentation-only, no logic change.
8. Add a downed/prone-carrier test case (symmetric to the marked-opponent prone case) -- Opus.
9. Telemetry: `ep_carrier_exposed_full/soft` -- unanimous yes, capacity headroom confirmed (~36-37/64 keys used).
10. Fix the "tight cage" test case (codex): all-8-adjacent-occupied = UNREACHABLE, not "must dodge" -- use occupied corners + open-but-TZ'd adjacent squares to test the dodge-cost path.

**VERDICT**: implementation-ready after these 10 fixes (applied as a revision appendix to the spec, not a rewrite). Next: codex-implementer build per the standing pattern, GPU-decoupled (doesn't compete with league7/league7b/statmatch2). Separately: the BBTV/seconds0.com security-review codex job (D125-adjacent) was killed after 80+ min with zero output (past the 35min ceiling, unlike this thread's codex which completed cleanly in ~25min) -- Opus's completed security review (SAFE to publish, only LOW findings) stands as the verdict; codex was non-cooperative on THAT task specifically, consistent with the prior session's note that codex's unproductiveness is task-specific, not categorical.**

**D127 — R6v1 IMPLEMENTATION COMPLETE (codex implementer, 2026-06-15): 361 tests pass, puffer-side wired, defaulting to 0.0 (inert to current runs).** Dispatched codex from `.codex-impl/brief-r6v1-carrier-exposure.md` (the D126-revised spec). Output log at `.codex-impl/r6v1-implementation.log` (31,857 lines). All 10 revision-appendix fixes applied cleanly in the implementation:

**Engine (commits `127ab51` + `322444f`, 478 lines across 6 files):**
- `engine/src/bb_reachability.c` + `engine/include/bb/bb_reachability.h`: pure-engine 8-connected 2D Dijkstra adapted from `bbe_macro_reach`'s proven algorithm (no `Bloodbowl*`, no env coupling, no caching). Per-node `(dodges, gfis)` cost tracked via `reach_len`; dodge counted on exit via `bb_tackle_zones`; GFI boundary from budget (`ma + bb_max_rushes`); `BB_PF_ROOTED` gates both the carrier and reaching opponents. Aggregation via boolean ORs (`any_free`, `any_one_roll`) across standing non-rooted opponents -- avoids the lex-min aggregation bug (D126 fix #3).
- `engine/tests/test_reachability.c`: 15 tests (open-field, tight-screened, marked carrier, one-dodge soft, one-GFI soft, aggregation regression, unreachable, endzone exemption, Sprint-aware, rooted adjacent/non-adjacent, prone opponent, diagonal adjacency, prone carrier guard).
- `bb_carrier_exposure_eval` pure-engine classifier + endzone-exemption helper exposed for direct testability from the Mac suite.

**Puffer wiring (`puffer/bloodbowl/bloodbowl.h`, `binding.c`, `puffer/config/bloodbowl.ini`):**
- Fields `reward_carrier_exposure` + `reward_carrier_exposure_soft`, both defaulting to `0.0` (fully backward-compatible with all current runs). Applied at the settled own-turn-end hook (after possession bookkeeping), one-sided penalty only (no opponent credit).
- `bb_reachability.c` added to the puffer amalgamation with its own `DIR8_reachability_tu` rename block; amalgamation comment updated.
- Telemetry keys `ep_carrier_exposed_full` and `ep_carrier_exposed_soft` in the log dict (capacity 38 keys).

**Verification (Mac):** `make test` → 361 tests, 0 failures. Reachability slice: 15/15. `make lockstep` → clean build. Binding syntax check → clean. Snapshot drift check shows stale vendor copy (expected -- run `install_puffer_env.sh` on boxes before next build).

**Sign convention (D126 fix #2 applied correctly):** positive magnitudes in config, subtracted in hook -- matches `reward_rush_cost` convention. Codex's sign-double-negate bug from the original spec does NOT appear in the implementation.

Also confirmed: opponents' reach fields use full MA (turn_start reset their `moved` before the hook observes the flip — D126's budget assumption); rooted carrier AND rooted opponents excluded; hook is one-sided with full-precedence-over-soft; early-out at `bb_min_access_cost:120` bounds the per-turn Dijkstra cost (watch league8's SPS vs league7 anyway — up to 11 reach-field recomputes per turn-flip is the one perf risk if it bites). Implementation is launch-ready as-is; no changes needed.**

**D128 — D124 A/B VERDICT (head-to-head, 2026-06-15): proven economy (league7b) BEATS statmatch-continued (league7) at matched 30B + same pool.** Both arms capped cleanly at 30.0B (league7 ~18:55 PDT, league7b ~19:22 PDT), both backed up to B2 (`league7_cap.bin`, `league7b_cap.bin`) and staged on japan. Ran the head-to-head on japan's judge GPU (`puffer match bloodbowl --load-model-path league7_cap.bin --load-enemy-model-path league7b_cap.bin --num-games 4096`): **`A=0.464 B=0.536 draw=0.460`** (A=league7=statmatch-continued, B=league7b=proven-economy). Score-style (half-draws split, the pufferl winrate convention): league7b 0.536 vs league7 0.464. Decisive-only: total decisive = 0.54, league7b won 0.306/0.54 = **56.7%** vs league7 0.234/0.54 = **43.3%**.

INTERPRETATION: this answers D124's question directionally — **the aggregate-stat-matching reward did NOT compound with the D111 pool lever; the settled v4 economy (possession annuity + k-half + dist potentials) is the stronger CONTINUED-training signal.** The conclusion is *strengthened* by the warm-start confound cutting AGAINST it: league7 warm-started from statmatch1 (D122 ladder #1, +326.5) — the HIGHER-rated checkpoint — while league7b warm-started from league6 (#2, +248.3), yet league7b still won. So statmatch1's D122 #1 placement was most likely a fresh-perturbation/measurement artifact (D122's own "soft #1" flag: 5B vs 15-28B, lopsided floor-node wins) rather than the statmatch reward producing a durably stronger policy. Statmatch as a one-shot perturbation reward may still have value; statmatch as a continued-training objective does not beat the proven economy here.

CAVEATS (this is PRELIMINARY pending confirmation): (i) single head-to-head, n=4096 games but 46% draws → decisive n≈2200, so the 56.7/43.3 split has real but not overwhelming separation; (ii) no full-ladder Elo yet — league7/league7b haven't been round-robined against the anchor set, so their absolute ladder positions (and whether league7b is the new #1) are unconfirmed; (iii) warm-start + reward differ together (not a single-variable isolation), though the confound direction strengthens rather than threatens the conclusion. A Codex review of this verdict + a full anchored-ladder extension (round-robin both new caps vs anchors on japan/2070) are the confirmation steps before D128 is treated as final. Per CLAUDE.md, the verdict is NOT yet a ship recommendation — but it does not block league8, which tests R6v1 on the proven economy regardless of the statmatch comparison.**

**D128-A — CODEX REVIEW of D128: H2H win is real, but the CAUSAL claim is not proven and "statmatch-reward is dead" is PREMATURE (2026-06-15, `.codex-reviews/d128-verdict-review.md`).** Read + accepted. Codex agrees the head-to-head result is statistically solid (league7b beats league7 with confidence) and that the proven v4 economy is the correct DEFAULT mainline (so league8's economy choice stands). But it correctly tempers three things D128 over-stated:

1. **The warm-start "confound strengthens the conclusion" argument is WEAKER than D128 claimed.** D128 argued league7 losing despite warm-starting from the higher-rated statmatch1 (#1) is evidence AGAINST statmatch. Codex's correction: *starting Elo is not a sufficient control for CONTINUATION potential* — a checkpoint can be higher-rated yet have less headroom to improve under further training. So league7's loss is "additional negative evidence for this exact recipe" but does NOT eliminate the warm-start confound. Compounding this: D122's league6 was a 28.03B checkpoint (the D116 KeyError ate ~2B); if the missing 2B would have raised league6, then "statmatch1 was the clearly stronger warm-start" is even less secure — which weakens the confound-cuts-against-me argument further, not the H2H itself.

2. **D124-A's "same pool" is only true for the INITIAL preseed banks (pool-drift confound).** The selfplay code uses the preseed dir as the LIVE pool dir, so interval/winrate snapshots accumulate per-arm after launch (`tools/build_league.py`, `training/selfplay_league.patch:17`). league7 and league7b therefore trained against IDENTICAL starting pools but DIVERGING full distributions (each accumulating its own statmatch-/v4-flavored snapshots). Fine for "which full recipe trains better," a real confound for "which reward signal alone is better." (This is the same 25-bank-vs-8-bank issue I noted for league8's pool — the accumulated snapshots, not just the seeds.)

3. **The 2×2 is incomplete — only 2 of 4 corners tested.** D124 tested league6+v4 (=league7b) vs statmatch1+statmatch (=league7) — the diagonal. The missing arms: **league6+statmatch** (isolates the reward change against league7b's OWN warm-start — the single most valuable missing cell) and **statmatch1+v4** (tests whether statmatch1 was a good perturbation worth handing back to the proven economy). Without these, "v4 reward is causally superior to statmatch continuation" is unproven.

REVISED D128 STATUS (per Codex's recommendation, accepted): proven v4 economy / league7b lineage is the default next mainline (unchanged — league8 correct). D128 = **strong negative DIRECTIONAL evidence against the EXACT league7 statmatch-continued recipe**, NOT proof that human-stat-matching rewards are dead as a family (D114/D118-A's formulation is one engineered instance — symmetric, match-level, terminal, non-PBRS, possession-off; a failure has many candidate diagnoses). Also note: "56.7/43.3 decisive" overstates the gap — the score-style 0.536 vs 0.464 (~+25 Elo) is the honest framing for ladder decisions; use that, not the decisive-only split. Confirmation order before any "statmatch continuation is dead" entry: (1) full anchored ladder for league7+league7b incl. the direct row + a reversed-order/fresh-seed H2H rerun as cheap insurance; (2) ladder statmatch2 when it caps (it's the D118-A CORRECTED formulation — the most relevant statmatch data point); (3) train league6+statmatch (matched-warm-start reward isolation); (4) optionally statmatch1+v4. Tasks #53/#54 updated to carry this order.**

**D129 — statmatch2 CAPPED (8.0B) + statmatch-reward convergence read + ladder round-robin LAUNCHED (2026-06-16 ~01:00 PDT).** statmatch2 (rig, the D118-A CORRECTED statmatch formulation, warm=statmatch1, 8B) capped cleanly. Backed up: `statmatch2_cap.bin` → B2 (via japan; rig lacks rclone). **statmatch_term convergence: −0.183 (early) → −0.118 (final)**, ~36% penalty reduction, plateauing at −0.117/−0.118 — so the reward DID pull aggregate stats toward the human baseline, but partially: final stats still show gfi_attempts 20.6 (human 2–5), block_2dred_frac 0.148 (human 0.017), pass_attempts 0.004 (passing essentially absent) — i.e., the L2-norm penalty closed ~⅓ of the gap and stalled, dominated by the dimensions furthest from human (gfi/block). tds 1.599, possession_rate 0.253. The reward works as a soft regularizer toward human stats, not a hard constraint; the residual gfi/block excess is the same artifact the rest of the lineage shows (D46 — unresolved by statmatch alone).

**LADDER ROUND-ROBIN running on the rig** (free since statmatch2 capped): 18 matches, {league7, league7b, statmatch2} × {statmatch1, league6, league5, gen1, exploiter1} + new-internal, 4096 games each (`/tmp/ladder_rr.sh` → `/tmp/ladder_rr.csv`). If the full round-robin confirms this, it's stronger than D128: the statmatch-continued reward didn't merely fail to compound, it actively REGRESSED the policy below its starting point — direct evidence against statmatch-as-continued-reward (addressing Codex's D128-A demand for ladder confirmation + the "continuation potential" question head-on). Full ladder + Elo refit in the next entry. **What this settles, addressing Codex's D128-A demands head-on:**
1. **D128 CONFIRMED on the ladder, not just one H2H:** league7b (146.7) > league7 (117.4) by ~29 Elo across 5 shared anchors + their direct row.
2. **Continuation-potential challenge ANSWERED:** league7 ended **52 Elo BELOW its own warm-start statmatch1 (117.4 vs 168.9)** — it loses to statmatch1 0.433/0.567 head-to-head. This is not a "lower starting Elo" artifact; the statmatch+pool+30B recipe ACTIVELY REGRESSED the policy below its starting point. Strong, direct evidence against THAT recipe.
3. **BUT "statmatch-as-reward is dead" is REFUTED — exactly as Codex cautioned.** statmatch2 (the SAME statmatch reward + D118-A formulation, but MIRROR selfplay, 8B, no hard pool) is **#2 at 161.3 — above league7b**, and only ~8 Elo below statmatch1 (minimal regression from its warm-start). So the statmatch reward in a mirror/short regime produces a TOP node; it's the combination **statmatch reward × hard-opponents pool × 30B** that regressed league7. Plausible mechanism: the hard pool forces adaptations that the human-stat-matching penalty actively fights (the penalty pulls toward human aggregate distributions while the pool rewards whatever beats strong opponents — a tug-of-war that over-regularizes over 30B), whereas mirror selfplay has no such conflict.

**REVISED DOCTRINE:** (i) D128/D129's "proven economy is the safe default mainline" STANDS (league7b #3 is the strongest 30B-hard-pool node). (ii) statmatch-as-reward is NOT abandoned — statmatch2's #2 placement REOPENS it as a promising MIRROR/short-continuation perturbation (candidate: a statmatch3 mirror run, longer, or statmatch×pool at SHORTER horizons to find where the conflict kicks in). (iii) statmatch1 remains the single strongest checkpoint (#1) — the natural warm-start for future arms per D107-A (league8 used league7b #3, fine but not optimal; not changing a live run). (iv) league7 is a dead-end recipe; do not continue it. CAVEATS: ladder omits league6b/tdmaniac1/stakes1 as league7/7b/statmatch2 opponents (rig lacked them — they're anchored via the D122 graph, so their Elo is still placed, just with fewer direct edges to the new nodes); the statmatch2-vs-league7 comparison still co-varies pool AND steps (not a clean single-variable isolation of "why league7 regressed" — that needs a statmatch+pool+8B or statmatch+mirror+30B arm). A Codex sanity-check of this nuanced finding is a worthwhile follow-up before it hardens into doctrine, but the full-ladder evidence is far stronger than D128's single H2H.**

**D130-A — CODEX REVIEW of D130: the league7-regression signal is solid, but the CAUSAL headline over-claims; two factual errors fixed (2026-06-16, `.codex-reviews/d130-ladder-review.md`).** Read + accepted. What Codex confirmed as SOLID: league7 regressed below statmatch1 — direct row 0.433 (95% CI ~[0.421,0.445]), fitted gap ~51.5 Elo (bootstrap 95% [47.4, 55.5]); the ladder graph is well-connected (each new node has 7 rows spanning top/mid/floor anchors). What it corrected:

1. **The causal headline over-reaches.** "the culprit is statmatch × hard-pool × 30B" NAMES the interaction before the missing 2×2 cells are tested — league7 vs statmatch2 changes pool regime AND duration simultaneously. Defensible version: *league7's exact recipe regressed below its warm-start; because statmatch2 used the same reward+warm-start and stayed top-tier under mirror/8B, the reward ALONE is not a sufficient explanation; remaining candidates are hard-pool pressure, longer duration, live-pool snapshot drift, or their interaction.* The specific interaction is a HYPOTHESIS, not yet shown.
2. **"statmatch2 > league7b" is model-fit-supported, NOT head-to-head.** Their direct row is exactly 0.500 (tied, draw 0.444); the +14.6 Elo gap comes from statmatch2's stronger SHARED-ANCHOR profile (vs league6/league5/gen1/exploiter1), not from beating league7b. Correct wording: "statmatch2 is top-tier and score-BT rates it above league7b," not "proven superior."
3. **"statmatch reopened as a mirror perturbation" is a HYPOTHESIS, not doctrine** — statmatch2 vs statmatch1 is only 0.489 (CI ~[0.477,0.501]), i.e. "didn't drift far from the champion," which could be warm-start inertia + short continuation rather than a genuinely stronger perturbation.
4. **Two factual errors fixed inline in D130:** (a) the "re-anchored to gen1" scale explanation was wrong — D122 was ALSO gen1-anchored; the scale differs because the metric changed (decisive-only BT → score-with-draws Elo); (b) D130 now states explicitly these are the score-based Elo ratings (draws=0.5), not bt_fit's default decisive-only table.

**NEXT-DIAGNOSTIC ORDER (Codex, accepted) — supersedes D130's statmatch3-first instinct:** (1) CHEAPEST + CLEANEST: ladder league7's OWN intermediate snapshots (verified to exist — the 2B-interval pool snapshots + frequent run-dir saves) at e.g. 2B/4B/8B/16B/30B vs {statmatch1, statmatch2, league7b, league6, gen1} — this traces the regression TRAJECTORY (early pool-conflict vs late overtraining) with zero new training, just matches. **D131 — PufferLib hyperparameter SWEEP: researched (smores), de-risked sweep LAUNCHED + RUNNING on ballhawk, real bug found+fixed (2026-06-16, Alex "go ahead").** Joseph Suarez recommended a perf sweep. Smores (claude-smores-eap[1m] via `claude -p`) researched PufferLib's Protein optimizer (CARBS-derived: 2 GPyTorch GPs for score+cost, Sobol-seeded, Pareto-front, cost-aware acquisition) and wrote `docs/pufferlib-sweep-proposal.md`. Its critical finding — VERIFIED in code — is that a plain `puffer sweep bloodbowl` DEADLOCKS: the non-match result path hardcodes `metrics['env/score']` (`pufferl.py:394`) but our `binding.c` emits no `score` key → trial subprocess KeyErrors, parent hangs on `result_queue.get()`. Fix = chess.ini-style MATCH MODE (score each trial by win-rate vs a fixed frozen checkpoint).

LAUNCHED the de-risked validation sweep (16 trials, 200M steps each, warm=league7b_cap, train-vs-frozen-league6, score-vs-league7b match-mode, curriculum maxdist 6). Three integration gotchas found + fixed live (the POINT of a de-risk run):
1. **PufferLib BUG (real, fixed):** the match-mode keys (`match_enemy_model_path` etc.) are MISSING from `sweep.py`'s skip-list (`_params_from_puffer_sweep`, ~line 148), so they hit `assert isinstance(param, dict)` → `Param match_enemy_model_path is not a dict`. Match-mode was half-wired in our vendored 4.0. Fix: add the 4 match_* keys to the skip tuple — committed as `training/sweep_match_mode_exclusion.patch` (+ applied on the box). The match-mode sweep feature literally does not work without this.
2. **`sweep_only` is MANDATORY:** without it, PufferLib inherits default.ini's FULL `[sweep.*]` catalogue and ALSO sweeps `policy.hidden_size`/`num_layers`/`train.total_timesteps` — which breaks warm-start AND match-mode (both need FIXED arch 512/3). No CLI flag exists; must be in the ini `[sweep]`. Added a turn-key `[sweep]` block to `puffer/config/bloodbowl.ini` with `sweep_only = learning_rate, ent_coef, gae_lambda, gamma` + the match keys + 4 param ranges.
3. **Stale `.pyc`:** after patching `sweep.py`, must `rm __pycache__/sweep.cpython-311.pyc` or Python runs the old bytecode.

VERIFIED RUNNING: after the fixes, the sweep restricts to exactly the 4 intended dims (trial suggestions show only `train/learning_rate`/`ent_coef`/`gamma`/`gae_lambda`, NO arch/timesteps), match-mode active (no deadlock), trials training. Box note: ballhawk (restarted from exited for this) had FLAKY SSH (repeated mid-command drops + 2 re-exits before stabilizing) — the direct endpoint `120.238.149.205:32743` works; monitor via SHORT connections, not long until-loops. Sweep is `--tag sweep-val2`, `/tmp/sweep_val2.log`. NEXT: collect the 16-trial Pareto result (~1-1.5h), read the best lr/ent_coef/gae_lambda/gamma, decide whether to (a) run the full 9-dim 32-trial sweep and (b) adopt the winning HPs into the mainline config. The whole sweep path is now turn-key (patch + config committed) for any stable box.**

So the R6v1 arm CONTINUED IMPROVING over its start (unlike league7's statmatch which regressed) — a positive signal.

Freed disk 96%→74% (deleted 33 ancient June-4-7 run dirs, caps already in B2). league8 still WON despite 2B fewer steps than league7b's 30B. **D133 — BACKLOG (Alex design, 2026-06-16): R12 = defensive scoring-lane threat — the DUAL of R6v1 carrier-exposure.** Alex flagged a real asymmetry: R6v1 prices only OUR ball protection (when WE hold the ball, is the carrier reachable without a dodge/GFI?). There is NO corresponding DEFENSIVE term — when the OPPONENT holds the ball, have we left a free lane to our endzone? Nothing currently prices defensive positioning at all (why untrained defenders clump/ball-chase instead of screening). The symmetry is sound: if pricing "is my carrier exposed" drives offense, pricing "can the enemy score for free" should drive sane defense.

**v1 (Alex's stated minimum = one turn):** reuse R6v1's `bb_reach_field_compute` (already a `(dodges,gfis)` Dijkstra from any mover to every square) as the DUAL — mover = enemy ball carrier (fires only when opponent holds the ball, mirroring R6v1's gate), target = our defensive endzone LINE (`x = bb_endzone_x(enemy_team)`), classify min `(dodges,gfis)` cost over that line within carrier `MA + bb_max_rushes`: `(0,0)`→FREE WALK-IN (defense breached), total==1→soft (one dodge OR GFI to score), ≥2/unreachable→screened. Fire at MY-turn-end when the opponent holds the ball (symmetric to R6v1's own-turn-end). Connection: R6v1's endzone-EXEMPTION already does a CRUDE version (Chebyshev distance ≤ MA+rushes, but IGNORES tackle zones) — R12 is that upgraded to real screen-aware reachability.

**Why potentially HIGHER value than R6v1:** offense exposure = one opponent reaching one carrier; defense = carrier reaching a whole LINE, so a SINGLE hole anywhere breaches the screen. "Cover every lane" is strictly harder than "protect one piece" and is exactly where RL defenders fail — a free-lane penalty would directly teach screen/deep-safety discipline.

**REFINED STAGING (Alex, 2026-06-16) — the v2 split is the key insight: carrier-only stays POLYNOMIAL, only v3 explodes:**
- **v1** — binary free-lane (0-dodge/0-GFI for the current carrier this turn). One Dijkstra.
- **v1.5** — graded by the NUMBER of dodges/GFIs required (continuous threat probability vs binary). Same engine, richer cost readout. Mirrors R6v1.5's graduated-probability refinement → keeps offense/defense symmetric.
- **v2** — two-turn, **CARRIER ONLY** (no passing, no handoffs): can THIS carrier reach the endzone in two of its own activations? Still SINGLE-PIECE pathfinding, just a larger budget (≈ 2×(MA+rushes), counting dodges/GFIs en route) — polynomial, NO explosion, because the ball never changes hands so no new movers enter. Catches the most common real defensive failure ("you left a two-move-deep hole"). Caveat to make explicit: v2 implicitly assumes the defense does NOT re-screen between the opponent's two turns (in real BB you'd get an intervening turn to plug it) → v2 slightly OVER-estimates threat, but that's the SAFE direction for a shaping signal (teaches "don't even leave a two-move lane"); modeling the re-screen turns it into a game-tree, defeating the point. Canary, not exact-solve.
- **v3** — the EXPONENTIAL case: any handoff or pass. THIS is what blows up — the ball can transfer to a fresh piece (new mover, own MA) or teleport via a throw, so it's no longer single-piece pathfinding but a search over which teammate gets the ball and from where. Defer; if ever built, via SAMPLING (à la tools/blockev_mc.c), only if v2's canary proves insufficient.

STAGING DISCIPLINE matches R6 exactly (v1 → v1.5 → v2a/v2b). Ship v1 first once the R6v1 line (D132) is validated — offense + defense from the same reachability core. Implementation cost is low given R6v1 landed; v1/v1.5/v2 all reuse `bb_reach_field_compute` with no new EV engine.

**D133-A — R12 REFRAMED (Alex, 2026-06-16): measure PLAYERS not the BALL — dissolves the v3 exponential entirely; the simpler model is also MORE defensively correct.** Alex's key insight: humans don't compute the ball's exponential branching to assess scoring threat — they look at which OPPOSING PLAYERS can get downfield. Shift the question from "where can the ball go?" (branches through handoffs/passes = the v3 blowup) to "who can reach my endzone by movement?" (per-player, O(players)). LEGITIMATE because ball-delivery is cheap and player movement is the binding constraint — a fast deep player is a scoring threat BEFORE it holds the ball (the ball can be handed/thrown to it). Measuring players instead of the ball DELETES the need to model ball-transfer, which was the entire source of the v3 explosion.

**THE METRIC (replaces the carrier-reachability v1):** per opposing player `p`: `reach_per_turn(p) = MA(p) + max_GFIs(p)` (≈+2, +3 w/ Sprint); `turns_to_score(p) = ceil(dist_to_our_endzone(p) / reach_per_turn(p))`; count `n_threats_1turn`(≤1) and `n_threats_2turn`(≤2). Two turns = "same thing, ×2 budget" — O(players), one subtract + divide each, NO Dijkstra, NO ball model. **Mitigation = the defensive job:** a MARKED deep player has reduced effective reach (must dodge to leave, costing tempo + turnover risk), so the live signal = **unmitigated deep threats** = count players who can score in ≤N turns AND are unmarked. Minimizing that = "mark/cover the deepest movers" = the human heuristic; policy learns to body the fast deep piece instead of clumping on the ball.

**WHY MORE CORRECT THAN THE CARRIER-CENTRIC VERSION:** the defensive failure vs fast teams isn't the carrier strolling through your screen — it's an UNCOVERED DEEP RECEIVER your carrier-lane screen never accounted for. Player-centric "how many pieces can get deep" is the right object. HONEST TRADE: drop tackle-zone-aware PATH precision (raw distance vs screened path) for ball-agnosticism + O(players) cost — but for deep coverage that's correct, because a screen between carrier and endzone does NOTHING to cover an open downfield receiver, so path-cost was measuring the wrong thing. Marking, not lane-pathing, is how you address a deep mover.

**SUPERSEDES the reachability-dual as R12 v1.** Revised ladder: v1 = unmitigated deep-threat count (1-turn); v1.5 = graded (margin = reach − distance, and/or degree-of-marking); v2 = 2-turn (just ×2 reach budget); v3 (handoff/pass) DISSOLVED — never needed. Also a natural **obs FEATURE, not just reward** — "this enemy is a 1-turn scoring threat" is exactly the state a defender needs (per-player threat flag in the entity rows). The reachability-dual framing (D133 above) stays as the OPTIONAL lane-denial complement (cover the carrier's walk-in path) but is secondary to deep-mover coverage.

**D134 — SWEEP INFRA ROOT CAUSE (definitive, 2026-06-16): Vast auto-stops bursty `puffer sweep` workloads within hours; continuous `puffer train` survives for days. Solution = run on the OWNED 2070 (rig), per Alex.** After 4 Vast-box deaths mid-sweep (ballhawk machine 69007 ×2, japan machine 11743 ×2), ALL client-side causes are RULED OUT: (1) NOT bb_idle_guard.sh — it logged only 1-2 misses (limit 6 for japan), no STOP today, and the pattern/SSH-failure bugs were already fixed (D131); (2) NOT the credit ladder — not running (PID stale, no script on disk, logged "exiting" 09:18 yesterday), balance $53 >> all thresholds; (3) NOT a crash — zero tracebacks, clean `puffer sweep` return. Every dead box shows `intended_status: stopped` issued to Vast while running a sweep, across TWO different physical machines. The ONLY consistent variable: bursty sweep GPU-util (match-scoring phases between trials drop util to ~0) vs continuous training's steady util. Conclusion: a **Vast-side idle/low-util auto-stop policy** trips on sweeps but not training — infrastructure, not client-fixable. VERDICT: stop restarting Vast boxes for sweeps (rabbit hole). Run the sweep on the **2070/rig** (Tailscale-owned, NOT a Vast instance → immune to any Vast idle policy AND to the bb-* idle-guard) once statmatch3 caps (~17:05, 7.8B/8B). ~6-7h there (9× slower than a 4090) but it WILL finish. Offline wandb capture (D-pending, sweep-japan2) is the right results mechanism regardless of box; japan's partial offline-run-* data persists on its stopped disk if needed. NOTE for future: sweeps belong on owned hardware or a Vast instance with idle-stop disabled; never assume a Vast box survives a multi-hour bursty job.

**D135 — R12 v1 IMPLEMENTED (Opus agent, 2026-06-16, Alex-authorized parallel build): per-player defensive scoring-lane threat, default-0.0 inert, 374 tests pass.** Per D133-A (the per-player reframe). Extended `engine/src/bb_reachability.c`/`.h` with `bb_def_threat_turns` (per-player: reach = MA + `bb_max_rushes`; dist to the player's OWN scoring endzone = our defensive endzone via `bb_endzone_x(BB_TEAM_OF(slot))`; ceil(dist/reach); −1 sentinel for ineligible off-pitch/down/rooted/immobile) + `bb_def_threat_eval(m, team)` (counts the team's OPPONENTS who are UNMITIGATED — `!bb_is_marked` — and reach in ≤1 / ≤2 turns). O(players), no Dijkstra, no ball model. Reward hook in `bloodbowl.h` (~L1969) at the settled own-turn-end flip (mirrors R6v1), `t`=defending team: subtracts positive `reward_defensive_threat` per hard (1-turn) threat + `reward_defensive_threat_soft` per DISJOINT soft-band threat (`n2−n1`, no double-charge); telemetry `ep_def_threats_1t`/`ep_def_threats_2t` (2t = inclusive ≤2). binding.c kwargs + log keys (dict cap 40/64); ini defaults 0.0 (both). 13 new tests (`test_defthreat.c`) incl. endzone-inversion guard, marked=mitigated, 1↔2-turn boundary, Sprint reach, prone/rooted/off-pitch exclusion: `make test` 374/0, ASan/UBSan clean. LEAD REVIEW (sign/team/endzone-direction/soft-disjointness) = all correct. Default-0.0 = fully inert (hook guarded, eval not called when off) — safe to land like R6v1. NOT yet box-built (Mac-local; needs install_puffer_env.sh + rebuild + grep per footgun #4 before a live arm). OBS-FEATURE deferred (D133-A's per-player threat flag changes obs size = 3-sync-point migration + bc retrain — separate). Ready to A/B (suggested 0.05/0.02) after league9, or fold into an R6v1+R12 combined-defense arm.

**D136 — R12 DUAL REVIEW (Codex + adversarial Opus, 2026-06-16, Alex-requested pre-live): geometry CORRECT, but ONE BLOCKER (kickoff-gate) + 2 follow-ups before the live arm. Both reviews converged independently; Codex empirically reproduced the bug.** Verdict from BOTH: NOT ready to train as-is.

**BLOCKER (both, HIGH) — R12 fires on setup/kickoff active-team flips, not only settled own-turn-ends.** R6v1's hook was safe only because `bb_carrier_exposure_eval` early-returns unless the just-ended team holds the ball — that ball-gate doubled as a turn-boundary filter. R12 is ball-agnostic BY DESIGN (D133-A), so it inherits the generic `active_team`-flip hook's broader semantics and charges the KICKING team for the receiver's SETUP formation at the setup→kickoff flip. Codex's runtime probe against the exact `c_step` path: `seed=2 pre-turn R12 reward=(-0.14,0.00) active 0->1 before=SETUP after=KICKOFF ep=0/7 ball=0` — a penalty with turn counters still 0/0, ball off-pitch. Also reachable via kickoff `Charge!` active-team changes (proc_match.c:594/701). FIX (Codex's exact pattern): capture, BEFORE `bb_apply_trusted`, whether the pre-apply stack is inside a real `BB_PROC_TEAM_TURN` for the active team (`bbe_in_team_turn` helper), and gate the R12 reward+telemetry block on it. Stack-based (not counter-based) so kickoff-event flips don't count.

**FOLLOW-UP 1 (Opus HIGH / Codex MEDIUM) — clamp-stacking from unbounded count.** R12's threat count is unbounded (~11); R12 lands on the same step as win/loss terminal bonus + possession + carrier-exposure. Opus's worst case: terminal LOSS + 8 deep threats ≈ −1.08 → clips the [−1,1] clamp (ini lines 35-40 warn about this), silently corrupting the loss gradient. Codex: R12-alone max 0.55 is under the clamp, but budget against same-step rewards. RESOLUTION: cap the charged count (`hard=min(n1,4)`, `soft=min(n2−n1,4)`) → bounds R12 at −0.20/−0.08, keeps the terminal stack inside [−1,1]; loses ~no fidelity (rarely >4 truly-unmarked 1-turn movers). Telemetry stays uncapped (true counts).

**FOLLOW-UP 2 (both) — no hook-level tests.** The 13 tests exercise the pure evaluator only; none drive `c_step`/the reward hook, so none would catch the gate bug. Add 2 Puffer-level tests: (a) setup→kickoff transition asserts NO R12 reward + no `ep_def_threats_*` increment before the first real team-turn end; (b) a controlled own-turn-end asserts `reward[t] == -(hard*scale + (n2-n1)*soft_scale)` and the telemetry increments.

**CONFIRMED CORRECT by both (ships as-is):** endzone direction (`bb_endzone_x(BB_TEAM_OF(slot))`, traced for home+away), sign (positive subtracted, no double-negate), soft-tier disjointness vs inclusive telemetry, integer ceil `(dist+reach-1)/reach`, eligibility filters (off-pitch/down/rooted/marked), `bb_is_marked` excluding no-TZ markers. Post-fix canary (both): watch contact rate / blocks / def-TDs-conceded for over-marking, and `ep_def_threats_1t/2t` dropping WHILE win-rate improves. Apply the gate (blocker) + cap + hook-tests, re-verify `make test`, THEN box-build for the live arm (still gated behind league9).

**D136-A — R12 fixes APPLIED + lead-verified (2026-06-16): all 3 D136 items resolved, 378 tests, ready for box-build.** (1) GATE (blocker): `bb_in_team_turn(m, team)` (proc_match.c:417, scans stack for `BB_PROC_TEAM_TURN` with matching team id), captured as `pre_in_team_turn` BEFORE `bb_apply_trusted` (bloodbowl.h:1872), gates the R12 reward+telemetry block (bloodbowl.h:1983). Setup→kickoff / `Charge!` flips have no TEAM_TURN frame → skipped; normal own-turn-end still fires. MUTATION-TESTED: neutering the gate → 179 failures incl. "R12 charged on opening setup/kickoff flip". R6v1 block untouched (its ball-held check already gates). (2) CAP: reward uses `min(n1,4)`/`min(n2−n1,4)`; telemetry records TRUE uncapped counts — bounds R12 at −0.20/−0.08 so the terminal-step stack stays inside [−1,1]. (3) TESTS: +4 engine (`bb_in_team_turn` seam true/false across team-turn vs setup/kickoff stack states; cap arithmetic) + a hook-level `--r12test` driving real `c_step` with the mutation check. `make clean && make test` 378/0, ASan/UBSan clean, default-0.0 still fully inert. Lead-reviewed the gate (capture-before-apply correct) + cap (reward-only, telemetry true). NEXT: box-build R12 (install + rebuild + grep symbols + smoke) for the live A/B arm — still gated behind league9 (task #61).

**D137 — SWEEP RESULT (16-trial Protein, match-mode vs league7b, 2026-06-16): clean read via wandb sync — LOWER lr + LOWER entropy beat the default by ~+6 win-rate points. Adopt for league9.** The whole sweep saga resolved: match-mode DID engage (all 16 trials scored by `env/match_score` = win-rate of the 200M-step continuation vs frozen league7b; `perf` unused — the earlier "did match-mode fire" worry was wrong). Captured via offline wandb (the export-WANDB_MODE fix, D134-era) and read by `wandb sync` + the wandb API (Alex's account already authed in ~/.netrc). Top trials (match win-rate vs league7b, higher=better):

```
0.6159  lr 0.000284  ent 0.0092  gae 0.846  gamma 0.9961   <- BEST
0.5973  lr 0.000122  ent 0.0064  gae 0.890  gamma 0.9970
0.5922  lr 0.0001    ent 0.0050  gae 0.864  gamma 0.9959
0.5863  lr 0.0001    ent 0.0050  gae 0.937  gamma 0.9976
...
0.5526  lr 0.0006    ent 0.020   gae 0.85   gamma 0.995    <- CURRENT DEFAULT (the 2 idx<=1 seed trials)
```

CLEAR PATTERN: every top trial has **lower learning_rate (0.0001-0.00028 vs the default 0.0006) AND lower ent_coef (0.005-0.009 vs 0.02)**; gae_lambda + gamma sit near the defaults (0.85/0.995). The best HP set beats the default by **0.6159 vs 0.5526 = ~+6 points of win-rate** — a real, actionable tuning win (standard result: a strong warm-start fine-tunes better with a gentler LR + less exploration entropy). RECOMMENDATION: launch league9 with **lr 0.00028, ent_coef 0.009, gae_lambda 0.85, gamma 0.996** (the best trial, rounded; gae/gamma kept near default since the sweep didn't move them). CAVEAT: optimized at a 200M-step proxy — direction is sound for a 30B continuation but the exact optimum may drift slightly; the lower-lr/lower-entropy direction is the robust takeaway. The sweep detour's full yield: this HP win + the upstreamed PufferLib match-mode bug fix (PR ready) + 2 idle-guard fixes + the D134 Vast-idle-stop diagnosis.

**D139-B — AUTOSTOP ROOT CAUSE SOLVED + FIXED (2026-06-17, Codex via Vast audit-logs): a SECOND idle-guard — a systemd `--user` timer ON THE 2070 RIG — was the persistent box-killer that survived disabling the Mac guard. **D141 — CONTACT-ECONOMY FINDING (Alex, watching BBTV, 2026-06-17): the league lineage trains with `injury_inflicted=0`, which removes the reward for the ENTIRE attrition game (blocking-for-removal AND fouling) — contradicting the canonical `run_league.sh` + the reward memo, which both specify injury ±0.15 / value_scaled 1. This reframes the "no defense" problem and demotes R12.** Chain of observation→diagnosis this session: (1) Alex on BBTV: "they literally don't play defense." (2) Telemetry confirms: blocks_thrown 6.8/game vs human 88.8 (−92%), block_2d_frac 0.44 vs 0.77 (under-throws FAVORABLE attacker's-choice blocks), block_2dred_frac 0.115 vs 0.017 (over-throws desperate ones), ~0 fouls (no foul telemetry surfaced). (3) Root insight (Alex): blocking is the COUPLED core of BOTH phases (offense blocks to make lanes/protect cage; defense blocks to slow cage/force turnover) — so when neither side contests, the whole melee collapses into a mutual non-aggression pact. This is a ~stable equilibrium: unilateral deviation toward contact doesn't pay (turnover risk + zero attrition reward + low marginal value in a fast score-trade), so MORE self-play TIME won't fix it (game-theory property, not exploration budget) — escaping needs an external perturbation. (4) Mechanism found: live league9 (and the league7→8→9 + statmatch lineage) launch with `--env.reward-injury-inflicted 0 --injury-taken 0 --injury-value-scaled 0`; NOT a resume regression (the ORIGINAL run_league9.sh had it 0 too, warm from league8_cap — the lineage carried injury=0 forward). The CANONICAL `tools/run_league.sh:190-191` has `injury_inflicted 0.15 / injury_taken -0.15 / value_scaled 1`; the reward memo (`docs/reward-design-coaching-wisdom.md:3,110`) lists injury ±0.15 as a SETTLED term and names injury-inflicted rate "the designated PASSIVITY CANARY." So zeroing it predicts EXACTLY the observed no-block/no-foul passivity — and the "fix" Alex remembers (injury 0.15 + value_scaled 1) exists in the canonical script + design but the mainline arms never actually ran it. Alex's fouling point (D141 trigger): a foul's only upside is the injury it causes (memo R3: "the injury knob pays the foul's upside +0.15 KO/CAS"); with injury=0 fouling is all-downside (send-off risk) no-upside → agent never fouls. CALIBRATION NUANCES before acting: (a) restoring injury 0.15 risks foul-SPAM unless the memo's R3 send-off PENALTY (designed, NOT implemented) prices the downside; (b) attrition reward is ~zero-sum in mirror self-play (D34) — teaches the SKILL, the winning EDGE needs asymmetry (→ the scripted contact opponent, doubling as the absolute-signal anchor the triple-review/D140 wanted); (c) D34/D39 documented the contact-vs-scoring tension — Profile-C k-values (k_kd 0.06/k_value 0.5) CURED never-blocking (D34) but crowded out scoring (tds 0.000) so they were HALVED (D39, live: k_kd 0.03/k_value 0.25); today's lineage scores FAR better than the D34/D39 era, so it can likely afford more contact reward now — that's the re-test. CONSOLIDATED EXPERIMENT (after league9 caps, gated on Alex): restore injury 0.15 + value_scaled 1, optionally raise k-knobs toward Profile-C, add R3 send-off penalty to keep fouling calibrated, A/B vs league9 watching the SCORING-retention canary (the D34 failure) + block volume/quality + foul rate climbing toward human. This is better-founded than R12 (D133/D140): R12 is a one-sided defensive bounty that doesn't restore the COUPLED offensive blocking and is distortive; the injury/contact economy is the actual collapsed lever, has prior proof it works (D34), and needs no new code. R12 stays demoted per D140.

(5) Goodhart: a "remove the assist-provider" bonus becomes an unconditional Guard-bounty unless folded into the SAME declaration's EV; per-knockdown/threat bounties reintroduce the D36/memo-line-92 "win the fight lose the game" LOS-punch-fest (D34: contact-seeking but tds 0.000; D39/D40: full-k harvested without win progress → halved). **D145 — KICKOFF "always touchback" is a LEARNING gap, not an engine bug (Alex observation on BBTV, 2026-06-18). The center-square tactic is faithfully modeled and the agent CAN select it; nothing teaches it to.** Alex: kicking team always touches back; the dead-center of the receiving half is the unique zero-touchback-risk placement (without Kick) because a max D6 scatter can't leave the half or go off-pitch. Investigation (subagent, file:line verified): (1) PLACEMENT is a real agent decision — `BB_A_KICK_TARGET` (bb_actions.h:23), kicking team chooses (proc_match.c:644), legal = EVERY square of the receiving half (proc_match.c:759-768, ~195 squares), encoded in the 391-wide spatial square head (each square independently maskable). (2) SCATTER = single D6 distance + D8 direction (proc_match.c:648-665); Kick skill halves it. NOT inflated. (3) TOUCHBACK fires correctly (proc_match.c:619-623/694-705): ball off-pitch OR in the kicking team's half → receiving team gives ball to any standing player. Matches BB2025. (4) CENTER-SQUARE math confirmed in our model: home-kicking safe center = x=19,y=7 (away-kicking x=6,y=7); max D6=6 from center reaches at most x=13/25, y=1/13 — all on-pitch, all in the receiving half. Zero touchback risk, exactly as real BB. (5) Agent CAN select center (distinct legal maskable square). VERDICT: pure LEARNING gap — placement is a genuine policy choice over ~195 squares, most carrying touchback risk, and **nothing rewards placement quality or penalizes touchback**, so an under-trained/exploratory placement head touches back most of the time. FIX CANDIDATE: a small `reward_kickoff_touchback` penalty charged to the KICKING team when its kickoff touches back — clean + targeted (touchback is unambiguously bad for the kicker; kickoff placement is a single isolated decision with a clear correct answer = low distortion risk, unlike positional shaping). Fold into a future arm (NOT the live attrition A/B). Alternative: leave to emerge from longer training (slower, uncertain). Recommend the penalty — it's the cleanest "teach the obvious tactic" signal and the mechanism is fully there for the agent to exploit.

**D146 — Two BBTV-observed behaviors diagnosed (Alex, 2026-06-18): (1) "blitz but no block" = REAL ENGINE BUG (missing reachability gate on Blitz declaration); (2) "grail knight oscillation" = the known over-rush policy pathology, faithfully rendered (NOT a bug).** 
**(1) BLITZ BUG.** BB2025 (`docs/vendor/bloodbowlbase/.../the_game_of_blood_bowl/index.html:7448`): declaring a Blitz MUST nominate a target the player can REACH (incl. Rush squares); may NOT declare if no opponent is reachable. The block itself is NOT mandatory once declared ("never required to perform the Block Action"). OUR ENGINE: `proc_turn.c:354-355` offers Blitz whenever `!m->blitz_used` with NO target arg and NO reachability check (contrast `proc_turn.c:351` BLOCK, gated on adjacency). So a player can legally declare a Blitz with ZERO reachable opponents → necessarily ends with no block = ILLEGAL in BB2025. `bb_reachability.c` exists (R12 uses it) but isn't wired into blitz-declare legality. This is a validation-layer miss (the kind the deferred FFB differential would catch). FIX: gate the Blitz declaration in `bb_legal_actions`/proc_turn on ≥1 reachable opponent (MA + max rush, dodge/GFI-path aware); do NOT force the block (keep END_ACTIVATION available). Engine change → changes the legal-action mask → goldens will change (expected, D6) → goes into the NEXT build, not the live attrition A/B. 
**(2) OSCILLATION (m_1781768323).** Macro-moves are OFF in the league9 STEPWISE lineage (server.py `--macro` defaults off; v5 macro retired D93), so the back-and-forth-then-GFI-turnover is genuine per-step policy choices = the documented over-rush/positional-mispricing pathology (D46 gfi 33/game vs human 17; D141 blocks 6.8 vs 88.8). NOT an engine bug, NOT a stream artifact. Only the reward-economy work fixes it — the live D144 attrition-restore A/B is the current attempt. 
ALSO this session: BBTV no-cache web server SHIPPED (serve_nocache.py + bbweb.service repointed; `Cache-Control: no-cache` verified — viewers auto-get UI updates after one refresh). **D147 — REWARD AUDIT: decision-time (EV-at-declaration) vs outcome (post-dice) — 5 SHAPING TERMS VIOLATE THE CARDINAL RULE (Alex, 2026-06-18, after the attrition A/B's pathetic blocks_thrown 6.8→7.8).** Alex's principle: "reward the DECISION at decision time, then the dice roll — don't reward on injury (outcome)." Two parallel sub-agents audited every reward term for WHERE it fires relative to `bb_apply_trusted` (the dice) and WHAT it reads (EV/settled-state vs realized result). Verdict:
- **COMPLIANT (A, decision-time/EV/potential/geometry):** `k_kd/k_value/k_ball/k_seq` (priced from `bb_block_ev` EV at BB_A_BLOCK_TARGET, pre-dice — bloodbowl.h:1935-1964), `rush_cost` (declaration tax), `surf_inflicted/taken` (deterministic crowd-push, no dice laundered), `dist_ball/dist_endzone` (telescoping potentials), `carrier_exposure±soft` (R6 reachability geometry), `def_threat±soft` (R12 geometry), `setup_done/autofix` (pre-apply action read).
- **OBJECTIVE/terminal (C, outcome correct — it IS the goal):** `td`, `win`, `draw`, and `possession` annuity (zero-sum settled-turn-boundary mini-terminal, not dice shaping).
- **VIOLATORS (B, outcome-based shaping — MUST convert to decision-time):**
  1. **`injury_inflicted/taken/value_scaled`** (bloodbowl.h:2213-2241) — read the realized KO/CAS box AFTER apply. THE textbook anti-pattern: two identical 2d+Block declarations pay wildly different rewards based on injury-dice variance. FIX: price `ev.p_def_removed` (inflicted) / `ev.p_att_removed` (taken), cost-weighted when value_scaled, at block declaration — the engine ALREADY exposes these (`bb_blockev.h:44`); injuries are literally the realized version of what `k_value` already prices as EV. Cleanest fix = fold injury shaping into the k_value channel, DELETE the post-apply scan. (This is why restoring injury_inflicted only nudged blocks 6.8→7.8: a sparse rare-injury signal can't drive contact; the dense EV-at-declaration k-knobs are the lever — D34.)
  2. **`send_off`** (R3, bloodbowl.h:2257) — reads realized SENT_OFF post-Bribe/Argue dice. FIX: price `P(send-off)=P(caught: doubles)·P(no bribe)·P(no argue)` at FOUL declaration (all inputs known pre-roll).
  3. **`kickoff_touchback`** (just added, bloodbowl.h:1848) — reads realized off-pitch scatter. FIX: price `P(touchback)` at KICK-PLACEMENT by convolving the D8+D6 scatter distribution over the aim square; needs a new pure `bb_kick_touchback_ev(m,x,y)` helper (the ONLY violator whose EV isn't already exposed).
  4. **`ball_gain/ball_loss`** (bloodbowl.h:2179-2193) — pay on realized possession transition (pickup/strip/scatter die result) = the "measured poison" that converged every masked arm to ball-avoidance. FIX: fold into the possession annuity (ball_loss already 0 in v4; set ball_gain 0 too) OR price `k·P(pickup success)` at the pickup/pass declaration.
  5. **`statmatch_scale`** (B, qualified, lowest priority) — episode-end penalty on realized match stats; intentional human-prior regularization, not per-decision dice shaping; most components are attempt-counts (decisions) not successes. Leave unless it misbehaves.
CODIFIED: added THE CARDINAL RULE to CLAUDE.md's Reward-economy section (was absent — only knob values + anti-farming invariants were there, which is why injury-restore slipped through; the principle had lived only in a buried bloodbowl.h header comment + scattered D-entries). NEXT-ARM IMPLICATION: the "make them fight" arm should NOT use injury_inflicted; instead raise the EV k-knobs (k_kd 0.03→0.06, k_value 0.25→0.5, Profile-C, which D34 proved drives blocking) and fold removal-EV into k_value — pure decision-time. Build the `injury→p_def_removed` conversion + (optionally) the touchback/foul EV fixes before the next contact arm.

**D148 — ATTRITION A/B VERDICT: injury-OUTCOME economy is a DEAD END (2026-06-18). Tournament attrition vs league9 = 0.493/0.507 (TIE, draw 0.437); blocks_thrown only 6.8→7.8.** The D141/D142 arm (warm league9_cap, restored injury_inflicted 0.15 + injury_taken -0.15 + value_scaled + send_off -0.15, k-half, 28B) capped clean (ATTRITION_AB_EXIT 0). Result: NOT stronger than league9 (statistical tie) AND barely more contact (blocks 6.8→7.8 = "pathetic", Alex). ROOT CAUSE (D147 audit): injury_inflicted is an OUTCOME reward (reads the realized KO/CAS box post-dice) — a sparse, rare, variance-dominated signal that can't drive the blocking decision; it pays the lucky injury, not the good block. tds dipped to ~1.0 early then recovered to ~1.4 (no scoring collapse, but no contact win either). CONCLUSION: the injury-restore hypothesis is REFUTED; the dense decision-time EV k-knobs are the contact lever (D34), not realized-injury bounties. attrition_cap backed up to Mac runs/league9/ (neutral checkpoint, not a lineage continuation). japan STOPPED (idle; next arm needs build). NEXT DIRECTION (Alex, 2026-06-18): a **THREAT ANNUITY** — the EV-weighted, zero-sum, decision-time dual of the possession annuity: carrier_threat = Σ_enemies P(blitz-reaches-carrier via dodges/GFIs) × P(knockdown via bb_block_ev), charged −to ball-holder / +to defenders, measured at settled turn-end. Subsumes R6 (tiered→EV-weighted, symmetric); prices knockdown VALUE endogenously (a prone/marked enemy contributes 0, so decking/marking a threat is rewarded by exactly the threat removed); rewards defensive positioning (the agents' biggest gap) + offensive cage/mark; reuses the reachability + block-EV engines; fully decision-time (cardinal-rule compliant). Caution: positive defense reward must price ACTIONABLE threat (can actually blitz), never just proximity (anti-turtle, distinct from the D67-69 "don't reward being safe" warning). Spec + adversarial + Codex review before build, per Alex's standing pattern.

**D149 — THREAT ANNUITY reviewed (adversarial Opus + Codex, 2026-06-18): SAFE to run default-0 A/B at k=0.03; 2 accuracy fixes applied; symmetric design KEPT over the reviewer's revert suggestion.** Opus built+ran+probed the impl (`reward_carrier_threat`, bb_reachability.c `bb_carrier_threat_eval`). VERIFIED CLEAN: cardinal-rule intact (0 bb_rng/dice in eval — decision-time pure, the whole point per D147), holder term `+k*(T_max-T_c)` is a REAL gradient (not inert; varies with T_c), per-step clamp can't mask a terminal loss (reward_win 3.0 saturates [-1,1]), T_max=2 cap sane, no R6 stacking (fails-fast guard), no double-count with possession/k-knobs/R12, baseline engine-computed 0.0976. (Codex review run was exploration-heavy, no clean verdict extracted.) FINDINGS + decisions: (1) HIGH-2 APPLY — P_reach compounds the cheapest-DODGE path not the max-SUCCESS path (a 0-dodge multi-GFI route can beat a 1-hard-dodge route) → systematically UNDER-prices threat (biases against the term's purpose); fix = also score the shortest/all-GFI path, take max. (2) MEDIUM-1 APPLY — only the first adjacent square/cost-tier evaluated for the blitz; fix = eval all reachable adjacent squares, keep max P_kd. (3) HIGH-1 KEEP DESIGN — Opus flags the holder's constant positive as a camping subsidy + suggests reverting to asymmetric `-k*T_c`; OVERRIDDEN: that's Alex's explicit symmetric-positive design (offense gets a positive for suppression, mirroring possession), and the camping risk was already accepted with small-k + canary; Opus's own math confirms scoring dominates camping 3.6 vs 0.72 over a drive at k=0.03. Mitigation: start k=0.03, ENFORCE the camping canary as a hard gate in the A/B watch (tds non-decreasing + carrier-dist-to-endzone delta negative + possession not turtle-spiking vs league9; halve k if camping emerges). (4) MEDIUM-2/3 LEAVE+NOTE — frozen-assist P_kd under-prices coordinated blitzes (deliberate O(enemies) R6v2a discipline) + threat priced on both flips (symmetric, acceptable); both bias conservative. ALL bugs bias the signal the SAME conservative direction (under-price) → weaken not poison. NEXT: apply HIGH-2 + MEDIUM-1, rebuild japan (with D146 blitz fix folded in), launch threat-annuity A/B (warm league9_cap, carrier-threat replacing R6, k 0.03, the rest = settled v4 economy held), watch the camping canary.

**D150 — THREAT-ANNUITY A/B LAUNCHED on japan (2026-06-18): live + training, tds healthy ~1.3-1.4, but SPS 237K = 8.4x slower than league9 (~2M) — the eval is the bottleneck.** Arm `league10-threat`: warm from league9_cap (threat_warm.bin), `reward_carrier_threat 0.03` REPLACING R6 (carrier-exposure 0/0), injury 0 (dropped the D148 dead-end), everything else = settled v4 economy + swept HP (lr 0.00028/ent 0.009, possession 0.03, ball_gain 0.05, k-half, rush 0.015, dist 0.05/0.2), league7 pool preseed, 28B, snapshot 2B.
