EARLY READ (~16M): tds 1.3-1.4 — scoring NOT collapsing, first sign the threat annuity doesn't break offense (unlike the camping fear). COST PROBLEM: SPS 237.7K vs league9 ~2M = 8.4x slower (Env 865ms/79% of step). Cause: the threat eval does O(enemies≈11) × (reach Dijkstra + up to 8 carrier-adjacent-square block-EV FULL-MATCH CLONES × 2 paths from the D149 accuracy fixes) PER own-turn-end. The per-square bb_match clone + bb_block_ev is the heavyweight; the MEDIUM-1 (all adjacent squares) + HIGH-2 (two paths) fixes roughly 2-3x'd the constant. At 237K SPS, 28B ≈ 33h (~$15-25). OPTIONS: (a) accept 33h; (b) OPTIMIZE the eval (clone once per enemy not per square; or skip the all-squares loop / second path when the cheapest is dominant) — recovers most SPS, needs re-test; (c) shorten the run (verdict likely visible by ~10-14B; stop early if clear). DECISION: let it run + WATCH the camping canary (tds non-decreasing, carrier dist-to-endzone decreasing, possession not turtle-spiking) + contact/sack rate; stop early at a clear verdict; offer the eval optimization to Alex. CAMPING CANARY is the hard gate (D149).

**D151 — THREAT A/B DIVERGENCE ROOT CAUSE: NOT the threat reward — a latent `exp()` overflow in the native PPO loss that affects EVERY native run (2026-06-18). FIX: clamp `logratio` before `exp` + skip non-finite minibatches in `torch_pufferl.py`.** The `league10-threat` arm (D150) trained HEALTHY (possession 0.11→0.21 stable, blocks/blitzes/knockdowns climbing — NOT camping; the camping canary did NOT fire) then SUDDENLY went `policy=inf` → all-losses=nan at 661M. Isolation ruled out every env-side suspect: reward is finite (`episode_return 0.018` at the NaN step — the T_max cap `min(T,T_max)` clamps even a NaN `uncapped_total` to a finite reward), obs is **uint8** (`(unsigned char)(p_def_down*255)` — physically cannot carry a NaN float into the forward pass), legal-action masks are **never empty** (0 empties over 12M random decisions), the D146 blitz gate is **pure** (stack-local `bb_reach_field`, clones for prone — no enumeration side effects). The tds 0.548 at the NaN point is the post-NaN dying policy, not learned camping. ROOT CAUSE in `vendor/PufferLib/pufferlib/torch_pufferl.py:599-600`: `logratio = newlogprob - mb_logprobs; ratio = logratio.exp()` with **no clamp**. The native CUDA rollout and the torch train-time recompute (`sample_logits`) disagree on a handful of masked-action log-probs every minibatch (even WITH the existing mask-recompute LOCAL PATCH), so `old_approx_kl = (-logratio).mean()` runs **~110-180 on EVERY native run** (verified: kickoff5-9 = 104-132, s4 = 113, all trained fine) — a chronic heavy-tailed `|logratio|`. Negative tails underflow to `ratio≈0` harmlessly; a single `logratio > 88` overflows `exp()` to **+inf** → `pg_loss1 = -adv*inf` → backward NaN → every weight NaN → all losses NaN (and post-corruption garbage: `illegal_frac 0.265`). Healthy runs survived only by luck of staying under the `exp(88)` cliff; the threat reward's net-positive injection nudged old_kl 130→180, closer to the edge, and a batch tipped over at 661M. FIX (Python-only, no rebuild): (1) `logratio = logratio.clamp(-20, 20)` before `exp` → ratio ∈ [2e-9, 4.85e8], far below inf and far wider than any legitimate PPO ratio (real per-epoch moves keep |logratio|<~3), so it never touches learning dynamics — it only defuses the overflow; (2) belt-and-suspenders `if not torch.isfinite(loss): zero_grad; nonfinite_skips++; continue` so no single bad minibatch can ever poison all weights again. This is a genuine harness robustness bug latent in all native training, relevant to the upstream PufferLib match-mode PR (task #58). FOLLOW-UP (not blocking): the chronic old_kl ~110-180 means rollout/train log-probs are systematically inconsistent (mask-mismatch on a few actions/minibatch) → those samples are silently zeroed (ratio≈0) = wasted gradient = training is mildly inefficient, not broken; worth a separate investigation into the CUDA-kernel vs `sample_logits` masking parity (D38 lineage). The threat-annuity design (D148/D149/D150) is VINDICATED — it never caused the NaN; relaunch with the patched harness to get a real verdict. Regression: `engine`/`make test` unaffected (Python harness); add a unit test asserting a synthetic `logratio=200` minibatch produces a finite loss + a recorded skip.

**D151-addendum — FIX REVIEWED (adversarial Opus) + REVISED to v2 + RELAUNCHED LIVE (2026-06-18).** Adversarial Opus review of the diagnosis+fix found 2 HIGH issues, both applied: (F4) the original `clamp(-20,20)` still lets a mask-mismatched NEGATIVE-advantage sample (ratio=exp(20)=4.85e8) dominate the minibatch mean — PPO's `max(pg1,pg2)` only clips the ratio on the positive-adv branch — so tightened to **`[-10,10]`** (ratio ≤2.2e4, contributes O(1) after averaging, still far under exp(88)); (F8) my in-place clamp made `old_approx_kl/approx_kl` read the CLAMPED logratio, erasing the ~180 heavy-tail canary that IS the diagnostic — fixed by clamping only the copy fed to `exp()` and keeping **raw `logratio` for the kl metrics**. Review CONFIRMED the diagnosis: obs is genuinely uint8 (cannot inject float NaN), `ep_carrier_threat` telemetry never feeds training, V-trace re-clips ratio to rho/c=1.0 so the advantage kernel is insensitive to the ratio blow-up → `pg_loss1=-adv*inf` is indeed the sole NaN entry. NOTED non-blocking: (F6, MEDIUM) on a skip the per-loss accumulators aren't incremented but the end-of-loop average divides by full `num_minibatches` → logged losses read low DURING a skip storm — moot in practice because the clamp makes the finite-loss backstop ~never fire; (F9, MEDIUM→upgraded) the chronic old_kl ~110-180 is a real rollout/train **logprob-parity bug** (native bf16 kernel rollout vs float32 `sample_logits` recompute + the `nan_to_num(probs,1e-8)` floor) — the clamp is a band-aid; proper fix = store/reuse the rollout kernel's logprob or match precision (the true follow-up, not "mildly inefficient"). v2 RELAUNCHED on japan (same `/tmp/run_threat_ab.sh`, warm threat_warm.bin): LIVE, steps advancing 0→2.9M, SPS ~270K, policy/value/entropy/total all FINITE, old_kl visible + climbing (23→43, canary intact) — overflow defused. Codex second-opinion review dispatched (`.codex-reviews/ppo-nan-clamp-fix.md`). NEXT: confirm it survives PAST 661M (original death point, ~40min), then watch the threat-annuity verdict + camping canary (D149/D150). FOLLOW-UP TASK: bf16/float32 logprob parity (F9) — affects every native run's sample efficiency.

**D151-v3 — v2 FIX FAILED IN PROD; v3 grad-norm guard deployed (2026-06-18).** The v2 `[-10,10]` clamp + finite-LOSS backstop survived the early run (validated to 2.9M) but NaN'd AGAIN at **675M** — past the original 661M death but same signature (old_kl→194 finite, then policy inf, **zero `nonfinite_skips`** = the loss-level backstop never fired). Root cause of the bypass: a finite-but-HUGE `pg_loss` (minibatch advantages normalized by a near-zero std via `(adv-mean)/(std+1e-8)`, times `ratio` up to exp(10)=22026) PASSES `isfinite(loss)`, then `loss.backward()` produces an **inf INTERMEDIATE gradient**, and `clip_grad_norm_` computes `inf*0 = NaN` → NaN weights before the next forward. A loss-level check structurally cannot catch a finite loss with inf grads. Codex's review INDEPENDENTLY flagged this ("other non-finite entry paths worth guarding, especially value and advantage normalization") and correctly predicted v2 would pass a short validation but risk a 600M+ run. v3 FIX: capture `grad_norm = clip_grad_norm_(...)` (it returns the pre-clip total norm) and **skip `optimizer.step()` when `not torch.isfinite(grad_norm)`** — a universal catch for inf/NaN grads from ANY component (advantage-norm, value, entropy, BC), dynamics-preserving (clean minibatches untouched), only skipping the rare catastrophic update. Editable install verified (single file, .pyc regen confirmed) so the patch IS loaded. Relaunched on japan. LESSON: validate a NaN fix PAST the known death step, not at 2.8M — armed a Monitor this time. The bf16/float32 logprob-parity bug (F9) remains the true upstream cause; the clamp+grad-guard are the robust band-aids that let the threat A/B produce a verdict.

**D152 — THE NaN IS A NEW-BUILD TRAINING INSTABILITY, NOT THE THREAT REWARD AND NOT THE PPO LOSS. Three guard-fixes (D151 v1/v2/v3) were chasing the wrong layer. Box idle; needs a revert/bisect decision (2026-06-18).** Decisive disambiguation run (threat term OFF, `reward_carrier_threat 0`, everything else identical on the same v3 build) ALSO went NaN — at epoch 729 (~190M steps) vs the threat arm's epoch 391 (~102M). Evidence chain:
- **Both configs NaN; threat only accelerates it** (102M with threat vs 190M without). The threat reward is NOT the cause — it changes WHEN, not WHETHER.
- **My D151 v1/v2/v3 torch_pufferl patches never engaged the real path.** The ORIGINAL unpatched threat run and the PATCHED v3 run NaN'd at the IDENTICAL epoch 391 / old_kl 183.759 / log line 12046. `nonfinite_skips` never incremented in EITHER the threat or control run → the NaN does not flow through a non-finite `loss` or `grad_norm`; it is entirely upstream of ratio/loss/gradient (the clamp + both backstops are downstream and inert against it). D151's "exp() overflow" root cause is WRONG (or at most a symptom): the real failure is upstream in the forward pass / data.
- **The signature is always the same:** `old_kl` climbs to ~185-190 (vs the healthy old-build ceiling ~104-132 on kickoff5-9/s4 — a ~47% higher mismatch), then `policy → inf` in a single epoch, then all losses NaN, then the policy is dead. old_kl IS the rollout-vs-train logprob mismatch (native CUDA kernel rollout vs torch `sample_logits` recompute over the legal-action mask). The new build inflates that mismatch until a logit overflows.
- **What changed vs the healthy billions-of-steps runs (league9, kickoff5-9):** the engine REBUILD folding in D146 (blitz reachability gate, `has_reachable_blitz_target`/`bb_reach_field_compute` in proc_turn.c) + D149 threat-eval code. The CONTROL has the threat eval disabled (`reward_carrier_threat 0` → `bb_carrier_threat_eval` never called), so the active engine delta in the failing control is **the D146 blitz-mask change**. PRIME SUSPECT: D146 made `bb_legal_actions`' blitz-declare legality state/path-dependent in a way that is nondeterministic OR differs between the CUDA rollout mask and the torch train-time mask → logprob mismatch (old_kl) inflates → overflow. (Candidates: uninitialized read in `has_reachable_blitz_target`/`bb_reach_field` stack struct; reachability result depending on scratch garbage; or a mask the rollout kernel and `sample_logits` compute differently.)
- **NOT yet ruled out:** value-function shock from warm-starting league9_cap (which trained under R6 carrier-exposure) into a different economy (R6 off); but old_kl (policy/mask), not value loss, is what climbs first — points to mask, not value.
NEXT (needs Alex's steer — invasive, and I've been wrong 3x so not guessing further autonomously): (a) REVERT just the D146 blitz gate, rebuild, rerun the control to ~250M (cheap: ~850K SPS → ~5 min) — if stable, D146 is confirmed and needs a determinism/mask-parity fix before re-landing; (b) determinism probe: run `bb_legal_actions` twice on identical states post-D146 and diff the blitz-declare bit; ASAN/valgrind the new engine for the uninitialized-read in the reachability path; (c) mask-parity probe: dump rollout mask vs train-recompute mask for the same obs and diff (the D38 lineage). DECISION REVERTS D151's "exp overflow" conclusion — the clamp/grad-guard are harmless robustness improvements worth KEEPING (they cost nothing and do guard a real cliff) but they do NOT fix this. Box japan is IDLE (both runs stopped, logs saved /tmp/threat_*.log + /tmp/control_nan.log). The threat-annuity DESIGN remains unfalsified — it has never had a clean run to be judged on.

**D152-addendum — MASK NONDETERMINISM RULED OUT (2026-06-18). The D146 reachability path is clean; the old_kl inflation is logprob non-parity (bf16 rollout vs fp32 train), not a mask bug.** Two zero-blast-radius Mac probes: (1) INSPECTION — `reach_field_compute_ordered` (engine/src/bb_reachability.c) FULLY initializes the field (opening double loop sets every cell cost=`reach_unreachable()`, len 0, prev -1, done 0) before the Dijkstra; `has_reachable_blitz_target`'s stack `bb_reach_field` is therefore never read uninitialized → no uninit-memory nondeterminism. (2) EMPIRICAL — `/tmp/maskdet.c`: called `bb_legal_actions` TWICE per decision on independent memcpy copies (one after poisoning 4KB of stack with 0xAA, one after zeroing it) over **6.0M decisions** → **0 mask mismatches, 0 blitz-bit mismatches**. The legal-action mask is deterministic. CONCLUSION: the rollout-vs-train logprob gap (old_kl ~190 fatal / ~130 healthy) is NOT mask nondeterminism — it is the **bf16-precision native rollout vs fp32 `sample_logits` train-recompute non-parity** (review finding F9), which the new build's D146-shifted (more peaked) masked action distribution likely amplifies past the overflow threshold. REMAINING LIVE HYPOTHESES for Alex: (1) bf16/fp32 logprob parity — store/reuse the native rollout kernel's logprob instead of recomputing in fp32 (the real F9 fix); (2) build bisect — rebuild the engine at the exact league9 (pre-D146) commit, rerun the control; if stable, re-add deltas one at a time (cheap at ~850K SPS, ~5min/run to 250M); (3) warm-start economy shock (league9_cap trained under R6, restarted with R6 off) — less likely since old_kl/policy, not value loss, leads. Four hypotheses now REFUTED with evidence (threat-reward-cause, my-PPO-patches, reach-uninit, mask-nondeterminism); the field is narrowed to logprob-parity vs a build-delta bisect. Recommend (2) first (decisive + cheap) then (1) as the durable fix. Box idle, awaiting steer — not guessing further autonomously after 3 wrong root-cause calls.

**D153 — ROOT CAUSE CONFIRMED (Codex gpt-5.5 xhigh, 2026-06-18): unclamped `__expf(logratio)` overflow in the NATIVE CUDA PPO kernel + bf16/fp32 logprob non-parity. My D151 patches were DEAD CODE for native runs; D152's "upstream of the ratio" conclusion was WRONG.** The decisive correction (`.codex-reviews/newbuild-nan-diagnosis.md`): the native bf16 league runs execute the PPO loss in the **CUDA kernel `vendor/PufferLib/src/pufferlib.cu` `ppo_loss_compute` (~L869)** and step via **`muon.cu` `muon_step` (~L159)** — NOT the Python `torch_pufferl.py train()` loop I patched in D151 v1/v2/v3. Proof: `pufferl.py:203` selects native `_C` unless `--slowly` (the launch scripts omit it); `torch_pufferl.py:21` REFUSES a bf16 `_C` build (the "PyTorch backend requires float32" error seen when probing). So `nonfinite_skips` never incremented and patched==unpatched onset because **the guards were on the wrong backend**, not because the NaN bypasses the ratio. This INVALIDATES D152's inference ("NaN is upstream of ratio/loss/gradient"); the original D151 MECHANISM (unclamped `ratio=exp(logratio)` overflow when the rollout/train logprob gap makes `|logratio|` huge) is almost certainly CORRECT — it just lives in `pufferlib.cu`, where `__expf(logratio)` is unclamped. CODEX RANKED CAUSES: (1ancy HIGH) native rollout stores **bf16** logprobs, train recomputes via a different fp32/log-space recurrent path → systematic non-parity → `old_kl` climbs to ~190 → a single `logratio>~88` overflows `__expf` to +inf → policy inf → all NaN (matches the observed signature exactly); (2-5 LOW) self-play frozen-row leakage (`compute_prio_normalize` +1e-6 samples frozen rows at tiny rate), stale/illegal-mask (would show `newlogprob<-1000` not a smooth climb — native masks with -1e4 not -inf), value/economy warm-start shock (rewards clamped + V-trace clipped, and policy-KL leads not value — so unlikely). The D146 mask change isn't a bug; it shifts the action distribution more peaked, widening the bf16/fp32 gap so the threat arm tips sooner (102M) than the control (190M) — both fail because the unclamped-`__expf` + bf16-parity gap is precision/build-wide, NOT threat-specific. FIX (native, needs GPU rebuild): in `pufferlib.cu` clamp `logratio` to [-10,10] before `__expf` (keep RAW logratio for the old_kl/approx_kl metrics), and guard `ppo_loss_compute` to zero policy/value grads + set ratio=1 + bump a debug counter when `!isfinite(total_log_prob||old_logp||adv_normalized||val_pred)`; guard `muon_step` to skip on non-finite grad norm. DURABLE FIX: bf16/fp32 logprob PARITY — store the rollout kernel's logprob and reuse it in train (don't recompute), or run native fp32 until parity lands. CHEAPEST CONFIRM (no rebuild): print `_C.precision_bytes` (expect 2 = bf16, proving the torch guards were off-path) + add native first-minibatch debug metrics (`mb0_old_kl`, `logratio_min/max`, `count(logratio>80)`, `count(newlogprob<-1000)`, `count(!isfinite)`) — if mb0_old_kl is already large pre-update it's rollout/train parity; if `count(logratio>80)` flips on in the fatal epoch the first non-finite is native `__expf`. STATUS: my D151 torch_pufferl.py patches are harmless for actual torch-backend (`--slowly`) runs but IRRELEVANT to native — keep as torch-path robustness or revert; they do NOT fix the native runs. Box idle; the real fix is a CUDA-kernel edit + rebuild, awaiting Alex's go (per "end research"). The threat-annuity design remains unfalsified — still never had a clean run. THIS IS THE 5TH AND CORRECT ROOT CAUSE; the prior 3 D151/D152 calls all missed the backend-dispatch fact (native `_C` vs Python torch). LESSON: for any native-backend numerics bug, confirm `_C.precision_bytes` and that the patched code path is actually executed BEFORE diagnosing — the loss math lives in pufferlib.cu/muon.cu, not torch_pufferl.py.

**D154 — NATIVE-CUDA NaN FIX IMPLEMENTED (Codex), REVIEWED (Claude), VALIDATED, COMMITTED (2026-06-18). The threat A/B now runs CLEAN past both death points; fork commit f14b71c.** Per D153, the real bug was the unclamped `__expf(logratio)` in the native CUDA PPO kernel (`pufferlib.cu`) — NOT the Python `torch_pufferl.py` I'd patched 3x (dead code for native bf16 runs). Codex (gpt-5.5 xhigh, plan tool + CUDA-doc lookup) implemented + Claude reviewed:
- **`vendor/PufferLib/src/pufferlib.cu` `ppo_loss_compute`:** `raw_logratio = total_log_prob - old_logp; ratio = __expf(fminf(10, fmaxf(-10, raw_logratio)))` — bounds ratio to [4.5e-5, 22026] (far below the exp(88.7) cliff) while the RAW logratio still feeds the `old_kl`/`approx_kl` diagnostics (so the heavy-tail canary stays visible). Plus a non-finite-input guard (new `ppo_zero_element_grads` helper): if old_logp/total_log_prob/adv_normalized/val_pred is non-finite → ratio=1, zero all grads (logits+logstd+value), `goto reduce` (element contributes 0 to losses). Value-loss block relocated after the guard.
- **`vendor/PufferLib/src/muon.cu`:** new `muon_norm_ok(sum_sq)=isfinite&&>=0`; `muon_nesterov`+`muon_weight_update` take the global grad-norm ptr and EARLY-RETURN (skip the weight update, momentum buffer preserved) when the norm is non-finite; `muon_clip_norm`/`muon_norm_apply` write 0 on a bad norm. Belt-and-suspenders against any residual non-finite grad.
- **CLAUDE REVIEW:** both edits correct — clamp keeps raw logratio for metrics (F8-consistent), guard neutralizes cleanly, `goto reduce` is legal (label outside the block scope), muon skip preserves momentum. APPROVED.
- **BUILD:** clean rebuild on japan, `precision_bytes 2` (native bf16 confirmed — THE path the Python patches missed), no compile fixes needed.
- **VALIDATION:** relaunched the threat A/B (warm threat_warm.bin, identical config); ran to **181.9M+ steps with ZERO nan/inf** (independently re-verified by Claude: 0 nan/inf lines in the whole post-fix log, policy 0.007/value 0.005/entropy 0.258 all finite, tds 0.74 healthy), past BOTH the 102M (threat) and ~190M (control) death points. `bad_nonfinite_count 0` → the element/muon guards never fired; the CLAMP alone is the operative fix (the logratio was finite-huge, not non-finite). old_kl still swings 40-300 (raw, unclamped diagnostic) but ratio is bounded → no overflow. The threat-annuity A/B is now LIVE and will produce a real verdict (its first ever clean run) + the camping canary watch (D149/D150).
- **COMMIT:** fork (vendor/PufferLib, branch 4.0) `f14b71c` "Clamp native PPO logratio and guard non-finite grads", scoped to ONLY src/pufferlib.cu + src/muon.cu (unrelated pre-existing fork mods left untouched).
DURABLE FOLLOW-UP (not blocking, per D153 F9): the clamp is a band-aid; old_kl 40-300 means the native bf16-rollout vs fp32-train logprob NON-PARITY is real and large — many samples get clamped to ratio=22026/4.5e-5 = bounded but noisy gradient. The durable fix is logprob parity (store/reuse the rollout kernel's logprob in train, or train native fp32). This affects EVERY native run's sample efficiency (not just threat) and is worth an upstream PufferLib fix alongside task #58. LESSON CODIFIED: for native-backend numerics, the loss/optimizer math lives in `src/pufferlib.cu` + `src/muon.cu`, NOT `torch_pufferl.py` (which native runs never execute — `pufferl.py:203` selects `_C` unless `--slowly`; `torch_pufferl.py:21` refuses a bf16 `_C`). Confirm `_C.precision_bytes` and that the patched path actually executes BEFORE concluding a fix is inert.

**D155 — BALL-ADVANCEMENT TELEMETRY added (Codex impl, Claude review) to diagnose threat-arm camping; restart baseline fwd_adv ~7 sq/possession = healthy advancing, NOT camping at start (2026-06-18, main-repo 5525a9e).** Alex's camping diagnostic: "from pickup, how many squares did the ball move?" Two per-episode dashboard stats (puffer/bloodbowl/bloodbowl.h + binding.c), averaged over the episode's possessions:
- **`ball_fwd_adv`** = net squares the ball advanced toward the holding team's ATTACKING endzone, pickup→possession-end. Camping ⇒ ~0; advancing ⇒ high.
- **`ball_path_len`** = total ball path (Σ per-step Chebyshev) over the same window. Pairing the two separates camping (low fwd, low path) from the OSCILLATION/shuffle pathology (low fwd, HIGH path) from clean advance (high fwd, path≈fwd).
IMPL: Codex refactored the existing inline possession-transition logic into a shared `bbe_update_ball_possession(env, scored)` serving BOTH the ball gain/loss reward AND the telemetry, reusing the `possessor` state machine (no parallel detector). `bbe_start/end_ball_possession` record pickup-fwd (in the team's attack orientation via `bbe_forward_coord`) and accumulate fwd_adv + path; ball tracked via carrier position; TD captured before score-reset. CLAUDE REVIEW: (1) REWARD-PRESERVING — `possessor` is used ONLY by ball_gain/loss (gated `pay_rewards`); the threat run has ball_gain 0.05 so behavior is identical to pre-refactor; for zero-ball-reward configs possessor now updates unconditionally but nothing else reads it → no reward-dynamics change (Alex's "telemetry must not change rewards" constraint SATISFIED). (2) telemetry correct — orientation empirically validated (fwd_adv POSITIVE ⇒ advancing-toward-endzone direction right), Chebyshev king-move distance, clean possession state machine matching the original transitions, no path double-count. (3) no obs/action/RNG impact. BUILD: native bf16 rebuilt on japan, `precision_bytes 2`, the D154 NaN fix (fork f14b71c `raw_logratio`/clamp) confirmed still present + losses finite. RESTART: threat A/B relaunched UNCHANGED (k=0.03, warm threat_warm.bin) — lost the prior ~699M (Alex approved; only way to instrument given one-GPU/no-checkpoint; scientifically a re-run of the same early arm). FIRST VALUES: **ball_fwd_adv ≈ 6.7-7.2, ball_path_len ≈ 8.8-9.1** (path≥|fwd|, ratio ~0.78 = fairly direct, little wasted motion) — the warm-started policy advances the ball ~7 squares/possession at restart = HEALTHY, not camping. This is the BASELINE; the camping test is whether fwd_adv DROPS (toward 0, or path/fwd ratio rises = oscillation) as the threat reward shapes the policy over training. Commit 5525a9e (main repo, bloodbowl.h+binding.c only), pushed. WATCH: ball_fwd_adv + tds together to the ~10-14B verdict window; if fwd_adv collapses while possession_rate spikes ⇒ camping confirmed ⇒ halve k to 0.015 (D149/D150 canary).

So the threat-position emphasis was the wrong tree; replaced. Human ball-advancement baseline (recorded-trajectory parser) building in parallel.

**D157 — VIOLENCE ARM CAPPED 28B CLEAN: a decisive win on volume/scoring/advancement, but block SELECTION did not improve. Higher-k sweep arm (violence2) launched (2026-06-19, autonomous).** The violence arm (D156: k_kd 0.1, k_value 0.5, threat dropped, warm threat_warm) ran the full 28B with VIOLENCE_EXIT 0, **zero nan/inf the entire run** (the D154 native-CUDA NaN fix held end-to-end — first 28B clean native run since the fix). RESULTS (vs the threat arm it replaced):
- blocks_thrown 5→**15.7**, knockdowns_inflicted 2→**7.2**, tds 0.35→**1.43** (4x), ball_fwd_adv ~4→**6.97** (now MATCHES the human ~6 sq/possession baseline from the recorded-trajectory parser), possession 0.29→0.21 (LESS camping — refutes the camping worry; the violence economy advances the ball).
- The "violence makes lanes" hypothesis CONFIRMED: more contact drove MORE scoring + advancement, not less. Trajectory: blocks/tds/fwd_adv all rose together and plateaued ~15B.
- **BUT block DISCIPLINE flat:** block_2d_frac 0.45→**0.49** (human 0.77), block_2dred_frac 0.10→**0.11** (human 0.017). KEY FINDING: cranking k_kd/k_value tripled block VOLUME but did NOT shift the dice MIX. Mechanism: k_kd scales reward ∝ p_def_down for ALL blocks; the RATIO between a 2d and a 1d reward is scale-invariant, so more k → more blocks of every kind (incl. ~10% unfavorable 2d-red), not more-selective blocks. To move the MIX you need either convexity (super-linear in p_def_down) or pricing the DOWNSIDE (p_att_down → attacker falls → turnover; currently UNPRICED — a 2d-red has high p_att_down that nothing penalizes at decision time). That turnover-risk pricing is the cardinal-rule-clean lever for discipline (bb_block_ev already exposes p_att_down) — but it's a REWARD-ECONOMY change → defer to Alex review per CLAUDE.md (do not ship a new reward term autonomously).
- CAVEAT: 2d-red isn't necessarily bad — blitzing the CARRIER on a 2d-red to force a turnover is often correct. Can't distinguish "undisciplined" from "aggressive carrier-pressure" without carrier-targeting telemetry (task #64) — which is exactly why #64 matters.
VERDICT METHOD NOTE: tournament confirmation (D46) attempted but `convert_checkpoint.py --to-cuda` chokes on native bf16 pool snapshots (invalid load key — they're native blobs, not torch pickles); deferred (not rabbit-holing per fleet-ops warning). The metric deltas (4x TDs, advancement to human level) are strong enough to proceed; a proper full-game tournament needs the native-checkpoint match path sorted separately.
NEXT (autonomous, sanctioned filed #63): **violence2** — warm from violence_cap (26B, the converged violence policy backed up to training/violence_cap.bin), **k_kd 0.2 / k_value 1.0** (doubled), everything else identical, 12B increment. Tests Alex's "do they need to be even higher?" Early (103M): LIVE, finite, SPS 850K, blocks already 15.7→17.4. PREDICTION (to falsify): higher k → even more volume, mix still ~flat (scale-invariance); if the absolute reward-gap sharpening helps, 2d_frac may tick up modestly. Carrier-targeting telemetry (#64) building in parallel for the NEXT arm. Box never idle.

**D158 — violence2 (k_kd 0.2/k_value 1.0) CONFIRMS scale-invariance: doubling k → MORE blocks, WORSE mix. NET-EV block reward (turnover downside) is the real discipline lever (Alex directive, 2026-06-20).** violence2 capped 12B clean (VIOLENCE2_EXIT 0, 0 nan/inf — native fix holds): blocks_thrown 15.7→**21.1**, knockdowns 7.2→**9.7**, but block_2d_frac 0.49→0.47 (flat) and block_2dred_frac 0.11→**0.13 (WORSE)**. Doubling k bought ~35% more blocks of EVERY kind and did NOT improve selection — exactly the D157 scale-invariance prediction (k scales every block's upside equally; the 2d:1d:2dred ratio is invariant). k-cranking is exhausted as a discipline lever.
ROOT CAUSE of the mix problem: the block reward (bloodbowl.h:2105) is **UPSIDE-ONLY** — `exposure = p_deliver*(k_kd*p_def_down + k_value*p_def_removed*value + k_ball*p_ball_out)`, zero-sum att/def. The only downside is the weak `seq` term (k_seq*p_turnover*pending, k_seq=0.01) which prices wasted ACTIVATIONS, not the turnover. So the agent never sees the actual cost of a 2d-red: its high attacker-down → high **`ev.p_turnover`** (engine already computes it, bb_blockev.h:47) is UNCHARGED. Nothing makes a 2d-red net-negative.
ALEX'S FIX (net-EV at declaration, cardinal-rule clean — all pre-dice EV): block_reward = TAKEDOWN VALUE − TURNOVER COST = `(k_kd*p_def_down + k_value*p_def_removed*value + k_ball*p_ball_out) − k_turnover*p_turnover`. New knob `reward_k_turnover`. MECHANISM: p_turnover(2d-red)≈0.30 vs p_turnover(2d)≈0.03 (≈10×) → charging k_turnover*p_turnover makes 2d-red net-much-worse than 2d → policy shifts the MIX (not just volume). ELEGANCE (Alex's earlier point): it does NOT ban 2d-red — against the ball carrier or a star, p_def_removed*value / p_ball_out is big enough to justify the turnover risk (2d-red-on-carrier-to-spring-the-ball stays +EV); against a backfield lineman it goes net-negative. Self-sorts by target value — the exact behavior we want, and the reason carrier-targeting telemetry (#64, committed 89fa711) ships in the same build to SEE it. NEXT: implement reward_k_turnover (Codex + adversarial review per reward-economy standing pattern), rebuild, launch "netblock" arm warm from violence2_cap (k_kd 0.1, k_value 0.5, k_turnover ~0.15 first guess — SWEEPABLE), carrier telemetry live. Watch block_2dred_frac → toward human 0.017, block_2d_frac → toward 0.77, AND blocks-vs-carrier (is the residual 2d-red carrier-pressure or sloppiness). Box idle ~1h for build is acceptable vs launching another known-dead k-variant.

**D159 — NETBLOCK arm LIVE: net-EV turnover charge IMMEDIATELY drops 2d-red (the mix lever k-cranking couldn't move). Reviewed (Codex impl + adversarial), F2/F4 applied (2026-06-20).** Implemented Alex's net-EV block reward: `block = takedown_value − k_turnover·p_turnover`. Adversarial review (general agent) found 6 items; adjudication:
- **F2 APPLIED (code):** charge `ev.p_turnover` (BLOCK-DICE turnover), NOT `p_own_to` — p_own_to folds the blitz rush-fail turnover which is identical for 2d vs 2d-red and dilutes the dice-mix signal. Commit ddabda9.
- **F4 APPLIED (doc):** attacker-only is intentional (turnover is the attacker's own-goal risk; opponent benefit already in their objective terms; crediting defender = double-pay). Commented.
- **F1 APPLIED (config):** zeroed reward_k_seq in the arm (it scales the SAME p_own_to → confounds the knob; with k_seq 0.01·pending~6 it was ~29% of the combined turnover price, and pending-scaling drifts within an episode).
- **F3 APPLIED (config):** pinned k_kd 0.1/k_value 0.5 (violence values) — k-sweep settled (D158, #63 closed), do NOT stack on a live sweep.
- **F6a RESOLVED:** the [-1,1] reward clamp DOES exist (native pufferlib.cu:1532 clamp_precision_kernel + torch_pufferl.py:549) — reviewer's "missing clamp/unbounded value-farming" worry defused. A high-value 2d-red staying +EV is INTENDED self-sorting (Alex: 2d-red-on-carrier is often correct).
- **F7 METHODOLOGY:** success = LOW-value-target 2d-red mix + carrier telemetry, not aggregate — which is why carrier-targeting telemetry (#64, commit 89fa711, reviewed reward-inert: blocks_vs_carrier guarded on target==carrier, carrier_knockdowns uses pre-apply carrier mask) ships in this same build.
ARM (league10-netblock): warm violence_cap, k_kd 0.1/k_value 0.5/k_seq 0/**k_turnover 0.15**, carrier telemetry live, 14B. Native bf16 rebuilt (precision_bytes 2, NaN fix f14b71c intact). EARLY (76M, warm-adapts fast): LIVE, finite, **block_2dred_frac 0.12→0.07-0.08** (turnover charge biting immediately — the scale-INVARIANT k-cranking never moved this), block_2d_frac 0.49→0.51, blocks_thrown 13.8 (volume preserved, not over-suppressed), blocks_vs_carrier 1.29 (telemetry populating). The net-EV design does what cranking couldn't: shifts the MIX, not just volume. WATCH to cap: 2dred → toward human 0.017, 2d → toward 0.77, AND whether residual 2d-red is carrier-concentrated (smart, via blocks_vs_carrier/carrier_knockdowns) vs lineman-sloppy; tds/advancement must not regress (over-caution check). NEXT after cap: if 2d-red still high & carrier-concentrated → working as designed; if lineman-concentrated → raise k_turnover (sweepable). k_turnover 0.15 is a FIRST guess — sweep candidate.

**D163 — ROOT CAUSE of the agent's poor block dice-mix: it UNDER-ASSISTS (Alex's H2 CONFIRMED, 2026-06-20). The agent brings ~HALF the offensive assists humans do on every tier — it blocks without ganging up, so more dice land unfavorable.** Measured via a new `block_tier × {is_carrier, off_assists}` telemetry crossing (env, commit 15f44c5) — agent eval on netblock_cap (513 games) vs the human corpus (32,483 blocks / 401 games, 1.4% engine-tier-vs-recorded mismatch audit). Matched mean offensive-assists-per-block:
| tier | agent | human |
| 1d   | 0.28  | 0.55  |
| 2d   | 0.52  | 0.94  |
| 2d-red | 0.09 | 0.17 |
Agent ≈ 0.5× human assists UNIFORMLY. This is the structural cause of both elevated 2d-red (0.05-0.06 vs human 0.017) AND depressed 2d-frac (0.54-0.59 vs human 0.77): humans turn marginal blocks favorable by bringing assists; the agent throws the same blocks with half the gang-up support. H1 (carrier-pressure) only PARTIAL: agent 2d-red IS more carrier-concentrated than human (0.26 vs 0.11) so SOME red dice are deliberate pressure, but 74% of agent 2d-red is NOT on the carrier → carrier-pressure can't explain the bulk (Claude's "probably carrier pressure" was mostly WRONG; Alex's skepticism correct). CORROBORATION: netblock2 (k_turnover 0.30, D162) made blocks more SELECTIVE (1d→2d) but couldn't FLOOR 2d-red → the residual isn't under-priced, it's structural (no better option in-policy because no assist was set up). WHY the agent under-assists (hypothesis): the block-EV reward (k_kd/k_value) already makes ASSISTED blocks more valuable (more assists → higher p_def_down → more reward), so the gradient EXISTS — but the SETUP move (positioning a teammate adjacent to the enemy to provide the assist) is UNREWARDED and DISTAL from the terminal block; the assist-provider isn't credited, so the agent doesn't learn the multi-step "gang up THEN block" coordination. This is a credit-assignment/positioning gap, not a pricing gap → raising k_turnover/k_kd won't fix it (proven by netblock2). CANDIDATE INTERVENTIONS: (a) **assist-EV reward** — credit a move by the offensive-assist EV it provides to a teammate's potential block (the bb_block_ev p_def_down DELTA the assist enables, decision-time/pre-dice, anti-farming-disciplined) — the mirror of pricing the block; (b) **BC-toward-human positioning** (humans assist; block-decision-weighted BC-CE would teach gang-ups — connects to the reward-discovery plan's BC-CE direction + D33's "state-averaged BC misses block behavior"); (c) obs feature: an "assistable enemy" plane so the agent SEES assist opportunities. Telemetry committed (block_2dred_carrier_frac, offassist_{1d,2d,3d,2dred}) + tools/bb_blockstats.c (human-corpus parser, reusable). NEXT: design + review the assist-EV reward (standing reward-economy review pattern), warm-start probe to test if it raises offassist toward human.

**D164 — ASSIST-POTENTIAL probe LAUNCHED (the D163 fix; bidirectional design from Alex's pressure-test, 2026-06-21).** After D163 (agent under-assists ~0.5×human), designed an assist reward and pressure-tested it with Alex. KEY DESIGN MOVE (Alex's bidirectionality question): a one-directional "reward providing an assist" is WRONG — it ignores removing ENEMY assists (blitzing an enemy off my blocker to free up my block), which is half of real BB. Fix = a **zero-sum telescoping potential** Φ = team aggregate contact block-favorability (Σ over my standing pieces adjacent to a standing enemy of max p_def_down), measured at settled own-turn-end (possession-annuity pattern). BIDIRECTIONAL by construction: adding my assist raises a contact's p_def_down (d0↑); blitzing an enemy that was defensively-assisting my contact raises my p_def_down (d0↑) AND drops the enemy's favorability (d1↓) → doubly credited via r0=k*(d0−d1). PBRS-ish (telescoping, can't double-pay k_kd by accumulation) + cardinal-rule clean (pre-dice bb_block_ev). CHEAP (learned from the threat-annuity 8× scar): Φ bounded to EXISTING adjacent contacts only — O(≤16 pieces × 8 squares), bb_block_ev on real adjacencies, NO per-square clones. Impl: `bb_team_contact_favorability` (bb_blockev.c), hook at the possession/threat turn-boundary site (bloodbowl.h:2412), `reward_k_assist` knob default 0, mutual-exclusion guard with reward_carrier_threat, `ep_contact_fav` telemetry. Committed 9d5a736; native built (precision_bytes 2, NaN fix raw_logratio intact), default-0 SPS not regressed. PROCESS NOTE: the Codex + adversarial-Opus pressure-tests both FAILED on infra (Codex over-explored 8h no verdict; Opus API ConnectionRefused) — pivoted to treating the LIVE probe + canaries as the empirical pressure-test (more reliable than stuck agents); Claude reviewed the diff directly (Φ bounded ✓, hook zero-sum/telescoping ✓, bidirectional ✓). PROBE (league10-assist): warm netblock_cap, netblock economy (k_kd 0.1/k_value 0.5/k_seq 0/k_turnover 0.15) + **reward_k_assist 0.03**, 12B. EARLY (32M): LIVE, finite, **SPS 609K** (~28% slower from Φ eval — bounded design avoided the threat-annuity 3× hit), 2d 0.506, 2dred 0.058, tds 1.40. CANARY (watch to cap): block_2d_frac UP toward human 0.77 + block_2dred_frac DOWN toward 0.017 (the GOAL — assists convert bad→good dice) AND tds/ball_fwd_adv HELD (not Φ-camping/farming). If 2d-red drops + 2d rises + scoring held → the assist potential works → graduate (cross-ancestor + from-scratch gate per D161). DISK: box healthy 63% post-D162-prune; standing-fix (launch-script snapshot pruning) still TODO so disk-full can't recur.

**D165 — ASSIST POTENTIAL FAILED (k_assist 0.03): did NOT raise the agent's assists. Clean negative + a strategic fork (2026-06-22).** league10-assist capped 12B clean (ASSIST_EXIT 0, 0 nan, SPS 609K — bounded Φ cost ~28%, NOT the threat-annuity 3x). DIRECT off-assist measure (training telemetry) vs netblock_cap (D163) and human:
| tier | netblock_cap | assist_cap | human |
| 1d   | 0.28 | 0.22 | 0.55 |
| 2d   | 0.52 | 0.50 | 0.94 |
| 2dred| 0.09 | 0.06 | 0.17 |
Off-assists FLAT/slightly-DOWN; block_2d_frac flat (0.543→0.540), 2dred flat (0.056→0.062). The bidirectional telescoping assist potential did NOT make the agent gang up. (It DID raise block volume 14→16.8 and tds 1.46→**1.66** — more aggressive/higher-scoring, but via more blocks, not better-assisted ones.)
LEADING EXPLANATION — PBRS optimum-invariance (the flip side of the design's elegance): a TELESCOPING potential can only SPEED learning of behavior the base reward ALREADY favors; it CANNOT create a new attractor. The base economy (k_kd 0.1 etc.) apparently does NOT make committing a teammate to assist worth its opportunity cost, so the optimum-invariant potential couldn't induce assisting — it just reshaped credit timing (+ slightly more aggression). Cranking k_assist likely won't help if this is right (telescoping nets out regardless of magnitude). This is the deep lesson: to CHANGE behavior toward human (vs speed learning of already-optimal behavior), you need a NON-PBRS push.
THE STRATEGIC FORK (Alex's call — touches the human-like-vs-win-maximal question he's been driving):
(A) **The assist gap may be a FEATURE, not a flaw (D46 discipline: ground inhuman behavior in WINS, not human-stat aesthetics).** The low-assist agent SCORES MORE (tds 1.66). Under self-play win-maximization it may be correctly finding that throwing more blocks + scoring beats slowing down to gang up like risk-averse humans; humans may over-assist out of convention/risk-aversion our win-maximizer doesn't share. TEST: does a higher-assist agent actually WIN more (tournament vs anchors)? If not, the agent is right and "match human assists" is the wrong goal.
(B) **If we DO want human assists, a telescoping potential is the wrong tool** — need either (b1) a NON-telescoping standing assist bonus that genuinely SHIFTS the optimum toward assisting (risk: farming/camping, no longer double-count-free), or (b2) BC/KL-toward-human positioning (the principled way to instill a human CONVENTION that isn't optimal under our reward — connects to the reward-discovery plan's BC-CE direction; humans assist, BC pulls there). (b2) is heavier (native CUDA) but addresses the root: this result is EVIDENCE that human assist behavior is NOT optimal under our current reward, which is exactly when BC-toward-human (not reward shaping) is the right lever.
RECOMMENDATION: don't reflexively crank k_assist (optimum-invariance says it won't work). Either accept the finding pending a strength test (A), or commit to the BC-toward-human path (b2) if we believe human-like blocking is worth instilling. assist_cap backed up. reward_k_assist code stays (default 0, inert). Box idle.

**D166 — DEFENSE RESEARCH SYNTHESIZED → root cause is OPPONENT-QUALITY, not reward design; first move = scripted offense bot, NOT a new reward (2026-06-22).** Alex: human beats the bots 3-0 to 6-0 (worst vs fast teams = defense is the bigger hole than blocking). Gathered defense knowledge: existing AndyDavo #07 Defensive Setup Guide (reviewed) + 4-agent web fan-out (`analysis/defense/defense-research-collected.md`, sources: grumbbl, bbtactics, thetacklezone, goonhammer, bloodbowlstrategies, Bonehead). CONVERGENT CORE: force-the-dodge (more dice=more failure), screen-don't-blitz, two-deep columns at 2-sq spacing, **keep a DEEP SAFETY** (the 6-0 failure mode — one broken screen = walk-in), mark-carrier-from-endzone-side + the one-good-blitz/turn, roster-conditioned mark-vs-screen (gated on relative speed + Tackle skills). Codex synthesis (`.codex-reviews/defense-paths-forward.md`) — OPINIONATED BOTTOM LINE: **"don't invent 5 more defensive rewards; make the agent defend against something that can actually score."** ROOT CAUSE: defensive skills ARE optimal vs a competent attacker, but the agent only ever faced its weak self-play mirror (can't punish a missing screen) → no gradient toward defense; per D165 PBRS can't induce behavior the opponents don't make necessary. So the lever is OPPONENT-QUALITY first, reward-shaping only as bounded scaffold after. RECOMMENDED FIRST EXPERIMENT (cheapest decisive test, answers the causal question): (1) build a scripted **offense_bot** (heuristic cage/advance/score) via the existing `scripted_opponent` hook (beside contact_bot.h); (2) add defensive-canary telemetry (deep_safety_count/zero, carrier min-dodges/GFIs-to-our-EZ, carrier-path zero-TZ squares, carrier_marked, bot turns-to-score, bot TDs); (3) baseline champion vs the bot; (4) train 3-5B warm-started vs the offense bot with the CURRENT reward economy, NO new defensive reward; (5) re-eval. PASS/FAIL: defense improves w/o reward changes → opponent-quality is the lever → graduate to hard-opponent/asymmetric-frozen-attacker curriculum; else layer bounded scaffolds IN ORDER: R12 reward_defensive_threat (already built, off — cheap A/B) → obs scalars (opp_carrier_min_dodges_to_ez, deep_safety_count, carrier_path_zero_tz, cage_corners_marked — spare obs bytes, no BBE_OBS_SIZE change) → narrow NON-PBRS deep-safety + lane-coverage rewards (lane = zero-TZ squares on carrier→EZ min-cost path via ONE bb_reach_field_compute Dijkstra, NOT per-square clones — avoid the D150 threat-annuity 8x scar) → BC-toward-human defense only if hard-opponent training still won't produce human screens. OBS GAP confirmed: agent can't directly SEE scoring lane / deep-safety / cage corners (must derive from raw rows under sparse pressure) → the scalar obs features are a real complement. Promote ONLY by anchored-strength (win/score vs frozen anchors + held-out scripted offense), never self-play TDs or prettier columns (D46). SEQUENCING: finish the block/turnover thread (turnover3, promising — 2d 0.625/2dred 0.045 at 1.1B) first per Alex, THEN the defense pivot starts with the scripted-offense stress test. NOTE: the scripted offense bot is the crux + non-trivial (cage/advance/score heuristic) — get Alex's input on its design/strength before building.

**D167 — OFFENSE BOT (bashy cage-advance) BUILT + RIGOROUSLY VALIDATED (2026-06-22, commit e27ecaa + tools/bb_offense_test.c).** The defense-curriculum keystone: a scripted bashy cage-advance attacker (puffer/bloodbowl/offense_bot.h, `bbe_offense_bot_pick`, selected via scripted_opponent + scripted_opponent_type=1). BLOCKING RULE (Alex, corrected): throw blocks ordered by p_def_down, gated on SKILL-AWARE own-turnover risk `ev.p_turnover <= 0.17` (BBE_OB_BLOCK_TURNOVER_MAX) — admits 1d-WITH-Block (~0.167, only skull turns over), excludes 1d-no-skill (~0.33) and 2d-red (defender picks). NOT a crude ndice>=2 rule (that bug — banning all 1d — was caught + corrected). RIGOROUS BEHAVIORAL SUITE (tools/bb_offense_test.c, 300 games each, Alex's 3 questions): (1) vs PASSIVE (does-nothing) opp: terminates 300/300, 0 non-termination, bot 1.34 TD/game, scored-in 73%, SHUTOUT 27%; (2) vs RANDOM: 1.65/game, shutout 17%; (3) BOT-vs-BOT: terminates 300/300, 0 infinite loops, HOME 0.83 / AWAY 0.48 TD/game, BOTH score (197 & 118 games) — not a stalemate; defense-probe: 0.0% immediate-END_TURN (never degenerates to passing turns). VERDICT: passes the critical pathology gates (termination, no deterministic loop, both-score, no passivity, zero red blocks 190/190 gated). The 27% shutout-vs-nothing is BALL-RECOVERY (its defense), NOT a finishing flaw — proven by: vs RANDOM (which fumbles → hands the bot the ball more) it scores MORE + shuts out LESS, so shutouts = games where the kicking opp received and the bot couldn't pry the ball loose. The bot is a competent ATTACKER, mediocre BALL-RECOVERER. CURRICULUM IMPLICATION (confirms D166/Codex): run the defense stress test ASYMMETRICALLY / from opponent-has-ball demo states (agent ALWAYS defends vs the offense bot holding the ball) — bypasses the bot's ball-recovery weakness, isolates the agent's defense vs a competent cage-advance. NEXT (after turnover3 caps): baseline current champion vs offense_bot from opponent-has-ball states + defensive-canary telemetry (D166), then train ~3-5B asymmetric defense vs offense_bot with NO new defensive reward → test if defense emerges (the opponent-quality hypothesis).

**D168 — STANDING RULE: probe run-length is set by PLATEAU, not a fixed step budget (Alex, 2026-06-22).** The fixed 12B/28B budgets were a pragmatic default, NOT principled — they can stop a run mid-trajectory. NEW STANDING RULE for reward-economy / behavioral DIAGNOSTIC probes:
- **Extend-on-still-improving, stop-on-plateau.** Do NOT declare a verdict at a fixed budget. Track the primary metric(s) the probe is testing (e.g., block_2dred_frac, offassist_2d). At each cap, compare the metric's value over the last ~2B-step window to the prior ~2B window. If still moving beyond noise → **warm-restart from the cap (chained) and continue** until it flattens. If flat (Δ < ~noise) OR the verdict is already decisively clear (clearly working / clearly dead) → stop + record.
- **Judge "still improving" on the metric that MATTERS:** for a behavioral probe, the behavioral curve (off-assists, dice-mix); for a STRENGTH/final run, Elo-vs-frozen-anchors — and there also stop on the OVEROPTIMIZATION downturn (EvalStop, k=2 consecutive Elo drops; D161), not just plateau, because a proxy can keep climbing toward human while true strength stalls/regresses.
- **Probe vs production:** probes stop at behavioral plateau / clear verdict (cheap, answer the question); final policy runs go to a real budget / Elo plateau for maximum strength.
- Mechanism: chained warm-restart from the latest snapshot/cap with the same reward config + pool preseed (the lineage continues seamlessly; total-timesteps can't be raised mid-run). LIVE CASE: turnover3 off-assists still climbing 0.52→0.60 (3.6B→4.7B) → it will NOT have plateaued at the 12B cap → on cap, evaluate the trajectory and CHAIN-EXTEND if still moving, rather than calling the verdict at an arbitrary 12B. Longer-term: automate plateau/EvalStop detection instead of eyeballing (the reward-discovery-plan guardrail).

PLATEAUED by ~1.5B (D168 windowed trajectory: 2d 0.60-0.62, 2d-red 0.04-0.05, off-assists 0.47-0.57 = noise, no sustained climb), capped clean (TURNOVER3_EXIT 0, 0 nan). FINAL: block_2d 0.608 (netblock 0.543 → human 0.77), block_2dred **0.044** (netblock 0.056, the best yet → human 0.017), tds 1.563 (held). VERDICT: Alex's turnover-cost diagnosis CONFIRMED — properly pricing the lost-activations cost (pending-scaled) shifts block SELECTION further toward human than the flat k_turnover alone (netblock). BUT the predicted ASSIST side-effect was WEAK/noisy: off-assists stayed ~0.51 (my earlier "0.52→0.60 climb" was single-frame NOISE, corrected per D168) — the agent achieves the better mix mainly via SELECTIVITY (throwing fewer, safer blocks) not via ganging up. So: turnover-cost is a real block-discipline win; assisting remains under-human (the D165 finding stands — assisting isn't induced by either the assist potential OR the turnover cost, consistent with the opponent-quality thesis that good positioning isn't gradient-incentivized in weak self-play). turnover3_cap backed up. **D170 — DEFENSE BASELINE: the trained champion's defense concedes ~2× what a simple scripted bot's defense concedes (2026-06-22). Alex's "I'd win 3-0 to 6-0" thesis CONFIRMED empirically.** Ran turnover3_cap (the settled-economy champion) FROZEN (lr=0) vs the scripted bashy cage-advance offense_bot (D167), bot = team1, full games, def-canary build. Over n=379 dashboard frames (≈196M steps of rollout): **tds_t0 (champion offense, vs bot defense) = 0.565 · tds_t1 (bot offense, vs CHAMPION defense) = 1.156** → the bot outscores the champion **2.05:1**. Symmetric read: the champion's DEFENSE allows 1.156 TD/ep; the *bot's* defense allows only 0.565 — the champion is ~2× leakier on defense than a deterministic script that just forms a cage and grinds forward. This is the opponent-quality failure (D166): self-play from a weak prior plateaus at a mutually-incompetent equilibrium — the champion never learned to screen/keep-a-safety/wall-lanes because no self-play opponent ever punished the absence. The offense_bot is the missing "competent offense." MECHANISM NOTE: the def-canary fields (def_deep_safety, def_carrier_path_zerotz, def_carrier_min_dodges, def_carrier_marked_frac — bloodbowl.h:209-213) ARE computed in-env (ep_* sums L500-504) but are NOT yet wired to the Log struct/dashboard, so this baseline rests on the scoreboard (tds_t1) not the mechanistic readout; wiring them is a deferred nice-to-have (the scoreboard already settles the question). UNBLOCK: turnover3_cap is a 16MB torch-float checkpoint — the whole block-economy lineage is TORCH — so the "native rejects scripted_opponent+learning (pufferl.py:191)" wrinkle is MOOT: the defense run trains on the torch backend (--slowly), which implements the scripted-row filter the guard demands. NEXT (D166 experiment): warm turnover3_cap, scripted_opponent bot=team1, learning ON, NO new reward, ~4B torch — does facing competent offense alone teach defense (tds_t1 falls toward the bot's own 0.565)? Caveat to hold: training vs ONE deterministic bot risks overfitting its patterns — first-read hypothesis test, validate later vs held-out/anchors.

**D170-CORRECTION — the block-economy lineage is NATIVE, not torch (I misread turnover3's 399K SPS as torch; it's native-on-the-slow-judge-GPU).** turnover3_cap.bin starts with raw float bytes `\xe7\xbaR>` (a native weight blob, biases not stored separately), NOT a torch zip (`PK\x03\x04`). So the native guard (pufferl.py:191, scripted_opponent+learning rejected — native lacks scripted-row exclusion) REALLY DOES block training the champion vs the scripted bot natively. Resolution path that worked: (1) PyTorch 2.6 flipped torch.load default to weights_only=True → patched both load sites in `vendor/PufferLib/pufferlib/torch_pufferl.py` (L791/L802) to `weights_only=False` (we trust our own checkpoints; correct compat fix — keep). (2) `training/convert_checkpoint.py --to-torch` converts the native champion → torch state_dict (turnover3_torch.bin, hidden 512×3, obs 2782) — **biases zero-filled** (D45 native↔torch limitation), so the warm-start is mildly degraded and re-learns biases in the first frames. Defense training then runs on the torch backend (--slowly), which HAS the scripted-row filter the guard demands.

**D171 — DEFENSE1 LAUNCHED + EARLY POSITIVE SIGNAL: facing the competent offense bot rapidly drops conceded TDs (2026-06-22, IN PROGRESS).** Warm turnover3_torch (champion), torch --slowly, scripted_opponent bot=team1 (bot runs the bashy cage offense; learner=team0 plays full games incl. defending the bot's drives), NO new reward (identical settled block economy), lr 0.00028, ent 0.009, 4B (~4.4h @ 253K SPS on box-1). At ~31M steps: **tds_t1 (bot scoring on the champion's defense) 1.156 (D170 frozen baseline) → ~0.83**, tds_t0 (champion offense) held ~0.56. Conceding down ~28% almost immediately → strongly consistent with the D166 opponent-quality thesis (self-play never punished the defensive hole; one competent attacker does). CAVEATS before any verdict: (a) only 31M/4B steps — NEED the plateau; (b) zero-biased warm-start conflates bias-recovery with defense-learning in the early frames — the verdict is whether tds_t1 keeps falling toward the bot's OWN defensive allowance (~0.565) well past bias-recovery; (c) training vs ONE deterministic bot risks pattern-overfitting (validate later vs held-out/anchors); (d) illegal_frac ~0.12 (watch; not 1.0-era broken). def-canary fields still not surfaced to the dashboard, so monitoring is on tds_t1. **D172 — BC BOTTLENECK SETTLED: it is NOT data volume (the ~25k-game corpus is saturated), and NOT mainly the discarded biases. The ceiling is the BC recipe/representation (2026-06-22).** Alex asked why 25k human games isn't enough for a functional bot and whether to scrape every FUMBBL game ever (incl. older rules). Ran two controlled experiments on box-1 (fixed val set = 413,130 pairs / 2,446 replays, checksum-verified identical across all 6 runs; 3000 steps cosine, seed 42; both defense1 + the BBTV server ran undisturbed). (1) **DATA-SCALING CURVE = SATURATED:** val exact 0.448 / 0.451 / 0.450 / 0.451 at train-frac 0.25 / 0.50 / 0.75 / 1.00 (424k → 1.67M pairs). Quadrupling the data buys ZERO (0.003 spread, inside noise); per-head acc constant to 3 decimals. **More data — including a mass older-rules scrape — is NOT justified.** (2) **BIAS-IMPACT = real-but-minor:** zeroing bc_v4's biases (the ones the native/CUDA bias-free pipeline discards at warm-start; decoder bias max |4.8|) costs only **−0.0133 val exact** (0.5077 → 0.4944, ~2.6% rel), spread across heads (type −1.5pts). So my earlier "bias-drop is the headline culprit" hunch was OVERSTATED — it's a measurable edge worth recovering if cheap (and defense1, being torch, already avoids it), NOT a dominant lever. CONCLUSION: the BC ceiling (~0.45–0.51 val exact) is bounded by the **model/recipe** — capacity, the **iid zero-recurrent-state (no-memory) BC formulation** (consistent with D35: sequence context > more data > bigger policy), and the inherent label noise of imitating diverse human play — not by dataset size or biases. The real levers for a functional/defending bot are therefore: (a) sequence-context BC (bc_v5, D35) to break the no-memory ceiling, (b) preserve the human prior THROUGH RL (KL-to-bc, stop annealing to zero) so self-play stops eroding it (the turnover3 "looks untrained on defense" = D170 erosion), (c) explicit defensive shaping + competent opponents (the cage-bot fix + defense pivot). Caveat: single seed, cosine-endpoint noise ~±0.02 (flatness robust to it); bias eval is exact/deterministic. Artifacts in box `/tmp/` (curve_*, bc_v4_nobias.bin, edited bc_pretrain.py); original bc_pretrain.py restored.

**D173 — DEFENSE1 verdict (champion trained vs the cage-bot, no new reward): opponent-quality direction CONFIRMED but the run is confounded; no checkpoint saved (lesson).** Warm turnover3_torch, torch --slowly, scripted_opponent bot=team1, identical settled economy, ran clean to EXIT 0 (~1B effective learner-steps). Conceded **tds_t1 1.156 (D170 frozen baseline) → 0.718 final (−38%)**; champion offense tds_t0 0.565 → ~0.474 (slight dip). So facing a competent-ISH attacker does pull the champion's defense down toward the bot's own ~0.565 allowance — the D166 opponent-quality thesis holds directionally. THREE confounds keep this from being the verdict: (1) it trained against the **pre-fix** cage-bot (D167/offense_bot 150a1fb fixed AFTER launch — the old bot walked its carrier into contact, so the champion partly "learned to punish a bad ball-handler," not general defense); (2) zero-biased warm-start (D170-corr); (3) one deterministic opponent (overfit risk). LESSON: the run had NO snapshot interval set, so NO checkpoint was saved — the trained defender is gone (only metrics survive). For any keeper run, set `--train.checkpoint-interval`/`--selfplay.snapshot-interval` AND back the cap to Mac (D160). CLEAN RE-RUN (ready, queued): **defense2 = warm turnover3_torch vs the FIXED cage-bot, with snapshots**, on the now-idle box-1 — the box is held free for the imminent bc-context A/B; launch defense2 after (or in parallel, BC is GPU-light). The strategic frame also shifted today (D172): opponent-quality is necessary but not sufficient — the champion is bias-free + never learned defense; the levers are bc-context (in progress), KL-to-bc-through-RL, and defensive shaping + competent opponents.

**D174 — BC TEMPORAL-CONTEXT SCREEN: NULL. Frame-stacked context does ~nothing because obs-v4 already encodes the within-turn state. The long-standing "sequence context" lever is, empirically, not the lever (2026-06-23).** Path-A cheap screen (context features computed from the ordered pairs at BC-load time, NO engine change; built by Codex, 2 review loops + a loop-3 obs-redundancy check; iid arm reproduces D172's 0.451 EXACTLY, checksum-pinned identical val set, strict --head-loss legacy ablation). Four arms, val exact: **iid 0.451 · structural 0.450 (−0.001) · structural+last-action 0.453 · last-action-only 0.453**. All within the ±0.02 cosine-endpoint noise band (D172). READS: (1) **structural features = NULL** — because the within-turn context they encode is ALREADY in obs-v4: per-player `BB_PF_USED`("activated this turn")/`BB_PF_ACTIVATING` flags (player bytes [4][5]), the [784+8..13] blitz/pass/handoff/foul/ttm/secure-used-this-turn scalars, rerolls [784+5/6], deciding/active [768+10/11]. A linear layer already reads all of it. (2) **last-action history** (the only signal NOT in the pre-action obs) gives a negligible +0.002 (within noise) AND is the copycat-prone feature — so even that hair is suspect and would need a Path-B rollout to trust. CONCLUSION: the BC ceiling (~0.45–0.51) is NOT from missing observable/temporal context — the obs is already information-rich. This triangulates with the loop-1 research (AlphaStar Unplugged: "no-memory ≥ LSTM for BC"; MimicBot single-frame won) and D172 (data-saturated). The "we keep naming sequence context and never build it" tension (D35/D45/D47/D140) is RESOLVED: we finally built it (the cheap, correct version) and it does ~nothing — so we can stop naming it. IMPLICATION for recurrence (the queued A/B): its cheap win (short history) just showed negligible, and its remaining value (long-horizon intent memory) is exactly what AlphaStar found doesn't beat no-memory for BC → recurrence is LIKELY low-ROI; recommend NOT spending the multi-day build, pivot instead. THE REAL LEVERS (re-confirmed, research-backed): (b) **KL-to-bc anchor THROUGH RL** — stop annealing to zero so self-play stops eroding the prior (AlphaStar persistent-KL, MimicBot hybrid-loss, Diplomacy piKL all independently endorse this; it's the turnover3 "untrained on defense" = D170 erosion fix); (c) **defensive shaping + competent opponents** — the fixed cage-bot (150a1fb) + defense2 vs it. Artifacts: training/bc_context*.py (committed), box-1 logs/bc_screen/, checkpoints/bc_context_*_head-legacy.bin.

**D175 — KL-ANCHOR experiment designed + reviewed; decision = run the CHEAP persistent-CE anchor A/B first (config-only), build KL-to-frozen only if null (2026-06-23).** Lever: "preserve the human prior THROUGH RL" (Alex "do 1, lean in"). Root cause confirmed: the champion lineage trained `bc_coef=0` (anchor-free, D57/D58) → self-play pruned the human defensive prior (D170 erosion). Design doc `docs/kl-anchor-design.md` (research agent + my review). KEY TECHNIQUE FINDING: our existing anchor is an iid masked-CE on human pairs scored ONLY on corpus states (torch-only; native has NONE, grep-confirmed); the principled fix is a PERSISTENT KL-to-frozen-BC on the policy's OWN visited states (AlphaStar "critical", piKL, MimicBot-in-BB) — because the erosion lives in off-corpus self-play states the CE never touches. STAGING (D140 cheap-first): run the persistent-CE A/B now (free), build KL-to-frozen (~1 day torch, distinct frozen-BC handle — NOT the self-play enemy `frozen_policy`) only if it nulls. EXPERIMENT: **A0 anchor-OFF control (= the clean defense2 re-run vs the FIXED cage-bot) vs A1 bc_coef=1.0 PERSISTENT (bc_coef_anneal 0, no decay)**, warm turnover3_torch, torch --slowly, vs fixed cage-bot=team1, turnover3's settled BLOCK economy UNCHANGED, 4B, **--train.checkpoint-interval SET + cap-to-Mac** (D173 lesson). MEASURE: frozen-eval `tds_t1` vs cage-bot (champion 1.156 / opp-only 0.718 / bot-floor 0.565) — A1≤A0 = anchor preserves defense; + tds_t0/tournament cost guardrail; + bc_acc trace; + def-canary `def_carrier_marked_frac` IF wired (optional). MY REVIEW FIXES vs the doc's draft command: (1) base on run_defense1.sh NOT run_synthesis_c.sh (the doc's k-half economy mismatches turnover3's block economy — both arms must use turnover3's exact economy); (2) verify bc_coef CLI flag spellings (else set in bloodbowl.ini); (3) canary-wiring deferred (tds_t1 settles the leak per D170; canary = mechanism nice-to-have). RISKIEST (acknowledged): iid CE may not reach the eroded off-corpus states → A1≈A0 → the null is the green-light to build KL-to-frozen. Confounds (shared by both arms, so the CONTRAST is clean): zero-biased warm-start, single deterministic opponent.

**D176 — KL-ANCHOR A/B VERDICT: the BC anchor FAILS; OPPONENT QUALITY is the defense lever (2026-06-23). Both arms capped at 2B vs the FIXED cage-bot, torch, warm turnover3_torch, settled block economy.** Frozen reference: champion baseline `tds_t1=1.156` / `tds_t0=0.565` (D170). RESULTS (training-time, last-30 avg): **A1 (persistent CE anchor, bc_coef=1.0 constant, on validation/pairs_v4): tds_t0=0.000, tds_t1=0.765, episode_return≈−2.0** — the full-strength iid CE anchor **WRECKED the policy** (offense collapsed to zero, net-negative game; bc_acc held 0.41 / bc_loss→1.87, so the anchor "worked" mechanically but pinned the policy off the reward manifold — the D45/design-risk-4 outcome, plus design-risk-1: the iid CE never reaches the off-corpus defensive states). **A0 (anchor-OFF control = the clean defense2 vs the FIXED bot): tds_t0=0.292, tds_t1=0.251** with HEALTHY possession/assists (offassist_2d 0.635, possession 0.351). So vs a genuinely competent attacker the champion's **conceding crashed 1.156 → 0.251 (−78%)** and the matchup went from losing 0.57–1.16 to roughly EVEN 0.29–0.25. THE VERDICT: (1) the BC anchor (cheap CE-on-pairs form) is **NOT the fix — it's harmful at strength 1.0**, and its whole "preserve the prior" premise is moot because (2) **OPPONENT QUALITY directly teaches defense** (D166 validated cleanly with the FIXED bot — the flawed bot only got defense1 to 0.718; the fixed bot gets 0.251). DECISION: **do NOT build KL-to-frozen** (anchor mechanism failed + opponent-quality already solves defense); **do NOT pursue the CE anchor further** (A2/0.5 would only cripple offense less, not fix defense). PATH FORWARD: train vs COMPETENT + DIVERSE opponents (the fixed cage-bot + a pool) — the lever that works. CAVEAT: A0/defense2 overfits to ONE deterministic bot (offense 0.292 partly = the bot hogging possession, fewer drives); NEXT = validate defense2 vs held-out/diverse attackers before trusting "general defense." Defenders backed up to Mac: `runs/caps/defense2_cap.bin` (A0, best defender) + the lineage caps. COST PIVOT (D-this-session): fast boxes gone, balance ~$7.4 → box-1 (the last box) STOPPED post-A/B; future training on the free 2070 rig.

**D177 — REPAIRED REWARD 2×2 VERDICT: distance shaping supplies nearly all current scoring learnability, but is a temporary scaffold, not a final utility (2026-07-10).** Frozen R0–R3 screen, paired seeds 42/43, exact `249,954,304` native steps per arm, ≥10,001 final-policy eval games per arm, immutable plan SHA `53d33f442be4a17577ec0fabf0bdff1d2dbf7ac35263a34ac9c8c58c6125a947`; all eight arms passed with zero clip/non-finite/engine-error/demo/fallback telemetry. Equal-seed distance-family main effects were TD/game `+0.76365`, match score `+0.11130`, draw `-0.17869`, possession `+0.07856`, ball-forward `+4.45069`, and ball-path `+4.67103`; it also raised blocks `+2.48105` and 2D-red fraction `+0.01377`. The possession+gain family was much smaller in-screen: TD/game `+0.02807`, score `+0.01038`, possession `+0.01252`. DECISION: keep distance on for the next causal work because removing it currently destroys learnability, but do not call raw `ΔΦ` exact PBRS at `gamma=0.995`; convert to `beta*(gamma*Phi(s')-Phi(s))` or demonstrate non-inferiority while annealing it to zero. Completion proof: `runs/reward-screens/reward-screen-20260709-v1/SCREEN_COMPLETE.json`, SHA `9a060329a3aaffcf38bc84675b7ae1227def913a7a46f2ef9d925c0ad5c498a0`.

**D178 — R0 SURVIVES R2 SCRIPTED TRANSFER; DO NOT REMOVE THE BUNDLED POSSESSION/GAIN FAMILY OR PROMOTE A PRODUCTION REWARD YET (2026-07-13).** R0 versus R2 completed `2 arms × 2 training seeds × 2 deterministic bot styles × 2 sides = 16` cells, ≥1,000 full kickoff games/cell, 16,076 total, strict schema/provenance/integrity gates. Paired R2−R0 match score was `-0.02844` and negative in all eight matched cells; loss rate `+0.04605` and opponent TD/game `+0.07324` were worse in all eight; own TD/game was nearly unchanged (`-0.00598`) while blocks rose `+0.51047`. DECISION: R2 is not transfer-noninferior; retain R0 only as the next-stage experimental baseline. The result does not identify whether the possession annuity, ball-gain event, or interaction supplies the defensive benefit. Next causal screen is distance-on with `{possession+gain, possession-only, gain-only, neither}` at `500M × 2 seeds`, followed by learned-opponent, roster-grid, longer, and second-ancestry confirmation. No production default changes until those gates pass. Evidence: `runs/reward-transfer-20260713-v1/ANALYSIS.json`, SHA `d8b688f78716705d8110ff73eaddbddaef58f67413c65549447cc93ed8f2d5ca`.

**D179 — REPLAY CORPUS MUST BE EDITION-EXACT AND IS OPENING-CENSORED (2026-07-13).** Exact inventory from embedded replay `rulesVersion`, not filenames/directories: 15,347 raw replays = 11,580 BB2025 + 3,767 BB2020; 12,304 BBP shards with 2,085,330 records; 9,170 joined BB2025 shards with 1,622,231 records, of which 9,118 are non-empty and form the strict allowlist (SHA `15d6f67852c6d556009a8f878f730c6fd6c0c45fdf77e1fd8a2b7d1b2c218585`). Turn-depth coverage falls from 9,118 replays at the opening to 35 at the deepest encoded turn; pass/handoff/foul targets combined are only 1,040 records (`0.0641%`), with zero Jump/TTM/Special targets. Corrected genuine-turn BB2025 human possession is `173,200 / 365,449 = 0.47393754` turn-weighted (per-game mean `0.47452514`), excluding 47,599 synthetic observations. DECISION: never mix BB2020 into BB2025 BC, never treat flat-record accuracy or human action rates as the RL objective, and never use this prefix-censored corpus as the sole source for second-half, stalling, comeback, or late-drive policy. Evidence: `runs/replay-audit-20260713/corpus.json` and `runs/replay-audit-20260713/bb2025-nonempty.ids`.

**D180 — BC DATA ACCESS IS NOW BOUNDED STREAMING; REPLAY-FIRST IS THE DEFAULT BUT NOT THE FINAL SAMPLER (2026-07-13).** `training/bc_pretrain.py` now validates shard headers/embedded IDs, accepts strict allowlists, splits by replay, memory-maps shards behind an evict-before-open bounded LRU, returns owning minibatches, and evaluates batchwise. Full strict-corpus probe: 9,118 shards / 1,622,231 records, 7,294/1,824 replay-disjoint split, 4,096 sampled records, observed cache `8/8`, 12.88s, ~179MB measured footprint (227MB max RSS); the historical eager path projected ~10.55GB CPU plus ~5.29GB device memory. DECISION: use replay-first rather than record-weighted sampling for the current compatibility baseline, but next stratify `replay → roster/matchup → turn/drive depth → action family`, cap setup/opening mass, and report group metrics. Replay-first removes long-shard dominance but does not cure opening censorship.

**D181 — FIRST POSSESSION/GAIN DECOMPOSITION ARM REJECTED ON PROVENANCE, NOT REWARD PERFORMANCE (2026-07-13).** The `both/seed-42` arm completed its exact `499,908,608` native steps and 10,080 final-policy games with zero clip/non-finite/engine-error/demo/fallback telemetry, but the screen correctly refused to accept it: its run manifest recorded Puffer patch-bundle SHA `07340d03c26cec5f63230bf56d5a02b2513ccce4c2d5b942fbef9002605217f2`, while the frozen screen contract required `24df29a1a3aa26695b56cbc7c13118cdadc323213798830c03cea80049b9230f`. Root cause was a partial launcher deployment: the screen froze all seven audited Puffer patches, but the remote per-arm launcher still hashed the older five-patch list. DECISION: accept no reward result from this arm and rerun it in a fresh screen after commit-backed deployment. The per-arm launcher now validates an expected frozen patch-bundle hash before starting training, the screen refuses launchers without that fail-fast contract, and regression tests require the same seven patch names in both scripts. This is a provenance rejection only; no production reward or default changes.

**D182 — THE COMPLETED POSSESSION/GAIN SCREEN IS REJECTED; ITS ONE CLIP ALSO EXPOSED AN UNSAFE TERMINAL-COMPOSITION PATH (2026-07-14).** The cleanly redeployed `500M × 2` possession/gain screen completed all eight training/evaluation arms and preserved every final checkpoint/result, but no `SCREEN_COMPLETE.json` was published. The final `both/seed-43` arm had one clipped raw emission in 351,253 training episodes: the only nonzero interval was epoch 3614 at `473,825,280` steps, with one clipped sample among 92 completed games and exactly `0.015` total excess. Its final cumulative train counters were `reward_clip_episodes=1/351253`, `reward_clip_excess=0.015/351253`, with zero non-finite, engine-error, demo, or fallback counters; final eval had 10,047 games and zero integrity counters. The acceptance gate therefore behaved correctly. The retained schema records neither the clipped sign nor terminal/non-terminal context, so the exact historical co-firing components cannot be claimed after the fact; `0.015` equals the rush-cost coefficient but does not prove causation. A code audit nevertheless confirmed an independent structural defect: `bbe_finish_episode` added win/draw/loss to the current action's entire shaping subtotal, so an arbitrary terminal-action scaffold could distort or exceed the learner's `[-1,1]` emission even though TD+result passed static validation. DECISION: reject the whole screen as causal evidence; do not manufacture completion, relax the any-clip gate, run transfer from it, or promote its preliminary factorial. Terminal composition now discards incidental same-action shaping, preserves only explicitly tracked objective reward (TD), then adds result utility; explicitly episode-terminal terms such as quarantined statmatch remain separate and clip-visible. Episode-return accounting follows the reward actually emitted. New telemetry splits terminal from non-terminal clipped samples so recurrence is classifiable. Rerun every compared arm under this single corrected semantic contract before interpreting possession/gain effects; any recurrence still fails closed and requires its own diagnosis. Canonical rejected evidence remains immutable at `runs/reward-screens/possession-gain-screen-20260713-v2` on the audit host; screen manifest SHA `e2c09590483f5703c03b53128b86535b35e08ada5a2a039abfa83b74e8133816`, rejected checkpoint SHA `9d368986f49903171cb563c48c02371d620159f0fc4260c903dedb0b10eca7f2`.

**D183 — THE SIX-DAY VACATION RUN IS A CLOSED TWO-LINEAGE CONFIRMATION QUEUE, NOT AN AUTONOMOUS REWARD SEARCH (2026-07-14).** The unattended system may consume already-reviewed evidence but may not invent candidates, change thresholds, promote a reward, or mutate production. Before the queue can be frozen, the corrected main lineage must complete a `1B × 2-seed` paired confirmation plus exact scripted and learned-opponent transfer; the builder refuses to choose the candidate itself. The literal six-job order is: second-ancestry (`league9`, exact cap SHA `359d14caa08f12362f799c4cab4f33301fc9ce2ba3dec85922abe9622670d5f5`) `1B × 2` paired confirmation, its scripted transfer, its learned-anchor transfer, a two-lineage gate, then fixed `6B × 3-seed` paired-final screens for the main and second ancestries (`72B` requested learner steps total). The gate requires self-play non-inferiority (`mean Δscore ≥ -0.02`, every seed `≥ -0.05`, relative TD drop `≤20%`), the existing scripted-transfer recommendation, and learned-transfer eligibility across both ancestries. Learned transfer is exactly `4096` games per cell with candidate/reference, seeds 42/43, exactly four identical pinned anchors, and both native backend orientations; per-cell outputs are atomic and hash-bound. Its mean, per-training-seed, per-anchor, per-orientation, and worst-cell thresholds are a deterministic fixed-stratum routing rule—not a confidence interval over pseudoreplicated cells. The typed queue pins every executable, runner, config, checkpoint, manifest, evidence file, and directory tree; enforces disk/inodes, progress, maximum runtime, three-poll thermal, validator, and completed-evidence revalidation gates; and halts with later jobs pending on any failure. PPO screens are non-resume-safe; only atomic, restart-validating transfer/gate jobs may resume. Queue-owned screens set `ARM_DETACH=0`, keeping the screen, arm wrapper, trainer, and descendants inside the queue job's new-session process group so a guard cannot strand GPU work. BBTV remains observational only: it may stream each newest completed checkpoint, but its output is never scientific input. No unattended result changes a production default; post-vacation promotion still requires human review.

**D184 — AN ALL-CANDIDATES-REJECTED RESULT NOW HAS A CLOSED R0-ONLY VACATION FALLBACK (2026-07-14).** Reliability audit found that D183's candidate freezer rejected `candidate_arm=both` even though the operational guidance promised to retain R0 when every simplification failed; that mismatch could have left the reserved RTX 2070 idle for the vacation. The fallback is authorized only when the exact decomposition hash chain recommends `both`, its eligible-candidate list is empty, the transfer uses `both` as reference and exactly all three simplifications (`possession_only`, `gain_only`, `neither`), and the source screen records the complete current recursive config-tree, explicit default-config, compiled-module, exact nine-file runtime, patch, warm, and pool identities. Pinning the current checkout cannot retroactively complete a legacy screen, so the active v3 screen may route a candidate into a new fully closed paired confirmation but cannot directly authorize this fallback if every candidate is rejected; that outcome requires a provenance-complete decomposition rerun. The freeze spec requires `candidate_arm=both`, null anchor/learned-transfer inputs, and `final_steps=12B`. It emits exactly two non-resume-safe `control-final` jobs: R0 at `12B x seeds 42/43/44` from the main ancestry, then the identical schedule from `league9`. This preserves the predeclared `72B` total while making no reward-promotion claim. The queue remains fully pinned and guarded; any eligible simplification, partial candidate matrix, incomplete provenance, inconsistent evidence, or attempt to provide candidate/learned/gate inputs fails closed.

**D185 — `NEITHER` FAILED THE FROZEN PAIRED GATE; SIX-DAY COMPUTE MAY CHARACTERIZE R0 BUT MAY NOT TRY ANOTHER CANDIDATE (2026-07-14).** The corrected main-lineage paired confirmation completed all four arms at exact `999,948,288` steps with at least 10,000 final-policy games and zero integrity counters. `neither - both` mean performance was `-0.0252731442`, below the fixed `-0.02` floor; seed deltas `-0.0332499743` and `-0.0172963142` passed `-0.05`, and TD relative drop `-0.1182473773` passed the `0.20` ceiling. The failure is exactly `mean_perf_delta`, so the candidate route stops before scripted/learned transfer or second ancestry. This does not mean all simplifications failed and does not authorize switching candidates. DECISION: add an explicit `confirmation-rejected-baseline` queue route, distinct from D184. It independently regenerates the paired analysis under the unchanged gate, requires a literal failure, and requires the screen's embedded selection evidence to equal the validated decomposition transfer. It then writes a pinned `BASELINE_AUTHORIZATION.json` and may emit only two R0 `control-final` jobs at `12B x seeds 42/43/44`, main ancestry then exact `league9` ancestry (`72B` total). These runs characterize long-horizon seed/ancestry variation and preserve checkpoints for future matched work; they cannot pass a reward gate, promote R0, or mutate production. Every freezer spec now names one explicit route so evidence types cannot be confused by `candidate_arm` overloading.

**D186 — MEASURED RTX-2070 THROUGHPUT JUSTIFIES ONE FAIL-CLOSED THIRD-ANCESTRY R0 OVERFLOW, NOT A NEW REWARD SEARCH (2026-07-14).** The live D185 queue advanced its first 129,892,352 learner steps at approximately 187K steps/second with zero integrity counters, implying about 107 training hours for its declared `72B` and likely leaving roughly two days of the full departure/return horizon idle. DECISION: after—and only after—the exact primary plan SHA `4ee72e3c58f09786cdd3bbf78a772e8de2d9a93e21a8b065cf0c5976ecced270` reaches terminal `complete` with both original success validators and recorded artifact hashes still passing, a separately frozen overflow may run one unchanged R0 `control-final` screen (`12B x seeds 42/43/44`) from the static pool's exact `netblock` ancestry SHA `9964cf4d4c9c2654157e898ff17327732e73c4c85a5883e7d311d8d3baade05e`.
